Chapter 9

AN: Thank you so much for the support. I hope you like this chapter.

About a week has passed since Rio ad Nicky got to Westview, and while neither of them have approached Agatha again, they are moving into a house down the road from her so that they can start to figure out how they are going to handle their next approach.

“It’s good that we were able to get a house so close,” Rio says as she and Nicky carry some stuff they have just brought into the house they are moving into, Rio knowing that the reason they were able to is because as soon as Wanda’s spell broke a lot of people decided to flee town, meaning it was easy to make this house theirs, and part of making the house feel like theirs involved Rio putting in place protections including, after a brilliant suggestion from Nicky, using the ‘left over interference’ as he calls it, from Wanda’s spell to add to the protection she put in place to help hide them. “I know it’s not ideal, but we’ll be close,” Rio says, trying to get Nicky to focus on the good as she knows that over the last week, as they research exactly what happened, Nicky has been unsurprisingly struggling. While she has also been struggling, she is trying to stay strong for her son.

“None of this is ideal,” Nicky admits. “I thought that when we found Mama everything would be okay, that we’d start to catch up on all the time we missed but now…” Nicky starts to say, before trailing off.

“It just feels like we are missing out on more time,” Rio finishes, and Nicky nods. “I know,” Rio says sadly. “Nicky, I don’t know how we’re going to fix this, I don’t know how we’re going to get Mama back, but I know that somewhere deep inside Mama is still there, and I’m not going to give up until we bring her to the surface,” Rio assures Nicky.

“I just hope we can,” Nicky admits, and before Rio can say anything to there is a knock on the door. “I’ll get it,” Nicky says, putting down what he is holding and heading to the door.

As soon as he opens the door Nicky feels shocked as he finds his mama standing on the other side, holding a gift basket, and he has no idea what to do.

“Um, hi,” Nicky greats, feeling awkward even though he knows it’s his mama standing before him and he shouldn’t be because right now, because of the spell, she isn’t his mama even though he desperately wishes it was.

“Hi there, aren’t you as cute as a button,” Agnes greats. “My name is Agnes, I wanted to welcome you to the block, I live just down the street if you ever need anything,” Agnes says to Nicky.

“Thanks…. Agnes…” Nicky says, it feeling extremely awkward for him to say that. “Would you like to come in?” Nicky asks.

“Oh, I would love to, you’re so polite,” Agnes says to Nicky as she walks into the house, rustling his hair as he goes.

“MOM!” Nicky yells, as he really needs Rio right now, and a few seconds later Rio hurries into the room, clearly expecting something to be wrong, but she relaxes when she sees Agatha.

“Well, hello there,” Agnes says, looking Rio up and down, clearly checking her out. “I’m Agnes, you must be this charming boy’s mom,” Agnes greats, and at those words Rio feels like she is being stabbed in the chest.

“I am,” Rio says, fighting to keep her voice even. “I’m Rio,” Rio says, searching Agnes for a sign of recognition whether because there’s some of Agatha coming through or because of their meeting a weak ago, but neither happens and it is clear that from Agnes’s point of view she has never met Rio before.

“Well, it’s nice to meet you, Rio. Is it just the two of you in this big house?” Agnes asks, clearly fishing for information.

“It is,”

“Well, if you ever get lonely, I am just down the road, my door is always open,” Agnes says as she hands Rio the basket.

“I’ll remember that,” Rio responds, being sure she will never forget. “Thank you… Agnes,”

“My pleasure, Rio,” Agatha responds, as Nicky looks between his mothers wondering what the looks they are exchanging means, as Agatha looks at Rio just a little too long.

“Agnes?” Nicky asks, resisting the urge to say Mama, as he can’t help but wonder if it means his mama is remembering.

“Sorry, don’t know where my mind went,” Agnes admits.

“It’s okay,” Rio assures her. “We haven’t really unpacked much, but would you like to stay for lunch?” Rio asks, knowing that while it might be difficult for her and Nicky it could be a way to figure out just how hard they can push against the spell.

“I’d lov…. I can’t,” Agnes says, both Nicky and Rio realise that she was going to join them but then something stopped them. “I should go,” Agnes says. “It was nice to meet you two, I’m sure we’ll see each other around.

“We will,” Rio assures. “Te Veo,” Rio says, as Agatha leaves trying to use a little hint of what they once were to put a crack in the spell that has enveloped Agatha, and Agatha doesn’t respond she just leaves, closing the door behind her. “Are you okay?” Rio asks Nicky, as soon as Agatha is gone.

“I don’t know,” Nicky admits. “I know she doesn’t remember us, but it was like she didn’t even remember meeting us a week ago,” Nicky comments.

“That’s because I don’t think she does Nicky,” Rio admits. “I’ve been watching, I think the spell resets every few days, makes her think she is a different version of reality every few days, and she doesn’t remember anything that happened in her last version of reality, ” Rio explains.

“If Mama’s reality keeps resetting, how are we going to break her out of it?” Nicky asks, as it seems to him like the spell is constantly adapting to make sure that cracks in it can’t form.

“I don’t know,” Rio admits. “But we’re going to figure it out, we’ll figure this all out,” Rio tells her son, who nods even though he doesn’t have quiet as much faith. “Looks like we’ve got some great ingredients in here, how about we get started on lunch,” Rio suggests as she knows what cooking means to Nicky.

“Sure,” Nicky responds, and the two of them head to the kitchen.

Once in the kitchen Nicky and Rio start to cook together it being clear to Rio that Nicky is still struggling with being around Agatha when she doesn’t know who he is.

December 2023

A few weeks have passed since Rio and Nicky moved into Westview and ever since it has become clear that Rio’s suspicion about the spell Agatha re-setting every few days is right, as is Nicky’s theory that the spell is trying to adapt to prevent it from being broken, and because of that neither of them have figured out how they can break Agatha out of the spell without causing more harm.

While his mother is off doing her job Nicky is in the living area of the house they are living in reading while sitting on the window seat, as he reads Nicky looks out of the window and notices Agatha, across the street, trying to carry too many shopping bags at once.

Not even thinking about what it will mean Nicky quickly gets up, puts his book down, and goes running as fast as he can outside, across the street, and to where Agatha has just dropped her grocery bags.

“Hi, let me help,” Nicky says to Agatha, getting to her and starting to help her pick up the groceries.

“Oh, that’s sweet of you,” Agnes says to Nicky. “I’ve been so busy at school that I didn’t realise I hadn’t done shopping in a while until I had nothing left,” Agnes explains.

“You’re a teacher?” Nicky asks amazed. “That’s amazing,” Nicky says, smiling slightly, as he knows that what he wants most is to get lessons from his mother.

“I think so,” Agnes says, as Nicky continues to pack up her groceries. “Sorry, what did you say your name is?” Agnes asks.

“Nicky, Nicky Vidal-Harkness,” Nicky responds, without even thinking about it, but the second he says it he regrets it, as Agatha gets a look that he can only describe as pure devastation on her face.

“No…. no…. I don’t know who you are… what game you’re playing… but you’re not him,” Agatha says, looking both furious and devastated, which for Nicky is everything, but after a few second it disappears, as Nicky ‘feel’s’ the spell once again tighten it’s hold on his mama. “I’m sorry, did you say something?” Agnes asks.

“No,” Nicky says, fighting back tears. “I’m going to help you,” Nicky says to his Mama.

“You already have,” Agnes tells Nicky. “You saved my groceries,” Agnes tells Nicky, before standing up.

“I’m going to save you,” Nicky mutters, and he watches Agatha walk away, feeling his heart break as she goes, as once again, just for a split second, he felt like he was getting through to his Mama.

Having no idea what Nicky has gotten up to while she has been gone Rio is returning home a little while after Nicky talked to Agatha, not that she knows that. Just like she always done the first thing Rio does is go in search of her son.

Not finding him downstairs Rio heads upstairs and the second she gets to the upstairs landing Rio hears a sound, but she knows, but hates, the sound of Nicky crying. Hurrying into Nicky’s room Rio finds him lying on his side, his chests against his chest as he cries.

“Nicky?” Rio asks concerned. “What happened, Mi Conejito?” Rio asks her son as she sits down on the edge of his bed. “Whatever happened, it will be okay,” Rio assures her son, even though she knows that is not necessarily the case.

“No, it won’t,” Nicky says as he rolls over and faces his mom, who sees a look of complete devastation on Nicky’s face.

“What happened?” Rio asks, feeling confused about what could have caused such a reaction in Nicky, but suspecting it might have something to do with Agatha.

“I saw Mama outside, struggling with groceries, so I went to help her,” Nicky explains, and Rio can’t imagine Agatha struggling with something so mundane as groceries. “She thinks she’s a teacher at the moment,” Nicky explains, saying so with a fond smile. “She asked me what my name was,” Nicky says, and as he does Rio tenses, as she realises what must have happened.

“What happened?” Rio asks concerned.

“At first she got really upset, and angry, said no, that she didn’t know who I was, but I couldn’t be him, that she didn’t know what game I was playing,” Nicky says, it feels painful for him to explain that. “But it only lasted a second and it was gone, and she had no idea what just happened… I don’t know what was worse,” Nicky admis.

“I’m really sorry, Nicky,” Rio says to her son. “But you need to know the reason Mama reacted like that is because deep down inside of Mama, in a place the witches spell can never destroy or truly hide, she knows how much she loves you, how much she misses you, and that’s what came out today,” Rio says. “You are Mama’s everything, nothing, not even someone as powerful as the Scalet Witch, can take that away,” Rio assures Nicky, hoping he believes her.

“It feels like she already has,” Nicky admits.

“She hasn’t, she would never,” Rio assures Nicky. “We’ll figure this out, we’ll get her back,” Rio promises Nicky.

“We have to,” Nicky says, and Rio agrees with that, so in response, she pulls her son up into her arms and holds him close, both of them desperately hoping they can get through to Agatha soon.

A few weeks have passed since Agatha freaked out when she heard Nicky’s name and ever since both he and Rio have made an effort not to use Nicky’s name around Agatha, something which is seemingly working well.

It’s Christmas Eve and both Nicky and Rio are in their kitchen putting some of the incredible amount of food into different containers.

“Do you think she will even accept it?” Nicky asks Rio, sounding worried.

“I have seen other people in the neighbourhood give her food and she’s accepted it, I think we’ll be okay,” Rio says, as she finishes putting the last of the food into containers, feeling glad that there are other people looking out for Agatha when it gets too much for her and Nicky.

“Good,” Nicky says, relieved. “Um, so there is the carols thing in the square tonight, do you think we could get Mama to come with us?” Nicky asks curious, as he knows he would love that, as since being in Westview he has realised that they take holidays very seriously, something which he has never experienced before, but very much enjoys.

“We can ask,” Rio says. “But Nicky…” Rio starts to say.

“Don’t be disappointed if she says no, I know,” Nicky confirms, knowing she was going to say that because she knows his mom is trying to help him with what he is feeling about everything that has been going on.

“Good, go get your coat,” Rio tells her son.

“Aren’t you forgetting something?” Nicky asks.

“Not I know of,” Rio responds, looking around, wondering what Nicky could be talking about.

“Your Christmas sweater!” Nicky says to his mother, like it should be obvious.

“Not happening,” Rio tells her son as while she appreciates that he brought her a novelty Christmas sweater that doesn’t mean she is actually going to wear it.

“But mom…” Nicky starts to object.

“But nothing, I’m not wearing it,” Rio tells her son. “Coat, gloves,” Rio tells her son, wanting to make sure he is warm enough as she never wants to go through Nicky having pneumonia again.

“Fine,” Nicky says, and he goes to collect what he needs.

A few minutes later Nicky is bundled up in a coat, gloves, beanie and scarf as he and Rio walk towards Agatha’s house, both of them carrying bags of food.

“Do we know what her current reality is?” Nicky asks, as he knows that will tell them a lot about what it’s going to be like to interact with Agatha.

“No, I haven’t seen her for a few days,” Rio admits, and Nicky nods in understanding. “We’ll find out as soon as we knock, I’d imagine,” Rio admits, as it tends to become clear pretty quickly what Agatha is seeing.

“Sounds about right,” Nicky says, as they get to the door which he reaches out and knock on.

Seconds after Nicky nod the door opens to reveal Agatha and as soon as she sees her Rio has to bite her tongue as Agatha is dressed head to toe in Christmas attire, something which is so far from Agatha, and isn’t always how the spell works as sometimes her clothes seem regular to everyone else, but Agatha sees them as something different.

“Merry Christmas!” Agnes greats with an over the top grin.

“Merry Christmas, Agnes,” Nicky says, smiling at her, as while he knows that she isn’t completely his mama at the moment he is glad to see her so happy as that’s often not a guarantee when it comes to what she is preserving as reality. “We made so much food that we thought we would bring you some,” Nicky says, as he hands Agatha the food.

“Oh, that is incredible of you! I have been so focused on decorations that I completely forget about food!” Agnes reveals. “And then guess what happened, I ruined my wreath! and I have no time to go get a new one!” Agnes explains, and it is clear to both Rio and Nicky that in this version of reality that is something that really bothers her.

“Well talk about serendipity,” Rio says, moving one of her hands behind her and using her green witch magic to conjure a perfect, lush, wreath, covered in purple flowers. “We just happen to have an extra wreath,” Rio says, as she presents the wreath to Agatha, who looks amazed, while it’s Nicky’s turn to attempt not to laugh at his mothers blatant magic use, and his how oblivious his Mama was to that use.

“It’s beautiful, thank you,” Agnes says to Rio, taking it form her, with an amazed look on her face.

“My pleasure,” Rio responds, and after a few seconds she has to look away from Agatha because it hurts to see her looking an her with affection but no recognition.

“So, um, we were going to head to the town square for the carols and we were wondering if you’d like to join us,” Nicky says to Agnes, being able to tell that his mother is struggling a little.

“Oh, I would love to!” Agnes exclaims. “Just let me take this food and beautiful wreath inside,” Agnes says.

“Of course, we’ll be right here,” Rio responds, and Agatha takes the food and wreath and heads inside.

“Are you okay?” Nicky asks his mother curious, as he can tell that she is struggling. While Nicky is also struggling his mama was always kind and joyful to him, so he isn’t as uncomfortable with the current persona Agatha is under as his mom is.

“Yeah, I’m okay,” Rio says, honestly not sure if she is, but before she can explain more Agatha, dressed in a Christmas coat, appears back in the doorway.

“Let’s get this show on the road!” Agnes says joyfully, and the three of them walk together towards the town square.

As they walk together, listening to Agnes happily talk about Christmas, both Rio and Nicky have complicated feeling as while they are both beyond happily that they are getting to spend time with Agatha there is a level of sadness because it’s not really her, and Rio can’t help but think about how this is everything she has wanted for the past five years and yet it is still wrong,

“Mom, there’s carnival food! Can I go see what they have?” Nicky asks excitedly, when they finally get to the square.

“Sure, just don’t leave the square,” Rio tells her son, as while there hasn’t been anything to indicate there is still danger in Westview, she can’t be too careful.

“Sure,” Nicky responds, and he hurries away from his moms.

“He seems like a great kid,” Agnes says to Rio.

“He’s the best,” Rio says, knowing that without the doubt.

“And it’s just the two of you?” Agnes asks, clearly trying to dig for information and Rio knows she has to play this delicately otherwise she risks the spell once again tightening it’s hold on Agatha.

“For now,” Rio says, choosing her words carefully. “But we’re going to get his other mother back,” Rio says, watching Agatha carefully to see if her words have any effect.

“I hope you do,” Agnes says, her words being innocent, but they severely hurt Rio. “And incredible boy like that deserves to have his mom and mama,” Agatha says in a quiet voice, and just for a second Rio sees a flicker of Agatha, but just like every time Rio has seen a flicker of the real Agatha it’s gone just a quickly. “Sorry, was I saying something?” Agnes asks curious.

“Just that you were going to get a table while I got the three of us some hot chocolate,” Rio says, needing some space for a minute.

“Seems like a plan Doll,” Agnes responds, and the two of them go in their different directions.

A few minutes later Rio, who has gotten hot chocolate and also may have punched a tree, Nicky who has gotten food, and Agatha who has gotten a lyric books and other souvenirs, all get to the same table where they sit down together, and start to share what they have all brought.

Even though it’s not perfect, and both Rio and Nicky would prefer that Agatha knew who they are, they both find themselves enjoying every second that the three of them spend single carols and celebrating Christmas, as for the first time in over a hundred years it’s almost like they are a family again.

Chapter 10

Chapter 10

AN: Thank you so much. You are constantly surprising me with how you respond to chapters. It means everything to me. So, I will be updating another chapter later tonight my time, but then the next chapter won’t be until after 1x07 is out. Hope you enjoy. Let me know what you think.

February 2024

Two months have passed since Christmas and in that time both Nicky and Rio have been spending time with Agatha and have started to realise how much they can get away with without causing the spell to tighten its strangled hold on her, but despite understanding the spell a little better they are no closure to figuring out a way to break it.

Standing in their living room hand and hand Nicky and Rio are both speaking in the language that only the two of them speak as they perform a spell, Rio’s green magic and Nicky’s blue with purple and green hue, magic dancing around them, combining, expanding, working in harmony with each other to create their goal.

“That’s done,” Rio says as the magic fades away, but both Nicky and Rio know that it is still unseen all around them.

“I can feel it,” Nicky says. “We’ve used the magic interference in this town to create a pulse within this house to try to interfere with all other magic,” Nicky says, knowing that it feels like a subtle pounding, like a pulse to him.  “It’s not going to last long,” Nicky says.

“I know, and with the fact that the spell Agatha is under is created from the same magic there is no guarantee it will work, but we need to try,” Rio says, knowing that they are both willing to do whatever it takes.

“I’ll go get Mama,” Nicky says, knowing that time is not on their hand.

“How are you going to get her here?” Rio asks, as she realises, they haven’t talked about that.

“This version of her thinks she is a plumber, I’ll say you need help,” Nicky says before hurrying out of the house.

“That’ll work,” Rio responds, as she watches Nicky go.

As he knows that every second counts Nicky runs, as fast as he can, across, and then down the street. Getting to Agatha’s door, a place he has become quite familiar with, Nicky quicky knocks, and after a few seconds the door opens to reveal Agatha.

“Agnes, good you’re here. We need your help we’re having a plumbing emergency,” Nicky says to Agatha.

“Let me get my tools,” Agnes says, and she picks up an empty shoebox which Nicky realises must be what she considers to be a toolbox. “Let’s go,” Agnes says to Nicky and the two of them hurry back towards Nicky and Rio’s house.

“The problem is through here,” Nicky says, leading Agatha into the living room and as soon as they walk into the house Nicky can feel the spell, he and Rio cast ‘fight’ with the spell Agatha is under for lack of a better word. “Something’s happening,” Nicky says, as Agatha freezes

“Agatha,” Rio says, taking a step forward, doing so hesitantly as she doesn’t know what expect, she doesn’t know if they are going to succeed at what they have tried to do.

“YOU!” Agatha says, looking furious, as she drops the shoebox she is holding.

“Do you know who I am?” Rio asks, feeling hope for the first time in months.

“Of course, I know who you are,” Agnes says angrily. “You’re my bitch of an ex-wife who left a trail of destruction and death in her wake!” Agnes exclaims.

“Not technically wrong,” Rio says, having a feeling that she is not completely ‘Agatha’ but that the fact that she is feeling so much anger for her gives Rio hope that they have an opening. “Agatha, look at me, see me, really see me,” Rio pleads.

“Agatha? Who’s Agatha? Is that your side piece?” Agnes asks, the words hurting Rio more than she wants to admit, but as Nicky knows his mom so well, he can tell that. “I’m out of here,” Agatha heads towards the door, Nicky feeling the spell Agatha is under drawing more power, more strength, from the caster, burying the real Agatha deep below the spider web of the magic.

“Mama!” Nicky yells but considering the magic he is feeling he isn’t surprised when Agatha doesn’t turn around, doesn’t look at him, and instead leaves. “Damn it!” Nicky says annoyed as the door slams.

“I’m sorry, I thought that might have worked,” Rio admits, feeling worse for her son than for herself.

“It started to, but the spell just drew more strength from Wanda,” Nicky says, knowing that is going to keep drawing strength from her while Wanda is alive, but she likely hasn’t even realised that. “Maybe Magic is the key, what if I just used magic in front of mom, or sent a blast at Mama so she could feel my magic, that would break through,” Nicky suggests, thinking that the connection his and his mama’s magic share could be key, and as she hears Nicky’s words Rio’s face loses all colour, clearly horrified at the suggestion.

“Nicky, no,” Rio tells her son, her voice stern.

“It wouldn’t be a strong blast, I wouldn’t hurt Mama,” Nicky says in his defence, feeling that that should be obvious, and his mother shouldn’t be looking as horrified as she does.

“Nicky, listen to me, you cannot blast your mom, you can never do that, no matter what,” Rio tells her son. “Even if it meant protecting yourself you need to find another way,” Rio tells her son.

“That’s the completely opposite to everything you’ve always told me,” Nicky says confused, as his mom has always made it clear that he is always to use magic to protect himself if needed.

“Sit down,” Rio says to her son, realising that they have to have a conversation that they should have had long before now.

“What am I missing?” Nicky asks curious, as he sits down, and Rio sits down next to him.

“Nicky, I know we’ve talked a lot about Mama’s magic, and how she is powerful,” Rio says.

“Yeah,”

“Well, one of her abilities is that if she is blasted with magic, she will start to siphon that magic from the person,” Rio explains. “She can’t control it, not really,” Rio says, knowing that because she has seen it, because she has seen what it does to Agatha when it happens. “So, whenever Mama is blasted with magic, she will keep siphoning the magic until there is nothing left,” Rio tells her son, who realises what her mother isn’t saying.

“And the person who she is siphoning from dies,” Nicky realises, not even being able to imagine what that would feel like for Agatha.

“Yes,” Rio confirms. “Which is why, no matter what, you can never blast Mama with your magic,” Rio tells her son, her voice stern, as she knows what would happen to Nicky, and what that would do to Agatha. “Promise me, Nicky, promise me, that you will never blast your Mama,” Rio says to Nicky, needing him to understand how serious it is.

“I promise,” Nicky says, and Rio looks relieved at that. “Are you okay? Mama words were kind of cruel,” Nicky says to his mother, having no idea how she seems to be okay considering what Agatha said.

“I’ve heard worse,” Rio respond, knowing that after Nicky died Agatha says things a lot worse to her.  “I’m okay, Nicky,” Rio assures her son.

“You don’t have to be,” Nicky responds, moving closer to his mother and hugging her, being able to tell that she is hurt, even though she is trying to hide it.

May 2024

Three months have passed since Nicky and Rio once again tried to break the spell Agatha was after and while it is clear that they weren’t successful it is also clear that they changed something as in almost every reality Agatha ‘knows’ Rio as someone from her past who she hates and has some kind of romantic history with, but she never knows more than that.

While his mom is trying to hide how Agatha hating her is affecting her Nicky can tell that it is starting to take its toll, and he hates that there is nothing he can do to help her. While Rio is off doing her job Nicky is walking around the neighbourhood as he was feeling a little cooped up inside. As he makes his way down the street Nicky sees his mama leave her house and as he does, he gets an idea.

“I’ve had worse ideas,” Nicky mutters, and before he can overthink what he is going to do too much Nicky hurries towards Agatha’s house, considering everything Nicky isn’t surprised that the door is unlocked, not that a look door would stop him.

Once in the house Nicky starts to look around the house, wanting to see if there is an consistency with his mama’s reality when it constantly changes. For a while Nicky looks around, not seeing anything that indicates his mama is experiencing any sense of constancy, but then he notices something on the bench.

Walking over to the bench Nicky sees that there is a piece of paper feeling curious he picks it up and to his surprise he finds that it is a drawing, a drawing of what is clearly him, before he died, with both his mothers.

“You really are still in there,” Nicky realises, picking up the picture and looking at it in amazement, not sure exactly how to feel about that because he has no idea how to help as he can feel how the spell strangles his mama every time he tries.

As he stares at the picture his mama drew, knowing how much he wants all three of them to be together all knowing the truth, Nicky hears the front door open and so to avoid awkward questions he quickly leaves through the backdoor, leaving the picture behind even though he would like to take it with him.

After leaving Agatha’s house Nicky continues his walk around the neighbourhood, not feeling completely ready to go ‘home’ yet as he doesn’t want his mom to realise how much it hurts him being so close to his mama when she doesn’t know who he is because he is pretty sure that the hate Rio is getting is worse.

So, instead of heading home Nicky just keeps walking, fighting back tears as he thinks about how much he wants his mama to remember who she is, who he is, so that they can be a family again.

August 2024

Three months have passed since Nicky saw tangible proof that somewhere deep down inside his Mama remembers who she is, but to his disappointment neither he nor his mom have been able to figure out a way to bring that part of her to the surface.

It is the day of Nicky’s fourteenth birthday and just like she has for the past six years Rio is walking into his bedroom first thing in the morning carrying a birthday cake she made.

“Happy Birthday, Nicky,” Rio says, as she walks towards her son, who smiles and moves up in his bed so that he is properly sitting up.

“Thanks Mom,” Nicky says, and once Rio, and therefore the cake, are close enough Nicky blows out the candles, making the same wish he has made for the past six years, for him to be truly reunited with his mama. “The record holds,” Nicky says with a proud look on his face, as every year he has managed to blow out the candles in one go.

“It does,” Rio confirms, and over the next few minutes she cuts a couple of pieces of cake, one of which she gives to Nicky while she keeps the other to herself as she sits down next to him. “So, you haven’t given me a straight answer about what you want to do today,” Rio tells her son.

“Come on, Mom, I don’t think either of us can do anything straight,” Nicky jokes, not being able to resist the opening he has been waiting for, and Rio has to chuckle at the joke.

“You might have a point there,” Rio says, knowing that is the first time Nicky has confirmed what she’s suspected for a while, and it makes her so happy to know that he felt comfortable enough to just casually say it. “But you’re also avoiding the question,” Rio tells her son. “Talk,” Rio tells him.

“I don’t want to do anything,” Nicky admits.

“Nicky,” Rio says, drawing out her son’s name because she knows there is something he isn’t saying.

“The only thing I want to do is break the spell on Mama and we proven that right now we can’t do that,” Nicky says annoyed. “There’s nothing else I want,” Nicky admits.

“I know, that’s what I want too,” Rio tells her son. “But we’re not doing nothing for your birthday,” Rio tells her son. “So, we’re going to finish the cake, and then you’re going to get ready and by the time you’re in the kitchen you’re going to have some ideas of what we’re going to do,” Rio tells her son, knowing she has her own idea, but she isn’t going to share that with Nicky as she isn’t sure she is going to be able to pull it off.

“Okay Mom,” Nicky responds, and the two of them continue to eat their cake together, as they do Rio puts her arm around her son and kisses his head, as Nicky snuggles into his mother’s side, feeling how much love and support his mother gives him.

A little while after she brought the cake into Nicky’s bedroom Rio is walking downstairs but rather than heading to the kitchen where she will be meeting her soon when he is ready Rio heads out of the front door and makes the familiar root to Agatha’s house.

Getting to the door Rio pauses for a second, knowing to expect anger as in the reality that started the day before Anges, the nurse, sees Rio as the doctor who broke her heart because Rio thought their relationship was a threat to their carer.

“For Nicky,” Rio reminds herself as while it is getting harder to be around Agatha’s hate she knows she will deal with it for her son, and so she reaches out and knocks.

“What the hell are you doing here?” Agnes asks angrily, as soon as she sees Rio standing on her doorstep.

“I’m not here for me,” Rio explains. “Today is my son’s fourteenth birthday,” Rio says, it taking everything in her not to say ‘our’ son, but she knows that won’t get her anywhere if she tries. “And he’d really like to spend time with you,” Rio says, not needing Nicky to say that to know it. “Will you come over?” Rio asks, desperately hoping that Agatha says yes.

“I can do that…. for him,” Agnes says, and Rio can’t help but wonder what Agatha considers her relationship with Nicky to be in this version of her reality, but whatever Agatha is experiencing Rio knows that Agatha wouldn’t be seeing him as a son as Wanda’s spell is designed to punish Agatha and allowing her to have maternal feelings towards anyone when she blames Agatha for losing her own children isn’t something she would allow.

“Thank you,” Rio says sincerely.

“I need to clean up, but I can be over in about ten minutes,” Agnes tells Rio.

“I’d say you look perfect to me, but okay,” Rio says, and Agatha smiles at that. “Te Veo,” Rio says before walking away, feeling relieved that that worked, as she isn’t entirely sure what she would have done if it hadn’t.

Not quite ten minutes later Rio is in the kitchen of her house trying to get breakfast ready, when Nicky walks into the kitchen.

“Mom,” Nicky says, and Rio looks up on him. “I know she’s not really Mama right now, and if it will just hurt you I understand and we don’t have to, but I would really like it if we could spend some time with Agnes today,” Nicky explains, needing to separate Agnes and his Mama in his mind as it’s the only way he can handle his reality, and before Rio can answer there is a knock on the door.

“You should get that,” Rio tells her son.

Feeling confused Nicky heads to the door and when he opens it, he is surprised, but absolutely thrilled, to find Agatha standing on the other side.

“M…Agnes?” Nicky asks amazed.

“I heard it was your birthday,” Agnes says with a grin, as she hands Nicky a phonebook which Nicky assumes she is seeing as some kind of present. “Happy Birthday, Kiddo,” Agnes says.

“Thank you,” Nicky says, fighting back emotions at that, as even if she isn’t really his mama at the moment it means everything to him to finally hear her wish him happy birthday and it takes all his strength not to throw himself into his Mama’s arms and hug her like he desperately wants to. “Thank you,” Nicky tells her.

“You’re welcome, but it’s your birthday, you get presents,” Agnes tells Nicky.

“And I think I just got an incredible one,” Nicky admits. “Mom’s in the kitchen, we’ve already had cake but we’re about to have breakfast,” Nicky tells Agnes.

“You’ve had cake before breakfast?” Agnes asks as they wake their way to the kitchen.

“It’s tradition,” Nicky says with a shrug.

“Not the most healthy one,” Agnes comments as they walk into the kitchen, a level of disapproval in her voice.

“If you don’t think eating cake for breakfast is healthy, you’re really not going to like what else we’re having,” Rio comments, trying to hide her amusement.

“Guess we’ll have to see,” Anges comments. “Are you cooking?” Agatha asks and the surprise in her voice makes Rio feel amazed, just for a second, as she knows that that is a hint of Agatha remembering something on a subconscious level, but because the day is about Nicky and not her, she doesn’t dwell on it. “We all are,” Rio says.

“It’s gonna be great,” Nicky comments, and to his absolute joy he and both his moms make breakfast together. For Nicky it is almost perfect as he knows the only thing that would make it better is if Agatha remembered everything, and when neither Agatha nor Nicky are looking, Rio manages to take a picture of the two of them cooking together using the cell phone she recently got.

September 2024

Not even a month has passed since Nicky’s fourteenth birthday and while Nicky, Rio and Agatha managed to have an incredible day together, and both Rio and Nicky have a copy of the photo Rio took, it has become clear that they would both give anything if it meant Agatha truly remembered who they were.

It’s a pretty average summers day and Rio is walking into the living room where Nicky is surrounded by books as there is something she needs to talk to him about.

“Nicky,” Rio says, as she walks over to him, being careful not to step on any of his books. “There’s something I want to talk to you about,” Rio says, as she sits down next to her son.

“You’re not giving up on Mama, are you?” Nicky asks terrified, as he can tell that his mother is using the serious tone, the very tone she doesn’t use often.

“Never,” Rio assures her son. “That’s never going to be something I’m ever going to even consider doing,” Rio promises he son.

“Good,” Nicky says, relieved about that. “So, what’s with the serious tone?” Nicky asks curious.

“You’re stating high school next week,” Rio tells her son, feeling that it would be best to just say it, rather than beating around the bush.

“What!” Nicky exclaims shocked. “I’ve never had to go to school before,” Nicky says to his mother.

“Because until Westview we’ve never stayed at a place too long,” Rio reminds her son. “But the truth is we are creating a life here, and we’re going to be here until we break the spell on Mama, which means you should go to school,” Rio tells her son. “Be around other kids,”

“What if I don’t want to be around other kids?” Nicky asks.

“Nicky…” Rio starts to say.

“NO!” Nicky says frustrated as he stands up. “Since when do you just unilaterally decide things without us talking about it?” Nicky asks annoyed. “I have nothing in common with other kids! I’m literally over a hundred years older than them,” Nicky reminds his mother.

“That’s exactly why you should go to school,” Rio tells him. “You’ve never had anything normal; this could be that normalcy you’ve missed out on,” Rio tells her son.

“Are you the one who says normalcy is overrated?” Nicky asks.

“I do,” Rio confirms. “But I want you to be able to make friends, to not be so alone,” Rio tells her son.

“I have you,” Nicky reminds him mom.

“And you need more than me,” Rio tells her son, knowing that he needs Agatha, and also feeling that he deserves to have friend around his age, at least his physical age.

“I never have before,” Nicky tells his mom, not understanding what changed. “You, mama, you’re all I need,” Nicky tells his mother.

“Nicky…” Rio stats to say.

“No! I’m not going! I need to spend my time helping Mama not stuck in a classroom,” Nicky says, and he runs out of the room, as Rio hurries to her feet to follow she is thrown backwards by a blast of magic as Nicky runs out of the house.

“NICKY!” Rio yells in terror as she tries, and fails, to get to her feet.

Chapter 11

Chapter 11

AN: Thank you so much for the support. Hope you like this chapter. I am extremely nervous for 1x07, so the next chapter will be out after that, partly because I am not doing night shift tonight. Please let me know what you think.

For about five minutes Rio has to fight against her son’s magic before being able to get up, and honestly if she wasn’t so worried about him, she would be impressed. Once on her feet Rio doesn’t even worry about shoes before she goes running out of the house.

Focusing only on her son and nothing else Rio looks around the street as she runs, looking for signs of him, and as she is so distracted she doesn’t even notice Agatha walking down the street until she barrels into her.

“I’m sorry,” Rio says, completely distracted.

“You should…. What’s wrong?” Agnes asks, there being something about the look on Rio’s face that makes all the anger she is feeling disappears.

“Nic… my son and I got in a fight, and he ran,” Rio explains, as she gets to his feet, correcting herself before she say Nicky’s name because she doesn’t want to to cause the reaction Agatha has whenever she hears Nicky’s name. “I don’t know where he’s gone,” Rio says, her voice breaking, feeling terrified as not only have she and Nicky never had a fight like the one they just had he has also never run away like he just did.

“It will be okay,” Agatha says, getting a feeling deep inside which tells her she has to do whatever she can to help Rio. “We’ll find him,” Agatha tells Rio, using a gentle voice Rio hasn’t heard form Agatha in the entire time they have been in Westview.

“We have to,” Rio says, tears coming to her eyes. “I can’t lose him too, not again,” Rio admits, feeling terrified of what one of their many enemies would do if they were to find Nicky alone, away from her protection.

“You won’t,” Agatha says as she reaches out and wipes Rio’s tears, and as she does Rio allows herself a few moments to lean into the touch. “Where do you think he would have gone?” Agatha asks, and for Rio she seems so much closer to being the Agatha Rio’s known for centuries again.

‘Um, maybe the library,” Rio suggests, purposely moving away from Agatha’s hand so she doesn’t lose focus. “He loves it there,” Rio admits, though she knows that that isn’t saying much as there aren’t a whole lot of places in Westview Nicky has spent time in.

“Then let’s start there,” Agatha says, taking Rio’s hand. “Come on,” Agatha says, and the two of them go running towards the library.

For the next few minutes Rio and Agatha run, still holding each other’s hands, towards the town centre where the library is.

“There,” Agatha says, pointing to the gazebo where she sees Nicky sitting.

“He’s okay,” Rio says amazed, feeling unbelievably relieved.

“Yeah, he is,” Agatha assures her, as she gently squeezes Rio’s hand, offering her silent support.

“He’s not going to want to talk to me,” Rio realises, knowing that, having no idea how she is going to handle this.

“All you can do is try,” Agatha tells Rio, and for the first time since Nicky died it feels like they are a team. “I can stay close, just in case you need backup,” Agatha offers.

“Thanks,” Rio says, and she reluctantly let’s go of Agatha’s hand and walks over to where Nicky is sitting, while Agatha stays nearby to watch them, or at least she does until the spell causes her to forget why she is there.

“Did I hurt you?” Nicky asks concerned as Rio sits down next to him.

“You can’t hurt me, Nicky, we’ve been over this,” Rio tells Nicky.

“I know... I’m still sorry that I used my magic against you,” Nicky admits, as once he calmed down, he realised that wasn’t okay.

“It’s okay, you were upset, you lashed out, that’s okay,” Rio tells her son. “But now that you’ve lashed out, we need to talk about it,” Rio tells him, knowing that both she and Agatha find the lashing out easier than the talking about it, so now she is worried that for Nicky it will be the same. “Why are you so against going to school?” Rio ask her son.

“I love learning, you know that, when you quoted Mama saying knowledge is power you were both right,” Nicky assures his mother.

“But?” Rio asks concerned.

“But what do I need to know that school can teach me?” Nicky asks, as he is pretty sure he already knows everything that school could teach him.

“A lot of different stuff,” Rio says, knowing it’s a weak answer. “But the education I want you to get isn’t just what you’ll learn in the classroom,” Rio says to her son. “I want you to learn how to socialize with people, to be apart of something, to spend time places other than our house, mama’s house, and the library,” Rio tells her son. “I don’t need to be around people or be truly apart of the world, but you do, and I want you to be,” Rio tells her son, as she doesn’t want him to be lonely, she doesn’t want him to be shut off from everything.

“I get that, Mom, I do,” Nicky admits. “But I just can’t help but think that every moment I spent at school will be time I’m not spending trying to help Mama,” Nicky tells his mother.

“I know you want to help Mama, I want to too, but trying to figure it out cannot be all you do. I don’t want that for you, and Mama wouldn’t either,” Rio says, knowing that.

“It just feels so wrong not to,” Nicky admits. “I can feel the spell, Mom. Whenever I’m close to Mama, I can feel what it’s doing to her, can feel how it’s strangling and suffocating the real parts of her, and I hate how violating it feels,” Nicky admits, not sure if that is the best description, but knowing that that is what it feels like, violating. “I can’t just do nothing when I can feel what’s happening to her,” Nicky says sadly.

“Nicky, I’m not asking you to, I never would,” Rio admits, trying to keep the horror she is feeling as Nicky describes what the spell Agatha is under feels like, out of her voice. “Let’s make a deal,” Rio says, and Nicky gives her an interested look. “You give high school a try until Christmas, a real try, that means you try to make friends, and you try to be apart of the world, and while you’re at school, I’ll continue your research,” Rio tells her son, knowing that Nicky is obsessively searching for an answer, a way to help Agatha. “We work on helping Mama together, so it doesn’t consume you,” Rio tells her son. “And at Christmas we’ll make a decision about revaluation,”

“I guess that sounds fair… you’ve got a deal,” Nicky says.

“Good,” Rio responds, and once she does Nicky laughs. “What?” Rio asks curious.

“There are like a million warnings against making deals with death,” Nicky says amused.

“With good reasons, but don’t worry you have nothing to worry about,” Rio assures her son, putting her arm around her son, and the two of them drift into silence as they sit together, Rio searching for Agatha as they and she finds herself feeling disappointed when she doesn’t see her.

A week has passed since Nicky and Rio made their deal and practically every day since Nicky has wondered if he has made the right decision, and as he gets ready Nicky is feeling that doubt even more.

“NICKY! BREAKFAST!” Rio yells from downstairs, knowing that she doesn’t want Nicky to make things harder on himself by being late on his first day.

“Coming,” Nicky calls back, and after picking up his bag he heads downstairs.

About a minute later Nicky walks into the kitchen and the second he does Rio uses her phone to take a lot of photos of him, something which Nicky has realised she has been doing a lot.

“Seriously? More photos?” Nicky asks his mother, looking annoyed.

“Of course more photos, it’s a big day,” Rio tells her son.

“Mom, I love you, but this photo taking habit of yours is getting really out of control,” Nicky tells his mother.

“There is nothing wrong with wanting to preserve moments,” Rio tells her son, and because he knows his mother he knows there is something she isn’t saying.

“Why are you… Mama,” Nicky realises. “You’re taking photos to show Mama when we break the spell,” Nicky realises, feeling like such an idiot for not realising that sooner.

“She’s missing out on so much, and I know she’s never going to get it back. So, I thought if I could take photos and videos, I’d at least have something to show her when we get her back,” Rio explains to her son, needing to focus on what they will do for Agatha after they lift the spell rather than her fear that they won’t manage to break it.

“Okay, that’s actually a really good reason,” Nicky realises, then sighs. “Okay, you can as many photos and videos you want to show mama,”

“Glad you agree,” Rio responds, as while she was going to keep taking photos anyway it is nice to have Nicky’s okay. “How are you feeling about school?” Rio asks curious.

“Nervous,” Nicky admits.

“You have no reason to be, you’ll be fine Mi Conejito,” Rio tells her son.

“Hope so,” Nicky says nervously, and his mother hugs him. After a few moments the two of them break apart and have breakfast together before Nicky heads off to school where, to his surprise, he actually enjoys his first day.

November 2024

Two months have passed since Nicky started school and to his surprise, he actually enjoys himself, though every time he goes to school he feels incredibly guilty, despite what Rio has told him multiple times, that he is enjoying himself when he feels like he should be helping his Mama.

For an entirety Rio has been ferrying people to where they need to go, there have been times where she found the job difficult, and one time in particular where she found it incredibly painful, so painful that she didn’t want to do it, but as she returns home from her latest time taking someone to the veil she knows she has never felt the amount of overwhelming feelings she is currently feeling.

Anger, pain, devastation, heartbreak, guilt, fury are all emotions that Rio feels as she returns to her son after taking Wanda Maximoff, the Scarlet Witch herself, to the veil that separates life from death. Having teleported straight into the house, as she couldn’t bring herself to walk past Agatha’s house, Rio spends a few minutes collecting herself before heading up to Nicky’s room.

As she approaches her sons room Rio needs to take several deep, calming, breaths, even though she technically doesn’t have to breathe. Getting to Nicky’s room Rio isn’t at all surprised to find Nicky sitting at his desk, digging through ancient spell books in an attempt to find a way to lift the spell on Agatha, something Rio knows might be impossible after what just happened.

“Nicky,” Rio says to her son, and he looks up at her.

“I know, I know, I should be in bed,” Nicky says, as he sees her.

“It’s okay,” Rio says to her son, as she walks towards him.

“Mom? What’s wrong?” Nicky asks, knowing from his mothers’ tone of voice that something is very wrong.

“There’s no easy way to say this, so I’m just going to say it, Wanda Maximoff is dead,” Rio tells her son. “I took her to the veil, she crossed over, but something felt different,” Rio admits, considering what she is Rio wouldn’t be surprised if Wanda came back, but that’s not her current problem. “She wouldn’t tell me how to break the spell,” Rio admits, honestly not sure if Wanda knew, but also knowing that as soon as Wanda realised that she cares about Agatha there was no way she was going to help. “I honestly don’t know how her death has effected the spell,” Rio tells her son.

“Let’s find out,” Nicky says as he quickly gets to his feet and hurries out of the room.

“Nicky wait,” Rio says as she gets up and chases after her son, getting to him as they both get to the front door. “Nicky, we don’t know effect Wanda’s death will have on the spell,” Rio tells her son.

“I know, but whatever effect it has I’ll be able to feel, I’ll know,” Nicky responds. “We need to know Mom,” Nicky tells her.

“Yeah, we do,” Rio confirms. “How close do you need to get?” Rio asks, as they have never actually talked about that.

“Ideally same room,” Nicky responds, knowing that will allow him to truly ‘feel’ the spell and the effects it is having on her.

“Okay, let’s go,” Rio says and the two of them head towards Agatha’s house.

A couple of minutes later Rio and Nicky get to Agatha’s house, and seeing no sign that she is awake, Rio uses her magic to open the locked door allowing both mother and son to enter.

“We’ll search down here first,” Rio tells her son in a quiet voice, Nicky nods, and they both head into the living room where they find Agatha unconscious.

Hurrying forward Rio checks and is relieved when she realises that Agatha is just asleep. “She’s asleep,” Rio says, turning around to look at her son, and as she sees the look on his face Rio feels dread rise up inside of her. “Nicky?” Rio asks, and Nicky stumbles back, but before he can fall Rio hurries over to stabilize him. “I’ve got you,” Rio assures her son as she helps lower him to his knees. “What do you feel?” Rio asks, knowing that that is what they need to talk to, as she squats down on the ground next to him, feeling terrified about what he is going to say next.

“The spell, it’s so much stronger,” Nicky admits, feeling the ‘weight’ of it. “It can’t draw strength from Wanda anymore so the last of her strength, before she died, went into keeping the spell intact,” Nicky admits, taking a couple of deep breaths, do to what he is feeling. “I can feel Mama bubbling deep below, but when I tried to reach that with my magic that part of her got buried deeper,” Nicky revels, and as he does Rio has a horrible feeling what he means by that.

“Are you saying you don’t think the spell can be broken?” Rio asks, needing to know.

“No, I’m saying it can be. but not by challenging her reality outright like we’ve been trying, but by using her reality itself to loosen the hold the spell has on her,” Nicky admits. “We need to start by figuring out a crack, turn that crack into something bigger,” Nicky realises. “Give the part of Mama buried below a place to escape too, allow the hold to lessen a little,” Nicky explains.

“How do we do that?” Rio asks, realising from what her son is saying that confronting Agatha with the truth isn’t going to work.

“I don’t know,” Nicky admits. “But I know where to start my research now,” Nicky admits. “We’re gong to figure this out, Mom, I really think we are,” Nicky admits, having faith, and in response Rio just hugs her son, feeling comforted by his faith, but also feeling terrified that they aren’t going to figure it out.

December 2024

Just over a month has passed since Wanda died and ever since Nicky has been obsessively searching for a way to break the spell that is now even stronger. While Rio has been doing her best to help, she is also trying to hide from her son how terrified she is that they aren’t going to succeed.

It’s New Years Eve and even though he was out with some people he goes to school with Nicky is returning home before midnight. As soon as he walks into the house Nicky gets a feeling that something is ‘off’.

For a second Nicky debates what to do, before deciding that he needs to know what is going on, and so with his left hand he makes magic dance around his fingers, while he pulled the knife his mother gave him with his right. Walking deeper into the house Nicky is just confused about what he feels until he hears sniffling. Not even thinking about possible danger Nicky walks towards the sound and after a few seconds he sees something which makes his heart break, his Mom, sitting on the floor, sobbing while surrounded by no less than eight empty scotch bottles.

Without a word Nicky gets rid of his magic, and puts his knife back in it’s safe place before walking over to his mother and sitting next to her.

“I’ve got you mom,” Nicky says, as he puts his arms around his mom.

“I miss her so much,” Rio says, as she completely breaks down in her sons’ arms, something she has never done before. “I just want her back,” Rio says.

“I know,” Nicky says, having no idea what else to do and so he just holds his mother, the cosmic entity, as she falls apart, Nicky knowing that he needs to do whatever he can to break the incredibly strong and intrinsic spell on is mama, that he owes that to both his moms.

For a while Nicky just holds Rio while she cries, until something truly concerning happens, and she passes out. Knowing that he cannot leave her on the ground Nicky uses his magic to levitate her and take her to her bed. Once Rio is in bed Nicky grabs his books and starts to research, knowing he is not going to give up until he has his answers, and when Rio wakes up in a few hours she doesn’t remember what happened, something which Nicky is sure is a good thing, and which isn’t something he is going to enlighten her about.

January 2025

A couple of weeks has passed since Rio completely broke down, something which she has no memory of doing, and ever since Nicky has been doing everything he can to try and help his moms. While he has been able to do ‘little’ things to help them Nicky knows that the only thing that will actually help them is breaking the spell, and Nicky hates that so far, his research hasn’t helped him figure out a way to do that.

It is Sunday afternoon and both Nicky and Rio are in the kitchen of their house making food together, food that is not for either of them.

“And you’re sure we haven’t made anything Mama doesn’t like?” Nicky asks, as he looks between the various things they have made, knowing that Rio will know that better than him.

“We’ve only made her favourites…. Whether Agnes likes them is another matter altogether,” Rio admits.

“Several things seem to be the same no matter the reality, hopefully taste in food is one of the things that stays the same,” Nicky comments, knowing one of those things is the reaction Agatha has to the name Nicky and because of that his name is never said around Agatha.

“Hopefully,” Rio responds. “You know, we talked about this once, what we would do for a milestone birthday such as this one,” Rio tells her son, knowing that it is Agatha’s three hundredth and fiftieth birthday.

“Yeah? What did you decide to do?” Nicky asks his mother, who gets caught up in a very fond memory. “Mom?” Nicky asks, after a few seconds, noticing the fond look on his mother’s face.

“You probably don’t want to know,” Rio admit, as what she is thinking is certainly not PG.

“Gross,” Nicky says, pulling a face, but then he turns serious. “Do you really think we’re going to be able to do this?” Nicky asks his mom.

“I think as long as we don’t remind Mama of what is actually real, who she is, we should be able to,” Rio admits. “I think we both understand enough about how Mama perceives reality to be able to manipulate it,” Rio tells her son, knowing that they have both been ‘studying’ the ways Agatha perceives reality.

“I wish we didn’t have to manipulate her,” Nicky admits.

“I know,” Rio tells her son. “But unless we break the spell it’s the only thing we can do,” Rio says.

“Until,” Nicky corrects.

“Huh?”

“Until we break the spell, not unless, until,” Nicky corrects. “We are going to break the spell, Mom,” Nicky says, feeling worried because it almost seems like his mom is losing faith.

“I know,” Rio says, though she knows she is having a hard time believing that lately. “Are you ready to go?” Rio asks, not wanting to talk about that anymore at the moment.

“Yeah,” Nicky says, as they both start to pick up the stuff they have made. “Are you sure you’re going to be, okay? I know Mama’s words hurt you even if you try to hide it,” Nicky says to his mother.

“They do, but it hurts more not being around her,” Rio admits, and the two of them head out of the house together, Nicky feeling worried about both his mothers as they go.

A couple of minutes later Rio and Nicky have made their way to Agatha’s house and are knocking on their door, after a few seconds the door opens to reveal Agatha.

“What are you doing here?” Agatha asks, looking at Rio with an annoyed look on her face, which to Rio is easier to handle than the looks of hatred she often gets from Agatha these days.

“You invited us over yesterday for your birthday,” Rio says, knowing that it is risky to mention Agatha’s birthday but feel that as long as they don’t mention how old she is they should be okay.

“I did?” Agatha asks surprised.

“You did.” Nicky confirms. “So, we brought food…. If you’re still interested, I know you’ve been really caught up with the article you’re researching,” Nicky says to Agatha, trying to tie their lie into her current version of reality to get her to agree.

“I guess I could eat,” Agatha admits. “And some company wouldn’t be too bad, even if it is yours,” Agatha says to Rio, looking less than happy to see her even if she is happy to see Nicky.

“I’ll take that to mean you’re inviting us in,” Rio says, and she walks into the house with Nicky right behind her.

For the next couple of hours Rio, Nicky and Agatha get to actually spend time together. From Agatha’s point of view, she is mending fences with someone who hurt her in the past while from Rio and Nicky’s they are actually getting to celebrate Agatha’s three hundred and fiftieth birthday together. As Nicky looks between his mothers, both of whom are drinking glasses of wine, he knows that as nice as it is, it’s not the way it should be, and he knows, without a doubt, that he needs to figure out a way to break the spell Agatha is under sooner rather than later.

Chapter 12

Chapter 12

AN: Thank you so much for the support. So, I loved 1x07. If you curious this is marked AU for a reason, even if things at certain times seem very close to cannon. I am still figuring out how everything will fit in the story. Next chapter will be up in about 12 hours.

March 2025

Two months have passed since Agatha’s three hundred and fiftieth birthday and in that time, it has become clear that the hostility Agatha shows Rio every time her version of reality resets is really starting to get to her.

As Rio has been gone longer than she typically is doing her job Nicky is distracting himself from the worry he is feeling about her by doing a whole lot of cooking. Having just finished cooking some chicken Nicky goes to put it on the bench when he notices just how much he cooked.

“I may have gone a bit overboard,” Nicky realises, as he looks between all the food he has made, knowing that if his mother were to arrive home, she would realise that he was worried as Rio knows the various ways, he distracts himself when he is concerned. “Mama could probably use some food,” Nicky realises, and he proceeds to pack up a lot of the food he has made so that he can give to Agatha, realising that that achieves two things, one is making sure his mama is looked after and two not causing his mom to worry when she realises how concerned he has been.

About ten minutes after he realised just how much food he has made Nicky is carrying a very large bag that is full of a lot of containers of a lot of the food he’s made and is walking up to Agatha’s door, knocking on it once he is close enough.

“Yes?” Agatha asks, opening the door, and Nicky knows that in her current version of reality she is works from home as tech support, which explains the headband she is wearing.

“Hi Agnes, I was doing some cooking, and I made some extra food, I thought you would like some,” Nicky explains, offering her the bag.

“Oh, that’s lovely! Thank you!” Agnes says, taking the bag form Nicky. “Would you like to come in?” Agnes asks curious.

“I’d love to,” Nicky responds, and he follows his mother into the house.

“This smells amazing, you cooked all this?” Agnes asks as they head towards the kitchen.

“Yeah, I love cooking,” Nicky responds.

“Has it been a hobby of yours for long?” Agnes asks curious as they get to the kitchen, and Agnes gestures to the kitchen bench for Nicky to sit down.

“A while, cooking has always just been something I enjoy,” Nicky says, knowing that he enjoys cooking with his mom, but he has to be careful about mentioning that as he could cause Agatha distressed and that’s the last thing he want to do.

“It’s good to have things you enjoy,” Agnes says, as she starts to put the food Nicky brough her away. “I enjoy fixing problems, and researching,” Agatha tells Nicky, and even though he knows she isn’t his ‘real’ mama right now it means a lot to Nicky to hear about a passion they share.

“I love researching too,” Nicky admits. “When I have a problem, I want to do everything I can to figure it out, no matter what, or how long, it takes” Nicky admits.

“Me too,” Agatha responds, and the two of them exchange smiles as Agatha finishes putting everything away and also sits down. “So, research, cooking, what else do you like to do?” Agatha asks.

“That’s about it, other than learning languages,” Nicky says, knowing he can’t mention magic. “But I have just started to do guitar lessons at school,” Nicky reveals, as he started those lessons after Christmas.

“And you’re not enjoying them?” Agatha asks curious.

“I don’t know,” Nicky admits. “I’m not finding it as easy as I find academic things, which is frustrating,” Nicky admits. “I’m not sure I should continue,” Nicky admits.

“The fact that you’re struggling is exactly why you should continue,” Agnes tells Nicky. “You can’t grow without both knowledge and challenges,” Agatha tells him and from everything his mom has told him over his life Nicky thinks, just for a second that is a flicker of Agatha rather than Agnes.

“Huh, I’ve never thought about it like that,” Nicky admits. “Thanks M…Agnes,” Nicky says, silently cursing himself for his almost slipup. “How’s your work going?” Nicky asks, quickly tuning the topic of conversation to her reality so that he doesn’t cause her harm by causing conflicts with the spell.

“Frustrating,” Agnes says. “People are very stupid,” Agnes responds, and Nicky laughs at that.

To Nicky’s joy he gets to spend the next hour just talking with his Mama, and when he gets home his mom is home again.

The following day Nicky, on his way to school, tries to talk to Agatha about what they talked about the day before, but it quickly becomes clear that her reality has reset, and she has no idea what he is talking about. While it causes him pain deep inside his heart Nicky keeps that to himself as he doesn’t want to cause his mom more pain than he already knows she is in.

June 2025

Three months have passed since Nicky got to spend an hour talking to his mama and because he has taken her advice Nicky has continued his guitar lessons despite how difficult he is finding it.

It’s Monday afternoon and Nicky is returning to the house after spending time at the Westview pool with people he goes to school with and as he walks into the house, he finds his mother sitting at the window seat staring outside, clearly oblivious to everything other than what she is looking at.

“Mom?” Nicky asks concerned as he walks over to her.

“Hi, did you have a good time with your friends?” Rio asks her son.

“Yeah, it was fun, I won our highest jump competition,” Nicky tells his mother.

“Did you use your magic?” Rio asks.

“Not intentionally,” Nicky admits, not even considering not answering honestly. “But in my defence, someone who gives everyone a hard time was winning beforehand,” Nicky explains.

“Then sounds like you did what you needed to do,” Rio tells her son, before turning back to the window.

“Mom? Are you okay?” Nicky asks, glancing out the window to see what she is looking at and considering everything he isn’t overly surprised to realise it is Agatha.

“Today’s our anniversary,” Rio reveals.

“It is?” Nicky asks surprised, feeling like an idiot for not realising that sooner. “How long?” Nicky asks, trying to do the math in his head.

“Two hundred and seventy-one years,” Rio answers, without needing to think about it.

“Wow,” Nicky admits. “Why don’t you go talk to Mama? Spend time with her,” Nicky suggests.

“No,” Rio says, shaking her head. “I can’t deal with her anger, her not knowing who I am, not today,” Rio admits, as Agatha’s reactions to her is really starting to take its toll on her, even if she tries to deny that fact, even if she tries everything to hide that from Nicky.

“When we break this spell, I’m going to make sure you and Mama have an incredible anniversary celebration, I’ll make sure you go all out,” Nicky tells his mother, having no other ideas of how to help her.

“Thanks Mi Conjito,” Rio tells her son, knowing that right now she is struggling to think about what it will be like when the spell is broken, and the two of them drift into silence as they sit together.

After staying with his mom for awhile Nicky has finally headed upstairs while she headed off to do her job. Considering how she is doing Nicky wanted to object to her go, but as he realised that it could be a distraction for her he held his tongue.

Walking into his room Nicky heads straight over to his desk, and turns on his laptop, and opens the webcam.

“Um, hi, Mama, today’s June 9th, 2025, you and Mom have been married for two hundred and seventy-one years, and we’ve all been in Westview for almost two years,” Nicky says, having no idea where he is going with what he is saying, but wanting to say it. “Right now, you’re still trapped, buried beneath the Scarlett Witches’ spell, but if you are watching this it means that I finally figured out how to break it, and if that’s the case I really hope I figure it out soon; Mama I’m really sorry it’s taken so long, I’m really sorry I’ve let you down,” Nicky admits, fighting back his guilt for a moment. “I know Mom is trying to remember everything about me so that she can tell you stories when we break the spell, well there are a few things I want to tell you about Mom,” Nicky admits. “The first is, she loves you, so much, and she’s taken really amazing care of me, she’s trying to be strong, and do everything alone, but I know how much she needs you,” Nicky admits. “There’s so much I could tell you about the last seven years, so many stories, I’m not sure where to start,” Nicky admits, then he gets an idea. “Oh, I know! I got mom to dress up as the Grim Reaper for a Halloween party! She did it once and said never again… she doesn’t know I got photos that I can’t wait to show you,” Nicky says, and he proceeds to spend the next little while telling stories about his mom, telling stories, filming a video he truly believes that one day soon his mama will be able to watch.

August 2025

Two months has passed since Nicky recorded a very long video for his Mama and since then he has recorded a few more shorter videos for her as he has realised that he enjoys doing so.

It is Nicky’s fifteenth birthday and because he knows the tradition well, he is already awake when Rio walks into his room carrying his birthday cake.

“Oh, that’s no fair, you’re meant to let me wake you up,” Rio tells her son.

“Sorry Mom, I was too excited,” Nicky tells her.

“I’ll forgive you, this time,” Rio tells her son. “You know the drill,” Rio says and as he blows out the candles Nicky makes the same wish he has made for the last seven years, having some hope that things are going to “And the record once again holds,” Rio says, in an over the top ‘announcer’ voice.

“I will make sure it always holds, trust me,” Nicky assures his mother.

“Oh, I do,” Rio assures her son as she cuts the cake for both of them, and sits down next to him. “So, any ideas about what you want to do today?” Rio asks Nicky curious.

“One… just not sure what you’ll think about it,” Nicky admits, sounding nervous as what he wants to do is not technically legal, not that he expects that to bother his mom.

“Well, you’ll only know if you say it,” Rio tells her son. “What are you thinking?” Rio asks her son curious.

“I know I can’t legally gat my permit until I’m sixteen, but I was wondering if you’d start to teach me to drive,” Nicky suggests, as even though he can travel by magic means, and is still excitedly looking forward to the day where he can fly a broom with his Mama for the first time, he also wants to learn to drive.

“Of course I can,” Rio tells her son. “I barely use the car might as well teach you to use it,” Rio tells her son, seeing absolutely no problem with teaching her fifteen-year-old son to drive.

“Awesome,” Nicky says with a grin.

“Once you know how to drive if you need to drive around town that’s fine, but not beyond without me knowing, and don’t draw attention to yourself,” Rio tells her son seeing no point in making him wait until he is sixteen to actually drive once he knows, but wanting to put a couple of conditions to make sure he is safe.

“Deal,” Nicky tells his mother.

“Another deal with death,” Rio says. “Those deals are starting to stack up Mi Conejito,” Rio tells her son, who just laughs.

Many hours after Nicky suggested spending his birthday learning to drive that is exactly what he has done, spent the entire day with Rio in the car driving. While he struggled at first, and knows he still has a long way to go Nicky definitely felt like he did well in the time he has had.

By pure chance Nicky and Rio are pulling back into the driveway of their house, with take out, just as Agatha is walking near their house.

“Mom…” Nicky starts to say, and Rio doesn’t even need her to finish the question to know what he wants.

“We can ask if she wants to stay for dinner,” Rio assures her son.

“Thanks Mom,” Nicky says, and he quickly hurries out of the car. “Agnes,” Nicky calls as he runs towards her.

“Well, hello, how can I help you?” Agnes asks, as Nicky gets to her.

“I was actually helping you could help me,” Nicky admits.

“Oh, and how can I do that Kitten?” Agnes asks, as Rio knows that is the most ‘unlike Agatha’ nicknames she has heard Agnes use.

“Today is my birthday, and my mom and I got way too much takeout,” Nicky reveals, that actually being the truth as they couldn’t decide what they wanted so they got everything they wanted to try. “Any chance you’re interested in joining us to eat it all? I know I’d like it,” Nicky says and as he does, he notices Agatha glance at Rio who is standing several steps away.

“I’d like it to,” Rio says knowing what the look on Agatha’s face means even if the real Agatha is deeply buried beneath Agnes.

“We how can I say no to an invitation like that, I’d love to,” Agnes assures them.

“Great, come on!” Nicky says excitedly as he hurries into the house, with his mothers following behind.

About forty-five minutes later Nicky, Rio, and Agatha have had an incredible dinner together, and unlike some of the other times they have spent together there is no tension between Agatha and Rio.

“You’ve got a pretty incredible kid in there,” Agnes says to Rio as the two of them walk into the kitchen carrying the dishes from their dinner while Nicky waits in the dining area.

“Yeah, I do,” Rio says, resisting the urge to say ‘we’.

“Is something wrong?” Agatha asks, having a feeling that there is something Rio isn’t saying, even if she doesn’t really know Rio at the moment.

“No, I just… sometimes I don’t feel like I’m enough for him,” Rio admits, admitting that because it is Agatha she is standing with, even if she isn’t actually Agatha at the moment.

“You are,” Agnes says. “From where I am standing you’ve been an incredible mother to him,” Agnes admits, and while Rio is sure Agnes intends for her words to help Rio her words actually do the opposite.

“I’m not so sure,” Rio admits, turning towards the sink to avoid looking at Agatha, but as she does, she feels Agath touch her shoulder, and just for a second she allows herself to lean into the touch, and while she would like to allow herself to continue doing that, she knows that with Agatha not being herself it wouldn’t be right. “We should get desert ready,” Rio says, trying to pull away from Agatha being the one of the hardest things she has done.

“Are you sure?” Agatha asks, and Rio feels her breath against her neck, and Rio closes her eyes for a few moments to allow herself to dwell on what it feels like to be so close to Agatha once again.

“Unfortunately,” Rio responds, and she heads towards the fridge to get the desert even though she would much rather stay closer to Agatha, and once she has the desert both she and Agatha head back out to re-join Nicky, spending the next couple of hours spending enjoyable time together even if it’s not really Agatha who is with them.

October 2025

Two months have passed since Nicky’s birthday and in that time, he has returned to school for his second year of high school and even though he was completely against going to school when his mother told him that that’s what he was going to be doing he has actually grown to enjoy it.

“So, he was giving a really hard time too a whole bunch of people, being a total ass, so I subtly used my magic to trip him over,” Nicky tells his mother, as the two of them do the dishes in the kitchen after dinner.

“Did anyone see?” Rio asks concerned, as that is her biggest concern.

“Nope,” Nicky responds, “And he hasn’t given anyone a hard time since,” Nicky explains.

“Sounds like the perfect way to deal with bullies,” Rio comments.

“I thought so,” Nicky responds, and as he does, he realises something. “Oh my god,” Nicky suddenly says.

“What?” Rio asks worried.

“I’m taller than you,” Nicky says with a smirk.

“No, you’re not,” Rio says, standing up properly, and knowing that if Nicky is actually taller than her then he is taller than Agatha as well.

“No, I am Mom,” Nicky says with a grin. “I’m really taller than you,” Nicky says with a grin, which makes Rio realises he is right. “This is awesome,” Nicky says, grinning from ear to ear, a look which makes him look so much like Agatha, and in response Rio grabs the tap and uses it to spray Nicky with water.

“Really? Oh, this is war mom,” Nicky says, and the two of them engage in a water fight, both of them using magic when they needed, which results in the two of them spending a lot of time laughing, while half the house, and both of them, get covered in water.

December 2025

Two months have passed since Nicky realised, he was taller than Rio, and therefore Agatha, and while Nicky allowed himself a little while to enjoy that his mind quickly went to Agatha and how it was something else, she missed out on.

As he doesn’t want his mama to miss out on anything else Nicky has become even more obsessive about tyring to find a way to loosen the hold Wanda’s spell has on Agatha so it can be broken. While she knows what her son is doing Rio is becoming incredibly concerned about him as it has been days since Nicky left the house.

“Nicky,” Rio says, walking into the living room that is covered in books which Nicky is sitting in the middle of.

After leaving the house Nicky starts to walk towards the town square, purposely avoiding going towards his Mama’s house because considering everything he is feeling incredibly guilty about still not managing to break the spell.

As he walks around the town square Nicky can’t help but think of his first Christmas in Westview when he, and both his mums, got to spend time together, where they got to have an actual holiday together. Back then Nicky believed it wouldn’t be much longer before he broken the spell, and now two years later he still hasn’t managed to do it, and he’s starting to hate himself for that.
