You just do everything you can to make sure it’s not you or mama I need to collect,” Rio tells her son, knowing that even without knowing Nicky is alive she won’t be able to resist staying away from Agatha on The Road if she is called.

“I’ll try,” Nicky says, though he isn’t sure how he feels arranging for people to come on the road who may die.

“Good,” Rio tells her son, and the two of them proceed to go over their plan several more times and figure out a few specific details that they know they need to decide on. As they discuss everything Rio knows that Nicky isn’t a big fan of the Sigil idea, so she does her best to try and convince him that it is necessary.

October 9th 2026

Three weeks have passed since Nicky figured out a way to break the spell on his Mama, since Rio discovered that the Salem Seven is getting close to both Nicky and Agatha, and ever since then the two of them have obsessively been working on their plan. While Nicky is still not a big fan of the sigil idea, he has accepted that it is necessary as both he and Rio know that it’s only a matter of time before the Salem Seven make their move.

It’s a Friday afternoon and Nicky is arriving home, walking straight into the living room where he and Rio have set up a board which has the steps of their plans all over it.

“How was school?” Rio asks from where she is staring at the board, as Nicky walks into the room.

“Good, I told Eddie we are going away this weekend, that we may be gone next week to, so he doesn’t try to come over or question why he can’t get in contact with me,” Nicky tells his mom, as he puts his bag down then walks over to his mother.

“Not technically a lie, good choice,” Rio tells him.

“Yeah, I thought so,” Nicky admits, though he does feel bad about lying to his boyfriend. “Have you been staring at this all day?” Nicky asks his mother curious.

“Pretty much,” Rio admits. “I just want to make sure we’ve got everything covered,” Rio admits.

“I think we do,” Nicky admits. “I also think you’re right and that fact that even after I break the spell Mama may have to claw her way out of it herself,” Nicky admits, knowing that he will do everything he can to break the spell, but it will ultimately be up to his mama to take the last step.

“It would make sense considering what we know how the spell works,” Rio admits. “And it might take some time,” Rio admits, though she doesn’t expect that to take more than a few hours.

“Yep, that’s factored in,” Nicky says, looking between everything on the board. “So, we know based on how long she stays in each reality that Mama’s reality will change at midnight, is this it? Is it time?” Nicky asks his mother.

“It is,” Rio confirms, turning to look at her son. “Are you ready for this?” Rio asks her son.

“Not sure,” Nicky admits. “But I know I don’t want to wait anymore,” Nicky admits, both he and Rio knowing that after the last whispers she has heard from the Salem Seven that they cannot wait any longer, and that even if the Salem Seven weren’t a factor neither of them would want to. “So, I’ll head to Mama’s, try to influence her next persona, and then in the morning we’ll see if we succeeded,” Nicky says.

“And if we have, I’ll play my role in her reality and give her more clues,” Rio says. “Then we cast the Sigil,” Rio says, knowing that they have to do the elements of their plan in a very specific order.

“Yeah,” Nicky says, in an almost disappointed tone of voice.

“Nicky, I know you don’t like the Sigil, but it’s necessary,” Rio tells her son, who she knows has been trying to think of another way to protect himself since they came up with the plan.

“Just because I know that doesn’t mean I have to like it,” Nicky admits. “You and Mama both not knowing who I am, it’s not something I can like,” Nicky tells his mom.

“Me either,” Rio confirms, having made it clear over the past few weeks that while it is her suggestion and it is what they are going to do, she doesn’t like it.

“I know,” Nicky says with a sigh. “Let’s go over everything one more time than I’ll head over,” Nicky tells his mom, who nods, and that is just what they do.

About half an hour after Nicky got home from school, he and his mom have gone over all elements of their plan one more time and he is walking towards Agatha’s door once again carrying a basket of baked goods he made. As he gets close to the door Nicky pauses and takes a deep breath.

“You can do this, Nicky,” Nicky mutters to himself before walking to the familiar door and knocking.

Seconds after he knocked the door opens to reveal Agatha who in her current version of reality thinks she is a handyperson and because of that she has several spoons hanging from her belt, as she believes they are tools.

“Hi Agnes, I know you have been working hard so I thought I would bring you some snacks,” Nicky explains, offering her the basket.

“Oh, that’s so sweet, come in,” Agnes says. “Come in,”

“Thanks,” Nicky says as they walk in into the house. “Here,” Nicky says, offering the basket to her, and as their hands touch at the same time Nicky knows that’s his cue. “Did you watch that true crime documentary last night?” Nicky asks, purposely keeping hold of the basket so that he can continue to touch his mama’s hand. “The one with the Scarlett haired women who no one could identify, wouldn’t be amazing to be the detective who solved that?” Nicky asks, finally pulling away form his mama once he has said what he needs to say.

“Yeah, I guess it might be,” Agnes says, looking curious. “What can you tell me about it? it sounds fascinating,” Agnes says.

“Oh, I can tell you everything,” Nicky says, with a grin, as the two of them head towards the kitchen and he proceeds to spend the next hour planting as many seeds as possible to influence what Agatha’s next version of reality becomes.

Chapter 15

After a night where Nicky got basically no sleep, and Rio didn’t ‘rest’ like she tends to do as they were so worried about what they are trying to do, the two of them are up early and are once again in their living room. As it gives them the exact view, they need both Rio and Nicky are looking through the bay window watching Agatha, who is seemingly taking pictures of a neighbour’s lawn.

“That could be Mama seeing a body,” Nicky realises, though he knows it’s hard to be sure as he isn’t seeing what she is seeing. “Do you think we did it?” Nicky asks his mother, wanting to know what she is thinking. “Do you think we did actually influence Mama’s reality?” Nicky asks, as that’s what it seems like to him, but he wants to know what Rio thinks.

“It definitely seems like it,” Rio confirms, feeling hope that they are actually going to pull this off, but she also knows that they cannot get ahead of herself, that what they are trying to do is too important to let that happen. “Okay, time for me to get ready to do my part,” Rio says, reaching out and placing a comforting hand on Nicky’s shoulder, which she squeezes, before walking away, heading upstairs while Nicky continues to watch his mama, taking notice of everything, so he can try to figure out just how she is perceiving everything.

A little while after Rio and Nicky first saw Agatha take picture of a neighbour’s lawn Rio, who has gotten changed into an outfit to fit with Agatha’s reality even though it’s not actually necessary, is approaching Agatha’s house. As she walks towards the house Rio notices that a neighbour, who’s name Rio has never bothered to learn in the last three years, is standing in the doorway, clearly talking to Agatha.

“Now get to the part I’m not gonna like,” Rio hears Agatha say and she has to resist the urge to laugh at that perfect opening.

“Here I am,” Rio says, as she walks into Agatha’s view.

“Okay, fancy dirt always attracts the attention of the feds,” Agnes says, and Rio knows she can make this work.

“She thinks she is a detective today, solving a murder,” The neighbour says to Rio, not addressing Agatha as he knows that Agatha will hear what she wants to hear. “She was walking around so I just wanted to make sure she was okay,” The neighbour says, and Rio can admit that that is one thing she has appreciated about Westview, that everyone looks out for Agatha.

“Probably a good idea, but don’t worry, I can look out for her today,” Rio tells the neighbour, hoping that by doing that she will be able to keep everyone else away from Agatha while she and Nicky do what they have to do.

“Eat my ass, Chief,” Agnes suddenly says, and Rio has to laugh that, as it is times like that when she sees the flicker of the true Agatha show through.

“I’ll leave you to it, good luck,” The neighbour says to Rio, before walking away, and after he walks away Rio walks into the house, closing the door behind her, and sits down across from Agatha, looking around as she does in hopes that she will get some kind of hint that will tell her what Agatha is seeing the environment around her as.

“It’s been a long time,” Rio says, knowing that ever since the last time she and Nicky made an explicated attempt to break the spell that Agatha always sees her as someone from her past, so she might as well use that to her advantage, might as well use that as an opening.

“What are you doing here?” Agnes asks, and Rio isn’t at all surprised to hear the hostility in her voice, as that is something she has unfortunately gotten used to over the last three years.

“My job,” Rio answers, doing so for two reasons, one is because she knows that it will fit with the version of reality she assumes Agatha is seeing, and the second is because she knows the anger that Agatha feels towards her job so she hopes that by mentioning it, considering it is a mundane detail connected to strong emotions, she can cause a crack.

“You wanna take control of my investigation,” Agatha says, and Rio has to bite the corner of her cheek at that as there are as so many other thing she would say to that, but because she knows it won’t get what she really wants she just instead spreads out a little in the chair she is sitting in, knowing that Agatha is watching her closely even if she doesn’t know what Agatha is actually seeing.

“No, if you wanna take control… you can be,” Rio says, purposely using a tone of voice she knows Agatha has always liked.

“She… the body was moved across state lines. Is that your play?” Agatha asks, and Rio feels some satisfaction that she can still cause Agatha to be flustered, even when she doesn’t even know who she is, but just like every time she has gotten closer to Agatha in the past three years, she refuses to do anything about it when Agatha isn’t herself.

“Is this really how you see yourself?” Rio asks, once again trying to cause a crack, but when Agatha doesn’t say anything about that she knows she has to give more clues so that Agatha can start to put things together. “Sure, let’s talk about the case,” Rio says, knowing that will help with the ultimate goal. “What are your theories? How’d she end up in the ravine?” Rio asks, saying ravine as that will fit with the seeds Nicky planted the day before but also knowing that if it is not right Agatha will hear whatever fits with her reality.

“No drag marks, thinking the perp carried her,” Agnes comments.

“Uh, seems logically,” Rio says, picking up one of the many, probably empty, files that Agatha has lying around and waking over to her. “But you don’t really believe that because… no tracks for the perp,” Rio says, as she sits right next to Agatha, assuming that in Agatha’s reality she will see her opening a file. “Not a leaf disturbed before Forensics showed up. It’s almost like she just magically appeared,” Rio says, purposely moving he hands in the exact way she knows Agatha moves her hands when using her magic.

“Let’s stick to reality here,” Agatha says with a scoff, and Rio knows that she has to temporarily dial back her attempts to put cracks in the spell otherwise she risks the spell ‘fighting back’ in a sense.

“Sure,” Rio says, crossing her arms, planning on taking her next cue from Agatha, as that is the only way she can use the conversion to her advantage.

“If there’s one thing we can agree on, it’s that these cases are always about the place. The specific small town, the history of it, the people in it, the secrets buried beneath it. That’s where the answers lie,” Agnes tells Rio, who once again realises that she has an opening to put a crack in the spell, to loosen the hold the spell has on Agatha.

“Well, who better to solve the mystery than one of Westview’s very own?” Rio asks, knowing that in every version of reality Agnes has lived in Westview a long time. “You’ve lived here your whole life. Isn’t that true… Agnes?” Rio asks, putting an emphasis on the name Agnes to make Agatha think that there is something wrong with that, and in response Agatha gets up and walks to the door, telling Rio that she has reached the limits of how she can put back against the spell for now.

“I don’t want you here,” Agnes says and because she has heard Agatha say that a lot over the past three years Rio isn’t even phased by that, so she gets up and walks to the door as well.

“Te Veo,” Rio says to Agatha before leaving, knowing she has done what she can to put cracks in the spell and now they have to give Agatha time to dwell on what she has said, to think about the clues she and Nicky left, which will hopefully cause cracks in the spell to form, cracks that Rio knows Nicky needs to cast the spells that he hopes will release Agatha.

“How’d it go?” Nicky asks, the second Rio walks back into their house, not long after she left Agatha’s house, as the entire time Rio has been gone Nicky has been wondering, and worrying, about what was going on between his mothers.

“As well as it could,” Rio tells her son, wanting to be optimistic but also not wanting Nicky to be disappointed if it doesn’t work out. “She thought I was an FBI agent so I gave a few more clues, I think I might have said somethings that could cause cracks,” Rio tells her son, feeling cautiously optimistic but at the same time she is terrified that they aren’t going to be successful.

“Good,” Nicky says, and then he notices exactly what his mother is wearing. “What’s with the outfit? You know that Mama would have just imagined you in whatever fit with her version of reality, so why did you dress up?” Nicky asks curious, as that doesn’t make sense to him.

“I had a point to make,” Rio says with a smirk.

“Yeah, I don’t want to know anymore,” Nicky admits, knowing his mother well enough to know that, and Rio laughs.

“Good choice,” Rio says, walking over to her son. “Nicky, there is something I want to tell you before we do the Sigil,” Rio tells her son.

“Mom?” Nicky asks confused, having no idea what else his mom could want to talk about.

“I am so proud of you, I love you so much,” Rio tells her son, wanting to make that clear before he deals with a version of her who doesn’t know who he is, before hugging her son.

“I love you too,” Nicky responds, feeling his mother kiss his cheek.

“And Mama loves you too,” Rio tells her son as she breaks apart from her son. “When the spell breaks, you’re going to spend time with a version of Mama who will put on a persona she uses to protect herself,” Rio tells her son, feeling the need to give the warning.

“What does that mean?” Nicky asks, confused, but he does have a bad feeling about that.

“It means she will be what people expect her to be, she will let anyone you interact with believe the worst in her,” Rio tells her son, knowing that she has always hated when Agatha does that, but it’s a side effect of what Evanora did to her that Agatha can’t shake.

“That’s awful,” Nicky says with a frown, not wanting that for his mama. “So, if someone is hostile to her….”

“She will be hostile back,” Rio finishes, with a nod, feeling glad that Nicky understands what she is saying.

“It’s because of Evanora, isn’t it?” Nicky asks and Rio tenses at her son actually saying the name of his Mama’s abuser. “Everything she did to mama that you won’t tell me,” Nicky says as while his mom has said enough for him to put some pieces together, he knows that there is a hell of a lot that he doesn’t know.

“Yes,” Rio confirms. “Nicky, I haven’t told you what Evanora did because you don’t need to know, and because Mama wouldn’t want you to know,” Rio admits, knowing that without a doubt. “But what you do need to know is that you should not take any hostility Mama shows you personally, it’s how she protects herself,” Rio tells her son. “When she finds out she has been under the control of another for three years, and that she doesn’t have her magic, she is going to be feeling vulnerable and your Mama hates feeling vulnerable,” Rio says, knowing exactly why that is, but it is something she would never, even consider, telling their son. “Just keep that in mind when interacting with her before she knows who you are,” Rio says, desperately hoping that by trying to protect herself Agatha doesn’t say, or do, anything that hurts Nicky as she knows the effect that will have on both of them.

“I will,” Nicky confirms.

“And even though Mama doesn’t have her active magic, no matter what….” Rio starts to say

“Don’t use my magic against her,” Nicky finishes. “I know,” Nicky assures Rio, as she has made that clear to him multiple times over the past three years.

“Good,” Rio says, as the last thing she wants is for Nicky to accidently use his magic against his mother because she knows exactly what would happen.

“We’ve got to cast the Sigil soon, don’t we?” Nicky asks, knowing that this is the part of the plan he has been dreading.

“We do,” Rio confirms. “I will be unconscious for a little while after we cast it,” Rio says, knowing that that is because she has so much ‘knowledge’ connected to Nicky being alive again, that will have to be ‘hidden’.

“Which is why I’m not approaching Mama until after sunset,” Nicky says.

“And we also want to give the best chance for more cracks to form,” Rio reminds her son.

“Yeah, I know,” Nicky confirms. “So, this damn Sigil, I can trigger it if I say my name?” Nicky asks, wanting to go over what he hates one more time just to make sure he hasn’t forgotten anything important.

“Yes, both Nicky Vidal-Harkness or Nicholas Scratch, and any variation of it,” Rio tells her son. “It will also be triggered if you talk about your life or anything about your identity that could reveal who you are,” Rio tells her son, who nods. “Do you remember the phase to destroy it?” Rio asks, wanting to double check.

“Yeah,” Nicky says, and he speaks the phase to break the Sigil, a phase in a language only he and Rio speak.

“Good,” Rio says approvingly. “Nicky, only use it in an emergency, when you really need us to know who you are,” Rio tells her son. “The second the Sigil is destroyed everyone, including the Salem Seven and every other enemy Mama and I have made over the centuries are going to know who you are, which means I am serious when I say you can only destroy it if it’s an emergency,” Rio warns her son. “As hard as it may be just being around Mama and I when we don’t know who you are that’s not an emergency,” Rio tells her son, needing to make that clear, even if it is harsh.

“I know,” Nicky admits.

“You have good instincts, trust them,” Rio tells her son. “I know you’ll know when there is an emergency otherwise the Sigil will be destroyed when we reach the end of The Road,” Rio tells her son.

“I know,” Nicky says with a nod. “Still hate it though,” Nicky admits, wanting to once more makes that clear.

“I know,” Rio tells her son before hugging him tightly. “Keep your knife with you at all times, but try not to let Mama see it,” Rio tells her son, knowing that Agatha will be able to identify it as the knife she gave Nicky is identical to hers, as she continues to hug him as she doesn’t want to let him go.

“I will,” Nicky assures his mother, as he continues to hug her tightly.

For a few minutes Rio and Nicky continue to hug each other, both knowing that the next time they see each other Rio will have no idea who Nicky is, which is something neither of them are trying to think about.

“Mom, we should probably let go at some point,” Nicky tells his mother.

“I know,” Rio says, and she places a kiss on her son’s head before reluctantly letting him go. “I love you so much, you and Mama are everything to me, always have been, always will be,” Rio tells her son. “Even if it doesn’t seem like it after the Sigil is in place,” Rio tells her son.

“I know, you’ve shown me that every single day of my life,” Nicky tells his mother. “You should probably cast that Sigil before we change our minds,” Nicky tells his mother, being sure that they are close to doing so and while he doesn’t like the Sigil idea, he knows that it necessarily.

“Yeah, we should,” Rio says, taking a step back from her son, and while she knows it’s necessary that it’s the best way to keep Nicky safe, to make sure Agatha gets her powers back which she is going to need to face the Salem Seven, Rio knows she would give anything not to do what she is about to do.

“It will be okay, Mom,” Nicky says, even though he isn’t sure he believes that, because he doesn’t want his mother to feel more guilty than she already does.

“I love you,” Rio says, and she proceeds to cast the Sigil that will protect her son’s identity from everyone, including her.

For the next couple of minutes Nicky watches as his mother casts the Sigil and he knows the second it is in place as he watches his mother fall to the ground. Hurrying over to his mother Nicky checks to make sure he is okay, and to Nicky’s absolute relief she seems to be fine, or as fine as she can be without knowing who he is.

“I’ll make you proud Mom, I’ll be strong,” Nicky promises his mother. “I’ll help Mama, and we’ll finish The Road, we’ll be together again,” Nicky says before leaning down and places a gentle kiss on his mother’s forehead. “I love you,” Nicky says before heading to the door.

Once he gets to the door Nicky looks back at his mom one last time before walking out of the house, knowing that he needs to be strong because his Mom and Mama, even if they don’t know, are counting on him, and he will never let them down.

In the hours that follow Rio casting the Sigil to hide Nicky’s identity Nicky spends his time walking around Westview, apart from when he has some food, until after sunset. Once the sunsets Nicky knows it’s time to put the next step into motion and so he makes his way to his Mama’s house, but as he approaches the house Nicky sees something he wasn’t expecting.

As his mother walks into his mama’s house Nicky knows that he needs to have some idea what is going on before he can do the next step of the plan. And she says, that I was using the wrong foundation brush,” Agnes says, and both Agatha and Rio laugh, Nicky knowing that that is a big dela with Agatha doesn’t know who Rio is and when Rio has no memory that he is alive. “Anyway… I have a lead in the case,” Agatha says.

“Eastview,” Agatha answers.

“Eastview? See, I thought you turned into a pumpkin that far afield,” Rio jokes, which tells Nicky she still knows parts of what’s going on even if she doesn’t know about him.

“Hey, I travel, I’m worldly,” Agnes objects.

“Where have you travelled?” Rio asks, with a laugh and as she does it quickly becomes clear to both Nicky and Rio that Agatha is becoming distressed, and because of that Nicky knows what he has to do.

“Okay, what about the car wreck?” Nicky hears Rio ask.

As he knows that he needs to get close to his mama so that he can cast the spells he needs to cast, ideally without his mom becoming involved as she will have more questions than the current version of his mama, Nicky knows that he has to play into his mother’s reality.

Coming to a decision Nicky makes his way to the back of his mama’s house, and enters through the back door, knowing that it will be unlocked as it always is.

“Okay, how I am going to do this?” Nicky asks himself as he knows that what he needs to do is draw his ama away from his mom, as he looks around. “Crash and run, sorry Mom, Mama,” Nicky decides, feeling a little bad about interrupting whatever conversation they are having, and he uses his magic to cause several of the appliances to be knocked over.

“HEY!” Agatha’s voice yells, and Nicky purposely waits until his mama sees him before he goes running.

Over the next minute or so Nicky runs so that his mama would chase him, and as she starts to struggle Nicky purposely trips over in her front yard, to allow his mother to ‘arrest’ him.

“You’re under arrest,” Agnes tells Nicky, pulling him to his feet, and while Nicky knows it would be a perfect opportunity to cast the blood-to-blood spell he knows that he needs to make sure that there are cracks in the spell, that it has loosed it’s hold on his mama, before doing so otherwise he risks the blood-to-blood spell not working.

After getting Nicky to his feet Agatha brings him back inside where she sits him down on the living room chair his mother was sitting on earlier. Thanks to his magic Nicky knows that his mom is no longer in the house, he assumes she decided that she didn’t want to be a part of Agatha’s hallucinations anymore, and his mama puts a folder, as well as duct tape and rope, on the coffee table. As he sees the action Nicky, who is glad his mother didn’t bind his hands, suspects that she thinks they are in an interrogation room, which he may be able to use to his advantage.

“So, I’m curious, what compelled you to break into the home of a decorated detective?” Agnes asks.

“Decorated detective? That really fits you,” Nicky says to his mother, as he knows she is an infamous witch, so decorated detective fits, he also knows that she will hear what she needs to hear, so unless he can use the situation to his advantage it won’t matter what he says.

“Let’s talk about you, then, you little dirtbag,” Agnes says.

“Ouch, that hurts,” Nicky admits, but because it’s not the worse thing his mama could say he doesn’t let it get to him.

“Is B&E your regular gig?” Agnes asks.

“Not breaking when the door is unlocked,” Nicky responds, smirking slightly.

“What were you looking for in my house?” Agnes asks.

“You actually,” Nicky says as Agnes moves closer to him.

“See, the things you’re roasting me for are the things that make me dangerous,” Agnes says. “So, you wanna keep poking the bear?” Agnes asks, as she leans in close.

“Not particularly, but I might have to achieve what I want,” Nicky admits, watching his mother carefully so that he can use any opportunity to test whether there are any cracks in the spell yet.

“What were you after?” Agatha asks her son, as she moves back to her chair.

“So, so, many things,” Nicky admits. “But let’s see how you respond to me saying the Witches Road,” Nicky says, as that will tell him if there are any cracks currently in the spell.

“What road?” Agatha asks, and Nicky grins, as that is an opening he has been waiting for.

“The Witches Road, focus on what I am saying, on what you know deep down is real,” Nicky says, as he wants to make sure there are a few more cracks in the spell, that it’s hold has loosed a lot, before he tries to break it completely.

“I was on a road this morning,” Agatha says. “It led to something pretty awful. New question. Where were you last night between the hours of one and three am?” Agatha asks.

“Laying wide awake in my bed down the road thinking about how I am going to help you,” Nicky answers honestly, as Agatha starts to play with her pen, trying to get it to work, and if he wasn’t so used to the way Agatha can be under the spell Nicky would be laughing at her behaviour, but because he is he doesn’t.

“Asleep in bed,” Agnes writes down. “Total loser? Or totally lying? Let’s find out,” Agnes basically yells, as she shows pictures to Nicky, pictures that he assumes are the ones he was taking earlier. “What do you know about this?” Agnes asks, as she basically slams the pictures down.

“Oh, so, so, much,” Nicky comments.

“Tell me about her!” Agnes exclaims, and Nicky decides to see if he can put a few more cracks in Agatha’s perspective before casting the blood to blood, magic to magic spell. “Tell me what happened to her!”

“What are you talking about? These are just flowers,” Nicky says, knowing that how Agatha responds to that will tell him if their plan to put cracks in the spell, to loosen the hold, is working.

“What?” Agatha asks, picking up one of the picture, which tells him that things seem to be working exactly how he and his mom were hoping they would.

“They are just pictures, of someone’s front yard or something,” Nicky says and as he does, he notices his mother look at the painting.

“Why do you keep looking at the painting?” Nicky asks, and as he does, he sees his mother look between the painting, and the pictures she took earlier, a look of confusion on his face which tells Nicky they have cracks, which means it’s time for the next part of the spell.

As Agatha is so focused on trying to make sense of what she is doing Nicky is able to pull his knife and cut his hand, before moving towards Agatha.

“What are you doing?”  Agatha asks confused, as she sees Nicky move.

“Helping you,” Nicky tells his mama as he moves closer to her and quickly slices her hand.

“HEY!” Agatha yells, as Nicky grasps her hand with his own bloody hand, focuses on what he needs to focus on, and starts to recite the two spells he has memorised, the spells that will increase the cracks in reality Agatha is experiencing, and then the second one which increases those cracks enough to break the spells hold. “What… what… have you done…” Agatha says confused, when Nicky has finished his spells.

“Everything I could, now it’s up to you, claw your way out,” Nicky tells his mother, desperately hoping he will succeed.

“You’re not going anywhere,” Agatha tells her son, and to his annoyance she uses the rope to tie his legs, and hands. “You’re going to stay right here,” Agatha says as she takes him towards the hall closest, accidently dropping a locket that Nicky knows means a hell of a lot to her, as they go.

“Seriously? Putting me in the closet before I have a chance to come out to you? Feels rude,” Nicky says, before his mama puts tape over his mouth and pushes him into the closet. “Come on, Mama, break through,” Nicky thinks to himself and as he does, he feels something that makes him feel relief, his powers telling him his mom is now in the house too, as he suspects she realised the Agatha was close to coming to the surface again and she wanted to be around when that happened. “Help her, Mom,” Nicky thinks as while knows it isn’t a part of the plan, he also knows his mom well enough, has heard her talk about his Mama enough, to know that if there is anyone who can help his mama claw out from below the weight of the spell now that he made the opening then it’s his mom.

While Nicky is out in the hall closet Rio and Agatha are both in the kitchen, which to Agatha appears to be the morgue.

“Case close, then?” Rio asks Agatha, who has just been muttering about the body she is seeing, a body which in her perception of reality is that of the Scarlett Witch.

“How did she die?” Agatha asks Rio.

“Wrong question,” Rio says with a scoff, as form her point of view Wanda doesn’t matter, all that matters is Agatha. “That witch is gone, and all the copies of the Darkhold with her, leaving you trapped in her distorted spell,” Rio says. “But you don’t have to stay there, do you?” Rio asks as Agatha grabs at her neck, from her perspective she is removing a scarf she has around her neck.

“It hot? Are you?” Agatha asks, as she pants, seemingly trying to claw at herself, clearly trying to get free.

“Yes, claw your way out,” Rio says, and she watches Agatha continue to claw at her skin, pulling off her clothes, trying to break through the spell she is under.

“I’m feeling,” Agatha says, and she moves her hands in a way which Rio knows is her trying to use her magic.

“Good,” Rio says.

“What?” Agatha asks.

“There are two Jane Does in this case, and you know her name. so, what’s yours?” Rio asks, and with her question, thanks to everything Rio and Nicky have already done, Agatha is able break through the last of the spell, clawing her way out, and resulting her collapsing so that her true self can finally come to the surface once more.

While sitting in a closet isn’t the most comfortable position Nicky stays where his mama put him, even though he could use magic to break free, as he knows that he needs to wait for his mama to ‘wake up’ again.

Being able to tell that his mom has once again left the house Nicky just continues to wait, and honestly, he isn’t sure how long has passed when he hears his mama scream and then a sound which tells him the front door has been opened.

Listening intensely to what is going on Nicky hears, a couple of minutes later, what he assumes his mama come back inside and run down to the basement. As soon as he hears his mama go down to the basement Nicky starts to make noises, in an attempt to remind his mama that he is there, as one thing that was never completely clear was just how much she would remember when they broke the spell. About a minute after Nicky started to make noise the door to the closet he is opens and Nicky sees his Mama, wearing only a robe and holding a wooden spoon like a weapon.

“So that arrest was maybe more of a kidnapping,” Agatha says as she sees him, clearly surprised. “But if you’re real, and not a figment of my imprisoned mind, then that means…” Agatha says, but before she can even get the question out the front door is blown to pieces, Agatha is sent flying across the room, and Nicky sees his mother fully dressed in what he knows to be one of ‘her job’ outfits, but with her face appearing ‘normal’ and not what she has never let Nicky see, as even when he died she took him to the vail as Rio.

“Bit dramatic there, mom,” Nicky thinks to himself, though he isn’t overly surprised, as he watches his mother use a wall to catapult herself across the room and push his mama against the wall, putting a knife to her throat. “I really shouldn’t be watching this,” Nicky thinks to himself, feeling torn between feeling disturbed and like he is intruding on a moment.

“I’ve missed you,” Rio says to Agatha, with a chuckle.

“I hate you,” Agatha responds, and Nicky desperately hopes that’s not true as he wants his moms to be together again as he knows how much his mom still loves his mama.

“How long has it been, Agatha?” Rio asks, not knowing that she has been close to ‘Agatha’ for three years because of the Sigil she cast.

“Not sure,” Agatha responds.

“Since you acquired the Darkhold, you hid behind all that dark magic, but then you lost it, and now..” Rio says, clearly hurt, as she brings the knife closer to Agatha’s chest, cutting her. “Touch,” Rio says cutting Agatha’s chest.

From where he is watching what is going on between his moms Nicky seriously considers breaking the Sigil, putting an end to their fight, but he reluctantly decides to hold off for a little while as he knows his mom would be unimpressed if he broke the Sigil so soon, and he also remembers that his mother warned him that his moms fighting is how they say hello. So, he decides that he will only break the Sigil and intervene if it seems like one of his moms is actually going to seriously hurt the other.

“You’re vulnerable,” Rio says to Agatha, and Nicky knows that is why the version of his mother who knows everything that is going on is so worried.

“Only physically,” Agatha says, and she grabs Rio and slams her head against the wall.

Once Agatha slams Rio’s head against the wall the two of them continue to fight, lodging Rio’s knife in the wall, and Rio puts her hands around Agatha’s throat before kicking her across the room. After Agatha is kicked across the room Rio grabs her knife out of the wall and throws it at Agatha who uses a baking tray to block it.

As the knife slides across the room both Rio and Agatha rush for it, getting to it the same time, and Nicky hears his mama wince in pain.

“Do you remember pain?” Rio asks as both Agatha and Rio continue to hold onto the knife, Rio holding the hilt while Agatha holds the blade, cutting her hand. “It kind of tickles, doesn’t it?” Rio asks, as they both laugh and after a few seconds Rio slices Agatha with the knife while Agatha hits Rio, causing her to be thrown backwards slightly.

“Coochie, coochie coo,” Agatha says moving towards Rio and once again Agatha and Rio fight, Rio slicing her knife through the air, and after a few moments Rio is on her back, with Agatha on top of her, using one hand to hold down the arm that Rio has he knife in while her other hand is around Rio’s neck.

“You can’t kill me,” Rio reminds Agatha, and Nicky who very much wishes he wasn’t witnessing this, knows how true that is.

“You can’t kill me, it’s not allowed,” Agatha responds, and once she does Rio, in a single move, headbutts Agatha which causes her to both get to her feet and be pushed backwards, and while Agatha is getting her baring’s Rio uses her magic to get back on her feet, and then also uses the same magic to send Agatha flying across the room, causing her to crash a cabinet and crumple to the ground.

“Maybe I can’t kil you, but I can make you wish you were dead,” Rio says, as she picks up her knife, and Nicky is just about to break the Sigil and intervene when his mama starts to speak before he can.

“Wait, wait, wait,” Agatha says, and Nicky is thrilled when he realises his mom is actually listening. “This isn’t what you want, me without power,” Agatha says as she gets to her knees. “This is undignified,” Agatha says. “Don’t you want me at my best?” Agatha asks getting to her feet. “Admit it, you prefer me…” Agatha starts to say in a seductive tone of voice.

“Horizontal?” Rio asks, completely disturbing Nicky, who is planning on making it clear to both his mothers just how much they disturbed him, once they know who he is. “In a grave?”

“Formidable,” Agatha corrects.

“So, take my power,” Rio suggests, even though everyone currently present at Agatha’s house knows that is not possible, and knows exactly why.

“That’s cute,” Agatha says with a smile. “But you know that would kill me,” Agatha says. “Just let me get my purple back, and then come find me,” Agatha says.

“I’m not the only one wants to see you dead,” Rio says, and while Nicky is surprised to hear his mom say that he notices her body language and he realises that this is Rio’s way of warning Agatha about who is coming after her, which is actually pretty smart. “Wants to see you burn. Or hang, or drown,” Rio says.

“There are no new options?” Agatha asks, and Nicky suspects that the words are actually getting to his Mama.

“I could just sit back and watch,” Rio says, and Nicky doubts that is true, while in a place deep down inside where Agatha would never admit too, she also wants to doubt it’s true.

“Come on, you love it,” Agatha says as she walks towards Rio, lowering her voice. “The Anticipation,” Agatha says once she is less than a step away from Rio.

“Okay Agatha,” Rio says, putting her knife away in it’s sheath. “But I’ll be sure to tell them were to find you,” Rio says, reaching out and touching Agatha’s face, while Nicky knows that is not needed as only a few days ago Rio discovered that The Salem Seven were close to finding out where he and his mom were.

“Who specifically?” Agatha asks, trying to make It seem like she isn’t at all phased.

“Mmm! The worst of them. The Salem Seven,” Rio answers. “I expected you’ll see them at sundown,” Rio says, as she looks down at Agatha’s bleeding hand. “After all these centuries, Agatha Harkness will finally meet her end,” Rio says as she lifts Agatha’s hand a little. “Ugh! It really warms the heart,” Rio says.

“You don’t have a heart,” Agatha snaps, as Rio moves closer into her personal space.

“Yes, I do, it’s black and it beats for you,” Rio says before bringing Agatha’s hand to her mouth and once it is close enough, she licks the hand, using her healing abilities to heal the cut.

Once Rio heals the wound she walks away from Agatha and because Nicky can see his Mama’s face, he can see the effects that action had on his mama, which tells him that despite what she may say still has feeling for Rio.

“Te Veo,” Rio says before leaving, leaving Agatha flustered by everything and Nicky feeling both incredibly interested, and incredibly disturbed, by everything he just witnessed.

Chapter 17

For the few minutes that follow Rio leaving the house Agatha walks around, getting dressed and ranting, mainly about Rio, while Nicky makes his way out of the closet, knowing that, especially with the Salem Seven coming, he needs to talk to his mama about the road.

“The house is yours, random boy,” Agatha says, and because his mama doesn’t know who he is Nicky doesn’t take that personally. “Be sure to tell the vengeance-seekers I said hi,” Agatha says, and Nicky makes it seem like he is using the wall, but he actually uses his magic, to half pull the tape off his face, Nicky having learnt a long time ago how to subtly use his magic so he doesn’t get caught, and it isn’t until after he does it that he realises that it might not be the smartest thing to do around his mama, but to his relief it doesn’t seem like she realised what he did.

“Take me to the Witches Road!” Nicky exclaims, knowing that it is what they both need.

“Come again?” Agatha asks, turning to look at him.

“The Witches Road, I want you to take me there,” Nicky says as his mama walks over to him. “Please,” Nicky adds.

“The Witches’ Road doesn’t exist,” Agatha tells Nicky, who has to resist the urge to roll his eyes, as he knows his mama is lying.

“You’re lying,” Nicky responds.

“Am I?” Agatha asks, giving her son a challenging look.

“That’s just what real witches say to keep the amateurs out,” Nicky says. “The Road will give you the thing you want the most if you make it to the end, and I can, I will,” Nicky says, knowing that because he is the son of death herself and one of the most powerful witches in the universe, as well everything he has been through, including dying, there is nothing that can stop him from getting what he wants from the Road which for him is for his family to be back together.

“Hmm,” Agatha says and for a moment she looks like she is considering what Nicky is saying. “The road is no place for a kid,” Agatha says, heading towards the living room.

“I’m sixteen,” Nicky corrects, not overly surprised that Agatha is objecting to him going on the road because of his age because his mom warned that that may be the case, which means he has already thought of a possible way around that.

“Oh, sorry, Teen,” Agatha corrects, and Nicky follows behind her.

“I don’t know where you heard about the Road….” Agatha starts to say.

“Books, the ballad, legend, lore,” Nicky says before adding in his head. “My favourite bedtime story,”.

“But it will kill you,” Agatha tells Nicky, who has faith that it won’t because he knows he knows he can’t do that to his mothers.

“It didn’t kill you,” Nicky reminds his mother.

“Well, I’m exceptional,” Agatha says, as she puts a black hat on.

“That’s my point,” Nicky admits. “Look, cards on the table, I know an embarrassing amount about you,” Nicky tells his mother, only stretching the truth a little as he isn’t embarrassed about how much he knows about his mama because he always wants to know more. “I’ve been obsessed since I first heard about your Salem days, one of my favourite you eras,” Nicky says, once again fudging the truth a little, but also considering his mother’s Salem eras to be one of his favourite times to hear stories about because it’s when mothers met so he has always wanted to know more about that time in his mothers lives.

“That’s a good one,” Agatha says, trying not to think about Rio.

“That’s why I came here last night, why I saved you from the spell you were under,” Nicky says, trying to get his mama to be interested in him, without knowing who he is, so that he can get her to agree to go down the road, and, to his relief, his mama looks very interested at that. “No, it was my pleasure,” Nicky says as Agatha sits down Nicky feeling that after three years of trying, he is beyond thrilled that it worked.

“Hmm, well... if you’ve got the goods to break the spell cast by the Scarlet Witch, why do you need the Road?” Agatha asks, gesturing to the couch for Nicky to sit down, which does, choosing his next words carefully because otherwise he risks, even with the Sigil in place, his mom realising who he is before agreeing to go down The Road.

“I mean, I’ve studied, don’t get me wrong, but that can only take you so far,” Nicky comments, knowing that how much studying he has done when it comes to magic is actually part of the reason why he is as powerful as he is. “I wanna blast, to shield, to levitate,” Nicky says, listing things he can already do because when his mother doesn’t know who he is, making it seem like they are both interested in power, is the best way to get her to agree to go down the Road.

“So, you want a shortcut?” Agatha asks, clearly disapproving, which doesn’t surprise Nicky as he has heard his mom tell him, more than once, how much his mama values research and knowledge.

“The road promises that what’s missing awaits you at its end. Power is what I’m missing,” Nicky says to his mother, feeling bad about lying, but knowing it’s the best way to get her to agree to go down the road. “Sounds like it’s what you’re missing, too,” Nicky says, and for a moment it looks like he has convinced his mother, but she quickly changes her mind. .

“Nope. Too risky. No time,” Agatha says, standing up and heading to the door, so Nicky decides to follow her and try another tactic.

“If you wanna run, fine, but these people who are coming tonight sound serious,” Nicky says, knowing that is the most he can say about the Salem Seven without revealing that he knows exactly who they are, and exactly how dangerous they are. “You really think you can outrun them with no magic at all?” Nicky asks, trying to remind his mother just how dire the situation is, as he notices his mother pick up the locket that he knows has his hair within.

“Who are you?” Agatha asks, and Nicky resists the urge to smirk, as this is exactly what he was hoping would happen.

“Nicky Vidal-Harkness,” Nicky says, and just like he was expecting the Sigil kicks in, and his mother doesn’t actually hear the words he says.

“Say again,” Agatha requests, walking towards Nicky, putting her locket into her bra, looking at him with a look of fascination on her face.

“I’m your son, Nicky,” Nicky says, and once again the words are distorted so that Agatha cannot hear what he says.

“Interesting,” Agatha comments, looking at him closely, and from the look on his mothers’ face Nicky can’t help but wonder just what she is actually seeing, can’t help but wonder if she suspects who he is yet.

“What?” Nicky asks, hoping that his mom was right and that the Sigil being triggered is enough to make her interested.

“I’m driving,” Agatha tells Nicky.

“What? Really? Yes!” Nicky says, feeling thrilled that worked and realising, even after so long, just how well his mom knows his mama.

Over the next minute Agatha goes into the other room where she has what Nicky knows to be what, while under the spell, she imagined to be the car. After realising her mistake Agatha makes it seem like she was actually collecting a pair of scissors which she drops at Nicky’s feet before leaving.

Even though he knows it is risky, rather than using the scissors, as soon as his mother leaves the house Nicky uses his magic to break the ropes that are binding his hands and feet before chasing after his mama.

After leaving his mama’s house Nicky sees his mother a little way down the street, actually not to far from his house, and so he hurries to catch up with her.

“Agatha! Agatha!” Nicky says, as he chases after her, really hating that he can’t call her mama, something he has been wanting to do for three years.

“What do you know about covens?” Agatha asks once Nicky catches up with her.

“Just that they are drawn together by mysterious forces of fate,” Nicky says, remembering what he read in his mamas old spellbook. “And that they are the truest form of sisterhood,” Nicky remembers. “Wait, do you have a coven?” Nicky asks, as he didn’t think so, but he also knows that because his mama and mom were apart for so long there could be things that he doesn’t know because Rio didn’t know to tell him.

“No, not for a very long time,” Agatha says, confirming what Nicky thought. “But we do need a coven to access The Road,” Nicky says.

“Oh yeah, right, that makes sense,” Nicky says, not believing that he forgot that, and now he can’t help but wonder how he is going to make it so Rio is apart of the coven when, considering the fight they had, he can’t see his mama being fond of that idea and he is meant to have no idea who she is.

For a moment his mother is silent as Nicky realises, she is staring at the plot where Wanda’s house once stood, something which tells Nicky she is still affected by what happened even if she is trying to hide it, something which doesn’t surprise him when he has felt what the spell feels like.

“Um, I’m over here,” Nicky says, pointing to where his car is, feeling glad that he gave enough forethought to move the car out of the driveway as that would lead to awkward questions.

“Oh, are you?” Agatha asks, an edge to her voice, as Nicky leads Agatha over the car, quickly running through his head whether there is anything in the car that could hint towards who he is.

A little while after they left Agatha’s house Nicky and Agatha are in Nicky’s car, which is technically Rio’s driving out of Westview. As they drive Nicky notices his mama is rather quiet as she looks out the window, and it takes pretty much everything he has not to talk to her, not to get to know the real her better, as that is all he has wanted for so long.

“Am I even going in the right direction…” Nicky starts to ask, doing so because he doesn’t want to sit in silent with his mama anymore.

“Be cool, man,” Agatha says, and soon after she does Nicky’s phone starts to ring, and he sees Eddie on the screen with his boyfriend caller ID.

“Sorry, he worries,” Nicky says, rejecting the call, knowing that that isn’t exactly how he wanted to tell his Mama that has a boyfriend, but now he has no choice.

“Aw!” Agatha exclaims in an overdramatic tone of voice.

“So, where do we just find a coven?” Nicky asks curious, as in all their planning his mom never made that clear.

“Wherever you are, a coven there shall be,” Agatha quotes.

“That’s beautiful,” Nicky says amazed, feeling that he is finally getting what he has wanted for a very long time, a witchcraft lesson from his mama.

“No, it’s definitely not,” Agatha says annoyed. “But it is the Covenstead rule,” Agatha explains. “Within any three-mile radius, there will be a collection of witchy-enough people to form a coven,” Agatha reveals, and Nicky finds that fascinating.

“Can you actually jot that down for me?” Nicky asks curious as he pulls a small spellbook out of his pocket, a book his mother originally obtained for his mama but which she gave to him. “There’s a pen in the glove compartment,” Nicky explains to his mother.

“Oh, okay, of course,” Agatha says, and she opens the glove compartment, pulls out the pen, which she then throws out of the window. “Do you want me to take that?” Agatha asks, referring to the spell book Nicky is holding.

“No, it’s…. I’ll remember it,” Nicky says, as he really doesn’t want his mother to throw his spell book out of the window too, but what he does want is to know more, so he decides to keep asking questions. “So, with a Covenstead, it’s unlikely we’ll find witches as high-profile as you,” Nicky says to his mother, through from what he knows he is pretty sure that there are very few, if no, witches who are as high profile as his mama.

“Yeah, there’s no such thing, Teen,” Agatha says, and Nicky is a little amused at what she has decided to call him because she can’t call him by his name. “But all we need is a bit of talent, even the most down and out witches when in close proximity with each other, bring out a magical spark,” Agatha explains, and once she does Nicky has to look away from his mother a this is the exact kind of thing, he has wanted his mama to teach him since his mother brought him back from the other side of the veil.

A little while after Nicky and Agatha talked about members of a coven bringing out power in each other the two of them are walking into a psychic’s store, the first location Agatha wants to check for an actual witch.

“Welcome to the curious,” An older woman greats Nicky and Agatha as they walk in, though considering how old Nicky knows his mother to be, he isn’t actually sure that she would be older than his mama even if their looks suggest otherwise.

“Good day Madam,” Agatha says, putting an over the top southern accent. “Oh, thank you so much for seein’ us. We are hopin for a miracle today,” Agatha says, continuing with the accent. “This is my boy, Beauford,” Agatha says and even though he knows that Agatha doesn’t know the significance it means everything to Nicky to hear her say that, and before he can say anything Agatha covers his mouth. “He doesn’t talk much. He’s got social anxiety,” Agatha says. “His Daddy recently passed, and we miss him somthin’ awful, and we surely would love to commune with him today,” Agatha says, and Nicky has to silently compliment his mother on her ability to pull a believable story out of nowhere. “But to be quite frank with you, what is top of mind is the location of some gold bars he may not have buried in our backyard,” Agatha explains.

“Please,” the woman, Lilia says, gesturing to the table, and both Nicky and Agatha sit down.

“Thank you. You’re a doll,” Agatha says, and both she and Nicky sit down.

“How, will you be paying?” Lilia asks.

“Oh, he’s got it,” Agatha says, looking at Nicky.

“Debit works,” Lilia says, and Nicky pulls a card he has to pay, purposely making sure Agatha doesn’t see the name of the card as he isn’t sure that the sigil will block that.

“He always takes care of mama,” Agatha says.

“Try to anyway,” Nicky thinks to himself, as that is the very thing he has been trying to do for the past three years.

“Your husband was a proud man,” Lilia says, and Nicky can admit that that does describe Rio, but he also has some doubts about what Lilia is going to do.

“Indeed, he was,” Agatha confirms, clearly playing into what Lilia is ‘seeing’.

“Did he golf?” Lilia asks and Agatha gives an over-the-top gasp. “He died on the eighteenth hole,” Agatha lies. “Oh, she’s good,” Agatha says, glancing at Nicky. “Now the location of the gold bars?” Agatha asks, and once she does Lilia makes over the top sounds which results in both Agatha and Nicky needing to resist the urge to laugh. “Brother,” Agatha mutters, and Nicky feels the urge to laugh get stronger.

“You’ll find the gold bars in an old bowling bag at the back of his closet,” Lilia lies.

“Yes, that’s it!” Agatha says, clearly becoming uninterested with Lilia. “Thank you, thank the lady would you Beauford,” Agatha says, standing up and turning away from Lilia.

“There’s something else,” Lilia says, and Agatha turns back around to look at her.

“What is it?” Agatha asks, giving her a challenging look.

“You’ve been under the influence of another, someone you hurt,” Lilia says, and both Nicky and Agatha know exactly what that means. “They took your agency, for three years,” Lilia says, impressing both mother and son who realise she may just be legitimate. “It’s not the first time your witch kin betrayed you,” Lilia says, and even though his mom didn’t tell him much Nicky suspects Lilia is talking about what whatever it is that happened between his mama, Evanora and her original coven. “But you survive, in a way few do. In fact, that’s why you’re here,” Lilia says, saying enough to impress Agatha, as she stands up. “And I’m not interested,” Lilia says.

“Seriously?” Nicky asks surprised.

“Thank you for your purchase. Your bank statement will say Lilia’s Leggings, but that’s just my side Hussle,” Lila says before heading into the back room and as his mother follows her Nicky does too, hoping Agatha has a better idea than him about how to get Lilia to join them.

“Lilia, you haven’t even heard the pitch,” Agatha says as she and Nicky follow Lilia into the backroom.

“I don’t need to,” Lilia says with a laugh. “What witch in her right mind would join Agatha Harkness’ coven?” Lilia asks, and Nicky feels a rush of protectiveness towards his mama, but before he can say anything Agatha is speaking again.

“Not looking for right-minded witches, as it happens,” Agatha says, and Nicky realises that either Lilia’s words don’t get to his mama or she is trying to hide the fact that they did, and suddenly Lilia screams.

“Are you all right, ma’am?” Nicky asks concerned.

“So, you’re a big of a kook. Every witch has their process,” Agatha notes. “You showed some real skill out there,” Agatha says as she sits down at the table.

“I didn’t read your fortune, I read your reputation,” Lilia informs Agatha. “Witches like you are the reason people think we poison apples and steal children, and eat babies,” Lilia says, and once she does Nicky sees his mama’s entire body language change, which tells him that he is about to see what his mom warned him about, his Mama putting on a persona to protect herself.

“Babies are delicious,” Agatha responds, proving what Nicky was suspecting. “How old are you? 410? 415?” Agatha asks.

“How dare you!” Lilia objects.

“Oh, I apologize, you don’t look a day under four hundred and fifty,” Agatha comments.

“Years old?” Nicky asks, not overly surprised by that because his mom is literally as old as the universe and his mother is over three hundred and fifty years old, but it is still a little surprising to know there are other witches older than his mama.

“You get what, maybe two suckers a day in here, and twenty bucks later, you’re sitting on a bad that’s also your wall,” Agatha says, pointing out the murphy bed that is in the corner. “Don’t you miss the glory days?” Agatha asks.

“When I was chased out of every village I passed through for accurately predicting tragedy?” Lilia asks, and while he doesn’t remember a lot about the world before he died Nicky can remember that, he remembers that he, his mama and mom had to move a lot to stay safe, he also remembers when they were ran out of a village. “No, I don’t. Beat it Harkness,” Lilia says, clearly not wanting to listen to her.

“I’m gonna walk The Road,” Agatha says, clearly trying to get her interested and Nicky is a little amused that his Mama is using the same technique he used to get his Mama interested.

“The Road is a death wish,” Lilia points out.

“I survived,” Agatha says, knowing the road once gave her what she wanted most, the ability to have children with Rio, and that she is hoping it will be able to give back to her what she has lost.

“Yeah? Where’s your power now?” Lilia asks.

“Time to restock,” Agatha responds, like it’s not a big deal. “I need a Divination witch,” Agatha says.

“Are you honestly asking me to coven up with the single most infamous witch on this continent?” Lilia asks.

“Oh please. Name a badded bitch in South America, or Europe,” Nicky says, feeling the need to defend his mother as he is pretty sure she is the most infamous witch in the world, not just the continent.

“Who is this child?” Lilia asks.

“I’m…” Nicky starts to say, but before he can say anything Agatha cuts him off.

“My pet,” Agatha finishes, trying to keep the sigil from being activated in front of someone she doesn’t know as she still isn’t sure what it means just yet. “This is my pet. Say hi, pet,” Agatha says.

“Hi,” Nicky says, resisting the urge to roll his eyes.

“You expect me to risk my life, on the Witches’ Road, and if we’re successful…” Lilia starts to say.

“When,” Nicky corrects, having complete faith that they are going to succeed.

“If we’re successful, watch you turn around and steal my power?” Lilia asks, and Nicky tenses at that, as he knows enough about that particular ability of his mamas to know it’s a sensitive topic.

Hearing the question Agatha clears her throat and moves closer to Lilia, clearly about to share something she doesn’t want anyone else, including Nicky, to know, but thanks to what his mother told him Nicky suspects he knows exactly what Agatha is going to say.

“Excuse me. “What is happening?” Nicky asks, feeling amazed when he realises what his mother is doing, having a suspicion about what is going on, but wanting to check to be sure.

“Witchcraft,” Agatha confirms with a smirk.

“Three of pentacles,” Lilia says before handing Agatha back the eviction notices with names written on it. “There, a list of four names. Looks like you’ve got your coven. Leave me out of it,” Lilia requests, and as Agatha reads it, she realises something.

“Be there five pm, plenty of street parking,” Agatha says, as she and Nicky head outside.

“What?” Agatha asks, turning to look at him.

What are they like?” Alice asks, as everyone turns to Agatha, even Nicky, wanting to know what she is going to say about that as Nicky has only knows the little that his mom told him, and he is sure there is more to what the trials entail than what she told him, he has no doubt that she tried to protect him from the truth.

“The Road will test us and our knowledge of the craft,” Agatha explains. “One trial for each skill,” Agatha explains.

“How do we pass them without any power?” Jen asks annoyed.

“Well, there’s always analogue magic,” Nicky says, remembering what he read in the book his mother wrote. “You know, labour-intensive manual acts of magic,” Nicky says, thinking of lessons his mom gave him. “Witchcraft, emphasis on the craft,” Nicky says, like it should be obvious.

“Again, who are you?” Jen asks annoyed.

“Nicky Vidal-Harkness,” Nicky answers, triggering the Sigil as Jen is annoying him, and because of that no one heard him say his name.

“Well, I’ll be someone’s put a Sigil on that boy,” Lilia says amazed, and being able to tell even though she can’t tell who exactly cast the Sigil that whoever did was incredibly powerful.

“A what?” Nicky asks, pretending to be confused, as he figures it is his best move, but he quickly realises that may have been a mistaken when he sees the suspicious look on his mama’s face as from her perspective Nicky has demonstrated a high level of understanding when it comes to Magic so she would expect him to know what a Sigil is.

“Don’t look at me,” Agatha says with a scoff when everyone turns to look at her. “I didn’t put that clumsy glamour on him,” Agatha reveals. “Sigil’s are beneath me,” Agatha says and Nicky is a little amused by that, but doesn’t let it show.

“A sigil is a spell?” Nicky asks, playing into his fake confusion as now that he choose to go down that path he has to keep it up.

“A Sigil is a redaction spell that hides something,” Alice says. “In this case, you from witchfoke,” Alice comments.

“No just witchfoke,” Nicky thinks to himself as he knows the Sigil also works, thanks to the fact that his mother cast it, other powerful being as well as it appears, Sharon, but that could be because she is currently around so many witches, or because she is on the Road, Nicky isn’t exactly sure.

“Looks like Agatha brought a sparkly little mystery with her,” Jen comments, clearly giving Agatha a suspicious look.

“She was probably trying to keep him all to herself,” Lilia comments.

“That is a little insulting, I am a person you know,” Nicky says, showing a little more of the sass he inherited from Rio than he intended, but to his relief his mama doesn’t seem to have picked up on the similarities between him and his mom.

“Look,” Agatha says, taking a step forward and pushing Nicky back, protecting him, even without knowing who he is.

“I have no idea what’s under that Sigil,” Agatha says, and while that is not strictly true as she has her suspicions, suspicions she can’t bring herself to hope she is right, at least not yet, so there is no way she is going to share those suspicions. “He could be something special,” Agatha says, and while everything she has seen, everything she has heard him say, indicates he is, she isn’t planning on sharing that with the rest of the coven. “Or he could be a pest that a cranky witch stashed under a rock, we can crack him open later,” Agatha says, hiding the fact that she is going to figure out who exactly Nicky is, hopefully sooner than later. “The real value lies at the end of the Road,” Agatha says, wanting to get the others attention of Nicky as she is feeling a need to protect him, even if she cannot admit that. “So, if you want to unbind,” Agatha says to Jen. “And you want to reverse your fortune,” Agatha says to Lilia. “And you want to find out what happened to mommy,” Agatha says to Alice. “And you…” Agatha starts to say to Sharon, but she is gone.

“Wait, where is Mrs D…Hart?” Nicky asks, being close to calling her Mrs Davies as that is what he has known her as for the past three years, but he quickly realises that’s not something he is supposed to know.

“I mean you take your eyes off her for two seconds…” Agatha says annoyed.

For the next couple of minutes everyone searches for Sharon until they finally find her off the road, being sucked into the mud, but with some difficulty the group manages to keep her from being sucked below, to her certain death.

“This is just a really, really horrible party,” Sharon comments, once she has been saved, seemingly no worse for ware even if she is covered in mud.

“Well, I thought that this was pretty obvious, but for the uninitiated, rule number one, do not step off The Road,” Agatha warns.

“Oh, I stray not from the path,” Nicky says, remembering the words of the ballad.

“Yes, thank you Teen,” Agatha says. “So, if we just follow the instructions of the Ballad, we’ll be safe as kittens. Okay?” Agatha asks, looking between the members of the group, and considering what he feels when he is close to Sharon Nicky very much doubts that is going to be the case, but he knows he can’t reveal that, especially because he doesn’t even want to think about it, and the group once again start to walk again.

“Well, I don’t know how you expect me to walk and walk and walk when there is no where to walk to,” Sharon comments.

“Look,” Jen says, and everyone suddenly sees a house a little way away, a house which is clearly where the Road is leading.

“Was that there before?” Alice asks surprised.

“We should stop asking that question,” Agatha advises, as they all walk closer to the house, so that they can have a better look.

“Now this is a house,” Jen says impressed, as it is an incredible looking house that has appeared.

“Right of your vision board,” Agatha says, assuming from Jen’s reaction that this is going to be her trial, but she isn’t going to voice that.

“Maybe this is the end,” Sharon says.

“That would be such a bummer,” Nicky comments, still trying to ignore what he is feeling now that he is right next to Sharon, even though it is getting harder for him to do so, but he knows that as long as he doesn’t touch her, he can continue to believe he is not sensing what he thinks he is sensing. “Sorry,” Nicky adds when he sees the less than impressed looks on everyone’s faces, and together the group continue to walk to the door.

“The phases on the moon,” Lilia notes when she sees what is on the door into the house.

“It’s full, the Water phase,” Nicky says, looking at his mama to see if he is right, and she nods. “So, what do we do?” Nicky asks.

“Well, we don’t wanna surprise anyone,” Sharon says before ringing the doorbell.

“Don’t we?” Agatha asks with an over the top grin and everyone walks into the house, Sharon doing so reluctantly.

The second the group walk into the house everything changes, and not only do they find themselves in an incredible beach house all of their clothing, and hairstyles, have changed to fit the aesthetics of what seems like rich people at a Hamptons weekend.

“It’s not exactly the stuff of nightmares,” Jen says, as she looks around the house.

“The road changes for the coven,” Agatha explains.

“It changes us, too,” Lilia says, realising that they have all been changed to fit the aesthetics.

“My amulets!” Alice exclaims, and Nicky notices his mama touch her locket, in a way which tells him she is reassuring herself that it is there, something which doesn’t surprise Nicky when he knows the significance.

“You still got em,” Lilia assures Alice, trying to be reassuring.

“It’s giving ‘middle-aged second chance at love’ vibes and I’m here for it,” Nicky comments, walking forward as he has a bit of a look around, there being apart of him that’s trying to get away from Sharon and what he is feeling.

“Definitely a sip-your tea-with-both-hands-kinda place,” Alice notes, as she, along with everyone else, starts to look around, trying to make sense of where they are.

“I look like one of my customers,” Jen comments as she looks in the mirror.

“These don’t open,” Alice says, referring to the doors on the other side of the room.

“Oh my god! Bury me in that kitchen!” Sharon exclaims, and for the next minute or so everyone looks around until Nicky finds a note on the mantal piece.

“What’s this?” Nicky asks, as everyone hurries towards him and his mama takes the note. “A wedding?”

“Please god, not a baby shower,” Agatha requests, as that would hit a little too close to home, and Jen steals the note from her.

“The Witches Road cordially invites you to the first trial,” Jen reads. “It’s a riddle,” she says. “My age has value. I’m no fun alone. I mess with your mind. My tricks are well known,” Jen reads and once she does Sharon takes the note from her.

“That’s a gorgeous card stock,” Sharon reveals. “Double-sided, too,” Sharon says as she closely inspects it.

“What does it mean?” Nicky asks, looking between the others as riddles have never been his strong suite.

“That it’s really expensive,” Sharon explains, even though that is not actually what Nicky is asking.

“My age has value, no fun alone, I mess with your mind, my tricks are well known,” Alice repeats, trying to make sense of what it means.

“Sounds like a witch,” Agatha speculates.

“Sounds like you,” Jen responds and Agatha mimics her, in an over the top sound, which makes Nicky even more curious about the history between his mama and Jen, as there definitely is some kind of history between them, but he knows he can’t ask about that without making Agatha even more suspicious about who he is.

“Wine!” Sharon exclaims as she sees a bottle of wine, with glasses, on a nearby table.

“That’s it! ten points for Mrs Hart,” Alice says.

“Ten points for what now?” Sharon asks as she picks up the wine bottle.

“Wait, we don’t know what’ll happen if we drink it,” Alice warns.

“Sure, we do, something terrible,” Agatha comments, knowing that. “But if we don’t follow these obvious breadcrumbs we can’t move forward and we won’t get to the big prize,” Agatha comments. “So, does anyone have a corkscrew?” Agatha asks.

“There’s a built-in bar,” Nicky says, knowing that because he noticed that earlier, and he hurries over to it.

“And I will help you,” Jen says, as she follows Nicky to the bar. “Hey, bit of advice,” Jen says as she gets to the bar, while Nicky searches.

“Yeah?” Nicky asks.

“Watch your back with Agatha,” Jen reveals, and while Nicky is able to roll his eyes, he feels the Sigil pushing back against most of the things he wants to say, but he is able to say;

“I know how people feel about her,” Nicky says, knowing that from not just what his mom has told him but research he was doing when he was trying to figure out how to break Wanda’s spell.

“Do you know she traded her own child for the book of the damned?” Jen asks, like it is a casual fact, and Nicky immediately feels furious, knowing for a fact that it isn’t true as from what his mom has said over the years, he has been able to figure out that his mama obtained the book of the Damned after he died in an attempt to bring him back.

“That’s not true,” Nicky says angrily, feeling his magic bubble below the surface, wanting to come out, feeling glad that the Sigil didn’t keep him from defending his mama.

“Maybe not, but it is what people say,” Jen tells Nicky, not realising just how close she is to being blasted across the room by Nicky’s magic.

“Well, it’s just what people say, then why the hell are you repeating it without knowing the truth?” Nicky asks, and Jen clearly has no idea what to say to that. “Maybe you should think about how you feel when people are talking about your lawsuits without knowing the full story before you spread rumours about things you don’t actually know anything about,” Nicky tells Jen. “Look corkscrew,” Nicky says with an over the top grin, before picking it up and taking it over the others, leaving Jen to wonder why he is defending Agatha so much while Nicky knows that when his mom arrives, and he is sure she will, it may be a good idea to keep her away from Jen.

“Here Agatha,” Nicky says, handing the corkscrew to her, and Agatha gives him a curious look, wondering what just happened between him and Jen as Jen looks like she has been knocked down a few pegs and Nicky isn’t doing a good job at hiding the anger he is feeling.

“Are you okay?” Agatha asks Nicky in a quiet voice, having lot of questions.

“I’m fine,” Nicky responds, and even though Agatha doesn’t believe him it is clear that he doesn’t want to talk about whatever just happened so instead Agatha uses the corkscrew to open the wine and starts to pour it.

“Ohh, healthy pour,” Agatha says as she purposely pours a large amount of the wine into her glass. “If you’re waiting for a charcuterie, I don’t think it’s coming,” Agatha advises, and Sharon drinks her entire glass of wine in one go.

“I have had a very hard day. Do not judge me,” Sharon says, as everyone else is looking at her, and once she does a timer with thirty minutes on it starts to beep, signifying the start of the trial.

“So, to harbingers of doom?” Agatha asks, raising her glass, tyring to seem relaxed.

“To the prize,” Lilia says, as everyone toasts, Nicky doing so without a glass.

“Here we go,” Agatha says, actually sounding nervous.

“Can I have some?” Nicky asks, as he notices that no glass has been poured for him, and it would be far from the first time he has had alcohol.

“You bet,” Agatha says, not seeing the big deal, but everyone else objects, making it perfectly clear that he isn’t going to get any of the wine.

“Should we take the girl talk to the sofa?” Sharon, who now has a second glass of the wine says, and everyone heads over to the living area, all feel apprehensive about what is going to come, while Nicky has a feeling, that he knows at least one thing that is a certainty to happen.

Chapter 20

Chapter 20

AN: Thank you so much for the support. I am extremely nervous for you to read the end of this chapter, so hope you like what I’ve decided to do. Next chapter will be up in about twelve hours.

As everyone heads over to the couches Nicky purposely sits down next to Alice for several reasons, one, he doesn’t want to deal with Jen anymore. Two, he doesn’t want to feel what he is feeling when he is in close proximity with Sharon as he knows what it means, even though he is still trying to ignore it. And the third reason is that ever instinct of his is telling him to run to his Mama, who is inspecting the windows, hug her and ask her why she lets people believe the worst in her, but as he cannot do that he sits next to Alice, figuring she is the ‘safe option,’, even though he is seriously tempted to break the Sigil so he can truly give Jen a piece of his mind and assure his mama that he doesn’t think she is the monster she clearly wants people to believe she is.

“Hey,” Nicky says to Alice, figuring that he might as well make an effort if he is going to sit with her.

“Hey,” Alice responds.

“I really like your tattoo. Where’d you get it?” Nicky asks, trying to make an effort.

“Nowhere,” Alice snaps, clearly not wanting to talk about it.

“Okay,” Nicky says, understanding her desire, and he glances over to his mama who is still inspecting the glass doors, and not long after he turns away she pours out her glass of wine.

“Got it in Colorado,” Alice says, feeling bad about snapping at Nicky. “My mom was playing Red Rocks,” Alice explains.

“That symbols wards off curses, right?” Nicky asks, as he remembers seeing it before, probably in one of his moms.

“She uh, made me get it,” Alice reveals. “Cause she said all the woman in our family were cursed… she wasn’t well,” Alice explains, trying to explain her mothers behaviour even though she doesn’t completely understand it.

“How old were you?” Nicky asks curious.

“Thirteen maybe,” Alice answers.

“A lot happened to me at thirteen too,” Nicky says, as that’s when he found his mama again, and she had no idea who he was.

“I miss your eyeliner, but the hair is cute,” Alice says, and at her kindness Nicky feels some of the anger he is feeling towards Jen slip away.

“Okay, so a witch is really just another name for a bad guy,” Sharon says as Agatha lies on the back of the couch behind her.  “Is that right?” Sharon asks.

“That is extremely reductive,” Lilia says annoyed. “We are not a monolith. And, you know, I blame Halloween,” Lilia says irritated, and considering he has seen how his mother, actual death, reacts to Halloween Nicky isn’t surprised about how Lilia’s feels. “Do you see any pointy hats in here?” Lilia asks and a few people around the room chuckle. “Any green skin? Any brooms? No sir,” Lila says.

“Well, I’m not saying that I wanna join the club or anything, but I would drink the blood of a virgin if it would smooth out some of these wrinkles,” Sharon says as she stands up and as the others notice her face Alice gasps.

“Oh my god,” Alice says.

“Oh, you are so sweet,” Sharon says, not realising the real reason why Alice just gasped. “I don’t really think I need it, either,” Sharon admits.

“Okay, so, Mrs Hart,” Alice says in a gentle voice as she stand sup.

“Sharon,” Sharon corrects.

“Sharon, you’re a little swollen,” Alice says gently.

“Is it bad?” Sharon asks worried.

“I think she looks fantastic,” Agatha comments.

“We’ve been poisoned,” Jen realises, also standing up.

“What?” Lilia asks surprised.

“I need a mirror,” Jen says, as everyone starts to freak out, and searches the room they are in for ways to see how bad the poison is affecting each of those who have drunk it.

“Does my face look that bad?” Alice asks worried.

“Let me see,” Lilia request.

“Oh, my god, I have jowls!” Alice exclaims.

“My face!” Jen gasps. “My formally perfect face!” Jen exclaims.

“Honestly, I don’t hate it,” Lilia admits, using a tray to see her reaction.
