“He can sense when a lot of people died in the same place, that’s what he felt when we went to the clearing,” Rio explains. “But he has another ability related to death,” Rio reveals, and Agatha gives her an interested look. “If he is in close proximity with someone and they are certainly going to die soon, it’s not clear exactly how soon, with no chance of survival, he can feel it. Usually, it requires him to touch a person, but being in close proximity can sometimes be enough,” Rio explains, feeling that it is important Agatha knows that because of how the Road can be, and as she does Agatha comes to a horrifying realization.

“Oh god,” Agatha says, as pieces fall into place.

“Agatha?” Rio asks concerned, knowing that it is bad that Nicky experiences that, but not completely understanding  Agatha’s reaction.

“Mrs. Hart, the person who was on The Road before we called you, she died in the first task,” Agatha reveals, saying what Rio already knew. “I checked her body after the task, I saw sighs of magic… and Nicky was with her when she died,” Agatha tells Rio, who closes her eyes, as she realizes the same thing as Agatha. “Do you think he….” Agatha starts to ask, having no idea how to ask what she is thinking, but feeling that because Rio spent more time with their son than her, she would know if what she suspects is something he’s likely going to do.

“I think if Nicky knew she was going to die, that there was nothing that could change that, and she was in pain, then yes, he would help her find some peace,” Rio says, having no doubt that Nicky would have had no malice intentions, that he would have seen it as helping her, and as she speaks she and Agatha see Nicky get up, walk away from the others, and sit down on his own, leaning against a large tree stump. “You should talk to him,” Rio says, knowing Nicky well enough to know that he would be struggling with whatever happened and that this is the exact kind of thing Agatha would understand more than anyone else, including her.

“He doesn’t know me,” Agatha says, sadly. “You should talk to him,” Agatha says, wanting what is best for her son, and because of that she can admit that maybe what’s best for her son at the moment, isn’t her.

“Agatha, of course he knows you,” Rio assures her.

“Knowing Agnes doesn’t count,” Agatha responds.

“I don’t mean Agnes,” Rio says “We talked about you every day. On every birthday Nicky wished to be with you, there was nothing he wanted more,” Rio assures her love. “I gave him the spell book you wrote, the one you gave to me for safe keeping, and long after I know he memorized every word of it I would still find that he fell asleep reading it because it made him feel connected to you,” Rio assures Agatha. “All he’s wanted since coming back is to spend time with you, he loves you, he is so much like you; you should talk to him,” Rio says, and Agatha isn’t sure if Nicky being like her, is a good thing. “Go, talk to him,” Rio encourages, as while she would like to talk to Nicky too, she knows that what both Nicky and Agatha need is to talk to each other.

“Okay,” Agatha says, as she feels Rio encouragingly squeeze her hand and feeling extremely nervous Agatha gets up and heads towards where her son is.

Chapter 26

Chapter 26

AN: IMPORTANT: I wrote all of this before 1x08 and 1x09. I am still trying to figure out what I felt about the episodes so I would love your opinions. Hope you like how this story is going to playout, I am proud of what I have written if that helps. Next chapter will be in 12ish hours.

With every step Agatha takes towards her son, away from Rio, she finds herself feeling even more nervous, having no idea how this is going to go as she knows she doesn’t want to let him down more than she already has.

“Can I join you?” Agatha asks Nicky, who looks up at her, and is seemingly glad to see her.

“Of course,” Nicky says, without hesitation, as all he wants is to spend time with his mama, and Agatha sits down next to him.

“So, I take it you’re not exactly missing power,” Agatha says, that being the first thing she can think to say, and she really hopes that wasn’t a mistake.

“Not so much,” Nicky says amused. “I didn’t take short cuts Mama, I studied, I did the work,” Nicky assures her, and as she hears Nicky once again call her Mama Agatha knows she is never going to stop being amazed by that. “Mom told me how you would say that knowledge can be more powerful than raw talent, so I’ve always made sure I never stopped learning,” Nicky assures Agatha, who is starting to see what Rio meant by Nicky being like her.

“I’m really glad to hear that,” Agatha says proudly. “Mom said you had the spell book I wrote,” Agatha says to her son.

“Yes! That book is amazing! The way you understand magic, it gave me so much to consider,” Nicky tells his mama, clearly excited to talk about that.

“I’m glad I could help,” Agatha tells her son, while it doesn’t make up for not being able to be with him, she is glad that she was able to give him some lessons, in a sense.

“You did, you really did, Mama,” Nicky tells her. “I know you said I had no reason to feel guilty about not breaking the spell sooner, but I am,” Nicky tells his mama. “I felt the spell. I felt how it strangled you, violated you, how it clawed it’s way into every part of you, and I hate that I wasn’t able to help you sooner, I am sorry Mama,” Nicky says, needing to say that even though she told him not to feel guilty.

“Nicky, it’s okay,” Agatha assures him, though she is trying not to think about what she knows it felt like, and after a moment of hesitation she puts her arm around him. “This wasn’t just any spell, it was cast by the Scarlet Witch, the fact that you managed to figure out how to break it is incredible,” Agatha says, and she knows that some point they will talk a little more about how he did that, but not right now. “It’s complicated magic, you have no reason to feel anything but pride about what you did. I know that’s how I feel,” Agatha assures her son. “I’m so proud of you, Nicky, you have no reason to feel guilty,” Agatha assures her son.

“I love you, Mama,” Nicky tells his mother, not sure if he can believe her words, as he snuggles into her side a little.

“I love you too,” Agatha assures him, as she leans down and kisses the top of his head. “Nicky, were you about to blast me when I was siphoning form Alice?” Agatha asks her son, as she needs to know how close she came to losing him before she even knew he was actually himself.

“Yeah,” Nicky answers. “I know mom told me to never do that, but I wanted to help,” Nicky tells his mama, and Agatha is glad that Rio at least stressed how important it is not to blast her.

“I appreciate that, I do, but Nicholas no matter what you can never blast me with your magic,” Agatha tells him. “Okay, no matter what, you cannot do that,” Agatha says, needing to stress that. “Promise me you won’t ever do that,” Agatha almost begs.

“I promise,” Nicky responds, only doing so because of the tone of voice his mother used, after a moment of hesitation.

“Good,” Agatha says, feeling a little bit better about that, but also knowing they will have to have that conversation again at some point and the two of them drift into silence as they sit together.

As they sit together in comfortable silence both Agatha and Nicky just embrace the feeling of being together again, something they have both wanted for a very long time, as they watch Rio rejoin the others. While she loves just sitting comfortably with her son Agatha knows there is another conversation, even if it is painful, that she needs to have with her son for his own good.

“Nicky, what happened to Sharon?” Agatha asks her son in a gentle voice as she feels him tense, which tells her everything about what they are going to talk about.

“What did Mom tell you?” Nicky asks, assuming that for Agatha to ask the question she knows more than just what she noticed about the body.

“She told me that you can tell when a lot of people have died in the same place, and that you can tell when someone is certainly going to die, when there is nothing that can save them,” Agatha tells her son, who avoids looking at his mama. “Nicky, it’s okay, whatever happened,” Agatha assures her son.

“I had a bad feeling about Sharon coming with us since she came into the basement,” Nicky admits. “At first I thought it was just because she was coming and not mom,” Nicky admits, and Agatha realises that Nicky’s behaviour in relation to who would be the Green Witch on the Road makes more sense. “But then we got into the first trial, and I knew what I was feeling, but I tried to ignore it, until I touched her hand when it tried to stop her drink more wine and I knew for sure,” Nicky explains to his mama. “She was going to die, and nothing could change that,” Nicky admits, sounding upset. “I checked the rest of you and was able to tell that you’d be okay, so I didn’t say anything because I knew we had to focus on completing the trial,” Nicky explains to his mama, still not sure if he made the right decision. “When she came out of the trial, she was alive, but I knew that she was going to die within a few minutes, that nothing could change that, but that she was going to be in a lot of pain for those few minutes,” Nicky explains to his mama. “I did my best to comfort her, and then I used my magic to speed up her fate, to take away her pain,” Nicky explains, tears coming to his eyes. “Are you disappointed in me? Are you ashamed?” Nicky asks his mama, as he never wants that.

“Never,” Agatha assures her son. “Sounds like you were trying to do a noble thing, that you took away her pain,” Agatha tells her son, realising that while he may have done a bad thing, he did it for the right reason. “Nicky, you never have to be worried about telling me something, never have to be worried about my reaction, because I’ve guaranteed I’ve done something worse,” Agatha assures her son. “I’ll never be disappointed in you, I’ll never be ashamed,” Agatha assures her son, knowing that she will never make him feel the way her mother made her feel.

“I’m a little ashamed,” Nicky admits. “I know I helped her, that if I didn’t, she would have had a few minutes of extreme pain, and I took it away, but it still doesn’t feel good,” Nicky admits.

“That’s because you’re a good person,” Agatha tells her son. “You used your magic for a good reason, took away someone’s pain, that’s incredible,” Agatha tells her son, not wanting him to feel shame or guilt about his magic.

“It doesn’t feel rather incredible,” Nicky admits, knowing that what he is mostly feeling at the moment is how he hates both his abilities sometimes.

“I know,” Agatha says as she certainly understands that. “I know it doesn’t help a lot with what happened to Sharon, but Nicky, you also saved Alice; she’s alive because of you,” Agatha tells her son, wanting him to focus on the good things, rather than the bad things, that he was able to do, and knowing she is incredibly thankful that her son was able to keep her from killing someone else.

“I knew she wasn’t a certainty to die, which meant there was hope,” Nicky tells his mama. “I knew what I had to do, even though it broke the promise I made mom,” Nicky explains.

“What promise was that?” Agatha asks her son.

“That I wouldn’t break the Sigil,” Nicky explains. “It was going to break on its own at the end of the Road, but mom made a way for me to break it if needed; there was so many times I was tempted to break it sooner,” Nicky admits. “My plan never involved a Sigil, Mom insisted on that,” Nicky admits, and hearing that Agatha knows there is a conversation that they need to have, but that Rio need to be involved in this particular conversation.

“I see,” Agatha says, feeling that she needs to know exactly what Rio and Nicky’s plan is, and that’s not a conversation to have with only Nicky. “Rio,” Agatha calls, and Rio excuses herself form the others and walks over.

“Yeah?” Rio asks.

“You decided to put the Sigil in place?” Agatha asks, wanting to know exactly why Rio decided it was necessary to make it so they both had no idea who Nicky was.

“I did,” Rio confirms,

“Why?” Agatha asks.

“Because if I hadn’t, you’d never agree to go down The Road,” Rio tells Agatha, as she sits down with Agatha and Nicky. “And we need to get to the end of the Road,” Rio explains.

“Why?” Agatha asks, as that’s the one piece of the puzzle that is not fitting for her, but to her surprise it’s not Rio who answers, it’s Nicky.

“In the last three years we’ve seen how the spell you were under adapts, I wasn’t sure if breaking the spell would be permanent,” Nicky explains.

“So, you wanted to go down the road to make sure I was permanently free from her control,” Agatha says, not sure how to feel about that, as she is terrified of going back under the control of Wanda’s spell, but she is also incredibly guilty that Nicky would put himself in incredible danger because of her.

“I want my family to be together as our real selves,” Nicky explains to his mother, who smiles at that and once again kisses his head, but then she notices the look on Rio’s face.

“That’s not your reason,” Agatha realises, knowing that because she knows Rio and knows what the look means.

“I do want us together, more than anything,” Rio assures Agatha, who believes her. “The Salem Seven has come after Nicky before, and I was barely able to get us away from them,” Rio reveals, and Agatha shivers at that because she knows how bad that is, and she also plans to ask Rio more about that when Nicky isn’t around as she doesn’t want to bring up painful memories for him. “I’m limited on what I can do,” Rio admits, saying what both Agatha and Nicky know.

“But I’m not,” Agatha realises. “You wanted me to get my magic back,” Agatha realises, realising that considering everything, that makes sense.

“It is the only way to make sure you and Nicky would be okay,” Rio explains. “Wanda’s spell caused a lot of magical interference in Westview, made it incredibly hard for you and Nicky to be found, which is why we were safe living there for three years, but as soon as I got word that the Salem Seven were getting closer, I knew it was only a matter of time before they attacked,” Rio explains to Agatha.

“And you weren’t sure you could protect us,” Agatha realises, knowing that while Rio is all powerful in a lot of ways, she is limited in the ways she can fight the living, and she cannot, ever, kill.

“What I did to get away from the Salem Seven the first time they found us took almost everything out of me, I knew I wouldn’t be able to do it a second time,” Rio admits, making Agatha curious about just what she did. “Nicky figured out a way to break the spell on you about the same time I found out the Seven were coming after you both,” Rio explains. “I hated the idea of the Sigil, hated that I was taking away time you and Nicky could spend time together, but I didn’t know another way to protect Nicky, and make sure you’d go down The Road, which is the only way for you to get your magic back,” Rio explains, and because she has known Rio so well Agatha knows she is feeling guilty about that, even though she is trying to hide it.

“I don’t know if I would have had the strength to make that decision,” Agatha admits, feeling that she may not have been able to, that she would have made a selfish choice. “You knew what you were giving up,” Agatha says, as there is no question that Rio would know about her own memory being erased if she cast the Sigil.

“I needed to believe I would remember again,” Rio admits, as that’s what gave her the courage to cast the Sigil, that she would get her memories back.

“And yet you made me promise not to break the Sigil,” Nicky reminds his mother.

“Which you did anyway,” Rio tells her son.

“I agreed not to break it unless there was an emergency, I thought what happened qualified,” Nicky admits, and Agatha is very glad that he thought that. “Besides you’re lucky I didn’t break it sooner with the way you two traumatised me,” Nicky tells his mothers.

“Traumatized?” Rio asks concerned.

“What are you talking about?” Agatha asks concerned.

“That fight you had at the house… I’m going to be traumatized for life,” Nicky tells his parents, both of whom exchange fond looks, and while Rio grins, Agatha blushes slightly, it being clear to Nicky that neither consider that fight a bad thing, in fact, unknown to him they both considered that to be foreplay. “Ew gross,” Nicky says, looking between his parents. “I know all I’ve wanted is for my moms to be back together, but I don’t need to see it,” Nicky tells him.

“You didn’t see anything,” Agatha tells her son, knowing that fight was pretty tame for them, and she is even more glad that he didn’t come looking for them before the last task, and hearing that Nicky decides he really doesn’t want to know what his mama would consider something.

“And now you know how I feel when Eddie is around, I didn’t need to see that either,” Rio tells her son.

“Eddie? Is that the boyfriend?” Agatha asks, remembering what Nicky said when they were driving together, becoming very interested in that, wanting to be caught up on what she has missed.

“Yep,” Nicky says happily. “Are you going to threaten him too?” Nicky asks worried as Eddie being threatened by one of his moms was bad enough, no he is worried about what his other mother is going to do.

“You threatened him?” Agatha asks, looking at Rio, not at all surprised by that, and a little amused.

“Not explicitly,” Rio says with a shrug.

“You played with your knife all throughout the first dinner we had together!” Nicky reminds his mom, causing Agatha to laugh, as she can imagine exactly what Rio would have looked like doing that.

“That’s something I always do, not my fault he got scared by it,” Rio responds, causing Nicky to roll his eyes.

“Are you happy, Nicky?” Agatha asks her son, wanting to know that. “Does he treat you well?” Agatha asks.

“Yeah, I am, he does,” Nicky assures his mother. “I can’t wait for you to meet him,” Nicky tells his mother, as it is something he has really wanted to.

“I look forward to it too,” Agatha responds, already having a few ideas about what she is going to do during that meeting, something which Rio realises from the look on her face, and the three of them drift into comfortable silence as they sit together, getting to spend time together, as themselves, for the first time in over a century.

While Rio, Agatha, and Nicky are talking, and spending time together Lilia, Alice and Jen are sitting around the fire, the three of them occasionally glancing over to where the Vidal-Harkness family are.

“What do you think the story there is?” Alice, who is feeling a little stronger, asks the others.

“Complicated,” Jen answers. “I knew Agatha had a son, but I’m going to assume everything else I have heard isn’t true,” Jen admits, very much doubting what she previously believed after everything she has seen on the Road.

“They’ve been apart for a long time,” Lilia admits. “This reunion is a miracle,” Lilia says, being able to tell that.

“Definitely seems like it,” Alice admits, as she knows it’s a miracle, she is still alive, and she has Nicky to thank for that.

“So, you’re doing well in school?” Agatha asks her son, as he and Rio are telling her various things about their lives, while the details may see mundane to others, to her they are incredible, and she is beyond thrilled to learn about them.

“Yeah, not too bad, I actually enjoy it,” Nicky admits, and as he does, he notices the look on Rio’s face. “You don’t have to be so smug about it,” Nicky tells Rio, and Agatha realises there is a story there.

“I didn’t say anything,” Rio tells her son, but the look on her face says so much.

“You didn’t have to, I know that look,” Nicky tells his mother. “You were right, I was wrong, happy?” Nicky asks his mother.

“Thrilled,” Rio responds, with a grin.

“I feel like I’m missing something,” Agatha realises, feeling extremely curious and also feeling a little sad that she doesn’t already know.

“Nicky wasn’t a big fan of going to school when I first told him that he was going to be going,” Rio explains.

“That’s a nice way of saying I sent Mom flying across the room and made it so she couldn’t get up for a while,” Nicky explains, still feeling guilty about that, and Agatha realises that, considering who Rio is, that would have taken some truly powerful magic.

“And I’ve told you that it’s okay, that you had no reason to feel guilty for reacting like that,” Rio assures her son, and Agatha is thrilled to hear that as she knows that it means Rio has been doing her best to make sure Nicky doesn’t feel guilty about his magic, something they both never wanted him to feel.

“Mom’s right, Nicky,” Agatha tells her son. “Sometimes we can’t control our magic, and we do things we don’t expect, never feel guilty for that,” Agatha tells her son, wanting his experience to be different from hers.

“I think I’m going to go for a walk,” Nicky says, making it clear he doesn’t want to talk about it, as he stands up.

“Nicky…” Rio starts to say.

“I’m okay, I won’t go far, I’ll stay on The Road,” Nicky assures his mothers, but before they can stop him, he walks away, causing both his mothers to watch him go with worried looks on their faces.

“Does he feel guilty about his magic?” Agatha asks Rio worried.

“He loves magic, and he loves learning about it, but yes, I do think he has a level of guilt about it, especially when it comes to his sensing abilities,” Rio admits. “Like I said, he’s a lot like you,” Rio says, knowing that she is the only person who knows just how much guilt Agatha carries around with her.

“That’s a part of me I never wanted him to inherit,” Agatha admits, feeling worried about her son.

After walking away from his mothers Nicky heads to a nearby cleaning where there is a swamp. While he appreciates how his mothers are trying to make him feel better about everything the truth is he just feels worse, he feels guiltier. Closing his eyes Nicky allows himself to feel the feeling of the ground beneath him, of the wind rustling on his face, but as he feels everything Nicky quickly opens his eyes as he feels something incredibly wrong.

“You,” Nicky says, horrified, as he sees the ghost of Evanora Harkness standing before him. “How?”

“You didn’t end the session on goodbye,” Evanora says, and Nicky curses the mistake, having no idea what Evanora could want, but knowing that it cannot be anything good, Nicky causes magic to dance around his hand, ready to use it to blast her, having no idea if it will work on a ghost, but knowing he needs to protect himself. “You’re evil, just like your mother,” Evanora tells Nicky, and before he can do anything she flies into him, possessing him, and she uses that control to throw Nicky into the swamp, causing him to sink below the Road, his hoddie being left on the bank as the only sign of him.

Chapter 27

Chapter 27

AN: Thank you so much for the support. I am glad that I am not the only one who has issues with the final two episodes…. Hope you like what’s to come with this story… I think you will. (I hope)

ALSO, this story is 37 chapters. Do you want me to keep updating every twelve hours, or do you want me more often. Let me know.

After watching Nicky walk away both Agatha and Rio want to go after him, but they can both appreciate that he would need some time, so rather than going after him they have re-joined the others around the fire.

“Something’s wrong,” Rio suddenly says, interrupting what Jen was saying, something she wasn’t even listening to. “Nicky knows we would worry, he wouldn’t stay away for this long,” Rio says, clearly concerned, and if her words weren’t enough to concern Agatha Rio’s tone of voice would be more than enough.

“He can’t have gone far,” Jen says, trying to be reassuring. “I’m sure there is nothing to worry about,” Jen says, trying to help but to both Agatha and Rio it just feels like she is being dismissive.

“Have you been on the same road as us?” Agatha asks annoyed as she stands up. “There’s every reason to be worried,” Agatha says, sounding annoyed wit Jen, but also being incredibly concerned about her son.

“You’re right, we’ll help look,” Alice says, standing up. “We’ll find him,” Alice says, trying to be reassuring.

“Thank you,” Rio says as Lilia stands up too. “Call out if you find him,” Rio says, and everyone, even Jen, head in different directions to search for Nicky, both Agatha and Rio feeling absolutely terrified about what has happened to their son, Agatha knowing that now she has gotten him back she cannot lose him again.

The second the ghost of Evanora Harkness flies into him all Nicky feels is hate, and anger, the kind of hate and anger he never wanted to feel, but then he feels pain.

“Ouch,” Nicky says annoyed, as he realises, he has hit the ground. “That was painful,” Nicky says, as he gets to his feet. While he is feeling sore because he fell, but he also feels pain in his heart knowing that his mama grew up around the kind of hate and anger he just got a small taste off.

As he gets to his feet Nicky looks around and as he does, he realises two things, the first is that he is obviously under The Road, and the second is that he is surrounded by the Salem Seven. “Oh great,” Nicky mutters, and having no idea if it will work Nicky uses his magic to levitate and tries to exit the tunnels the same way he came, but he quickly realises that is impossible, and he falls back to the ground. “Okay, running it is,” Nicky says and even though he knows it likely won’t do much Nicky starts to run, going in the direction that tells him there is only one Salem Seven member breaking.

As gets closer Nicky quickly sends a blast at the Salem seven member, knocking them over, before using his magic, in the same way he saw his mom use at his mama’s house, to enhance his jump and catapult over the Salem seven member.

Once he is over the member of the seven Nicky runs down the tunnel that is now clear and without pausing for a second, he uses his magic to cave in the tunnel behind him, trying to prevent the Seven from following, having only one thing on his mind, surviving long enough to get back to his moms.

“Nicky!” Agatha yells, feeling absolutely terrified that she is going to lose him again, as she hurries down The Road, looking for him.

“So, you can care about something other than yourself,” A voice that has haunted her as long as she has been alive says, and Agatha turns to see her mother’s ghost.

“You,” Agatha says furiously. “What did you do?” Agatha asks angrily, as for the first time in her life she doesn’t feel like the scared little kid her mother always made her feel like, rather she just feels worried about her son, and determined to find out what happened to him, no matter what it takes.

“Exactly what I should have done to you,” Evanora says, causing Agatha’s blood to run cold, as she knows exactly what her mother meant by that.

“No, he’s not dead, he can’t be,” Agatha says, needing to believe that.

“He’s already died once,” Evanora says before ‘flying’ away, feeling very satisfied with the pain she just caused her daughter.

“No, he can’t be,” Agatha repeats, needing to believe that, needing to believe that she hasn’t already lost her son before getting a chance to really know him, and as she tries to convince herself that Nicky isn’t gone, she notices something.

Hurrying across the clearing Agatha sees what she knows to be Nicky’s hoddie, which she picks up, but no other sign of him.

“RIO!” Agatha yells, knowing that Rio is the only one who will be able to tell if Evanora was telling the truth. “NICKY!” Agatha yells, and as she does Rio, Jen, Lilia and Alice hurry into the clearing where Agatha is.

“Agatha?” Rio asks, hurrying towards her, seeing what Agatha is holding.

“She says he’s gone,” Agatha says, the heartbreak she is feeling clear in her voice. “Was she telling the truth?” Agatha asks, and while Rio has no idea who ‘she’ is she knows it doesn’t matter, all that matters is their son.

Closing her eyes Rio focuses, and just for a second Agatha, Lilia, Jen and Alice see her Lady Death, persona flicker through, something which confuses everyone but Agatha, and within seconds she has her answers.

“He’s alive,” Rio says, relief clear in her voice as the relief she is feeling is reflected on Agatha’s face. “But I can’t tell where he is,” Rio admits.

“He’s alive?” Agatha asks, needing to once again hear Rio say it.

“He’s alive,” Rio assures her.

“We need to find him,” Agatha says, feeling prepared to do whatever she has to do.

“You can find him,” Rio tells Agatha. “You and Nicky are connected in a way I’m not,” Rio says, feeling very glad about that at this current moment. “He can sense you, can find you, which means you’ll be able to find him,” Rio tells Agatha, having complete faith in Agatha and her ability to find their son, even without her ‘active’ magic.

“I’ve never done that before,” Agatha admits, feeling worried that she is gong to let her son down, again.

“Since when has that ever stopped you before?” Rio asks, as in all the years she has known Agatha she has continuously done things she has never done before, and Agatha smiles slightly.

“Good point,” Agatha says, closing her eyes and focusing on nothing else but her son, and after a few moments she realises something. “He’s that way,” Agatha says, pointing in the direction where she ‘feel’s’ Nicky.

“Then that’s the way we’re going,” Rio says, completely trusting Agatha, and once she does Agatha turns to Lilia, Alice and Jen.

“If you want to stay, or continue on without us, that’s your choice, but we’re going to find our son,” Agatha says, knowing that going on a search for Nicky isn’t what they signed up for.

“There’s no way we’d continue on without you,” Alice tells Agatha. “We’ll help you get him back,” Alice says.

“We share burdens remember,” Lilia says.

“He’s just a kid, I wouldn’t leave him,” Jen says, stressing the ‘I’, and making it clear that she isn’t doing this for Agatha, she is doing this for Nicky.

“Thank you,” Agatha says, everyone else knowing just how much of a big deal it is that Agatha is actually thanking him. “Let’s move,” Agatha says, and not allowing time for the others to dwell on what she said Agatha starts to walk in the direction she knows she will find her son, the others following behind; though in Rio’s case she hurries forward so she is walking side by side with Agatha.

Being sure that his mothers have realised that he is missing and that they are looking for him, Nicky who has no idea where he is going, is continuing to walk through the tunnels beneath The Road. As he can’t ‘feel’ the Salem Seven anymore Nicky is no longer running but is instead walking.

Due to the fact that he is trying to use his abilities to give him as much warning about what is coming as possible as he approaches a corner Nicky realises exactly what he is going to find when he rounds it. As he knows what he is going to face Nicky pulls the knife his mother gave him as he approaches the corner as while he isn’t sure it will do anything he figures, that considering who’s knife it is, it is his best option.

“Should have known you weren’t done with me,” Nicky says as he rounds the corner and sees Evanora’s ghost.

“You and your mother are stains on my family!” Evanora tells Nicky. “I am ashamed that you share my blood! I will not rest until you’ve been removed,” Evanora tells Nicky, who rolls his eyes at her.

“Wow, do you realise how much of a hypocrite you’re being?” Nicky asks his grandmother, not at all phased about his grandmothers’ words as she doesn’t matter to him. “From the moment Mama was born you decided who she was. You decided that because she wasn’t the same as you imagined she would be she was evil,” Nicky tells Evanora. “Did ever even try to see who she really was?” Nicky asks his grandmother, as he very much doubts it, but wants to know what she is going to say to that.

“I didn’t have to,” Evanora says. “She was a devil child, stole the magic of others! Corrupted other girls!” Evanora exclaims.

“She couldn’t control it! she still can’t because you didn’t teach her how to!” Nicky exclaims, feeling very protective of his mother. “You were her mother, the head of her coven! You had a responsibility. You were meant to teach her, not give up on her!” Nicky exclaims, tightening the hold on his knife, feeling angry, but trying really hard not to lose control.

“I tried to teach her to be righteous, tried to teach her to be proper! To not be unnatural! But she never learnt, no matter what lessons she received,” Evanora says, and because he can read between the lines of what Evanora is saying Nicky feels sick; not realising that the reality of what his mama went through is actually worse than he is imagining.

“That’s it isn’t it?” Nicky asks, taking a step towards Evanora, feeling braver. “Your biggest problem with mama isn’t that she can take others magic, it’s not that she can’t control her abilities,” Nicky says. “Your biggest problem is that she’s a lesbian,” Nicky says to his grandmother, feeling horrified by her, and feeling incredibly sorry for his mama, and the disgusted look on Evanora’s face is enough to confirm what he is thinking. “You never accepted her at all,” Nicky realises, having no idea what that would have been like for his mama to grow up like that as all he has never experienced anything other than supportive moms.

“It’s unnatural, it makes her an abomination; that can never be acceptable,” Evanora says, her voice full of disgust and hate.

“That’s where you’re wrong,” Nicky says angrily. “A parent is meant to love and support their child, always. By not doing that you’re the unnatural one, you’re the evil one,” Nicky says, taking a step closer to her, standing tall, showing that he is not afraid of her. “And you know what, despite everything you did, all the hurt you cased, as much as you tried to make Mama believe she would never be loved; she is,” Nicky says. “Mom found her, they found each other, and they fell in the love, the truest love you could never understand, and because of that love they had me,” Nicky tells his grandmother. “And you know what else? Even though she never had an example to use all I’ve ever known from mama is acceptance, love and support; she couldn’t be further from what you tried to make her be,” Nicky admits. “You’ve may have hurt Mama in the past but you’re never going to hurt her again, Mom and I won’t let you, because that’s what actual family does; protect each other,” Nicky says, feeling his magic crackling within him.

“You speak like you have a choice… you don’t,” Evanora says, starting to fly towards Nicky, it being perfectly clear that she is going to possess him again, and as she flies towards him Nicky knows exactly what to do. Having no idea if it is going to work once his grandmother is close enough Nicky thrusts his arm out and stabs the ghost with the knife that belongs to death.

For a second it is almost like the knife did nothing, but then Nicky’s magic encircles the blade, and it spreads from the knife all through Evanora causing her to scream in excruciating pain before, with a force so strong that it knocks Nicky off his feet, Evanora is destroyed.

“Well, that hurt,” Nicky says, feeling rather dizzy, and as he still has the knife in his hand Nicky can feel it’s power, he can feel that what he did was only possible because he, the son of Lady Death and one of the most powerful witches to ever exist, wielded that specific blade. “That was for you, mama,” Nicky mutters, feeling proud that he is going to be able to tell his mama that her mother will never hurt her again, and as he sits up, he realises that he has landed on something. Feeling curious Nicky digs around the dirt and finds his spell book. “Huh,” Nicky says as he holds the object, feeling glad to have it again, but also feeling a little drained because of everything that just happened.

Having no idea what their son is currently experiencing Rio and Agatha are still walking with the rest of the coven, walking towards where, according to the connection Agatha shares with their son, they will find, Nicky.

“How’s his defensive magic?” Agatha asks Rio, wanting to know if Nicky will be able to defend himself if he comes face to face with the Salem Seven.

“Pretty good,” Rio assures Agatha, who is relieved about that. “He also has one of my knifes,” Rio reveals.

“You taught him to use your knife?” Agatha asks, causing the others to exchange looks as while Rio teaching Nicky how to use her knife is clearly something significant, they don’t know why.

“When he was ten,” Rio says, and from the look on Agatha’s face Rio is sure she isn’t completely happy about that. “I couldn’t always be with him, I wanted to make sure he had as many ways to protect himself as possible,” Rio admits, and as she does the disapproval on Agatha’s face slips away.

“Seems like it was a good thing you did,” Agatha admits, giving Rio a look which means ‘it’s okay,’ and the two of them drift into silence.

“So, Nicky, he’s both of your son?” Jen asks, breaking the silence, causing Alice to give her a ‘are you seriously asking that right now,’, look.

“Yes,” Agatha and Rio say together.

“In every way,” Agatha adds, wanting to make that clear.

“And you were separated?” Lilia asks in a gentle voice, trying to understand a little more.

“For too long,” Agatha says, and once she does Rio reaches out and takes her hand, giving it a supportive squeeze and as they see the actions of the pair Lilia, Jen, and Alice exchange looks, and while they are incredibly curious about what that means they also realise that it’s not the time to ask.

As she is holding Rio’s hand Agatha feels her suddenly tense, and let out a small gaps,

“Rio?” Agatha asks concerned, dreading what she is going to say as she knows it’s not often Rio reacts like that.

“I just felt something, something I’ve never felt before,” Rio admits, trying to make sense of what she just felt. “An incredible release of power, caused a ripple,” Rio says, feeling confused about what could have caused that.

“It was Nicky,” Agatha says, knowing that their son being the reason Rio is feeling is the only thing that makes sense.

“I think so,” Rio admits, feeling that that makes sense. “But whatever he did… I’ve never felt that before,” Rio admits, and as she does Agatha has a suspicion as deep inside, she feels like a weight has been lifted.

“My mothers ghost escaped the trial,” Agatha reveals, causing Rio to give her a surprised look. “Do you think he somehow managed to destroy her?” Agatha asks, as that is the only thing that makes sense to her, the only thing that would fit with what she is currently feeling.

“I don’t know,” Rio admits. “If any being was capable of destroying ghosts it would make sense to be him… but I just don’t know,” Rio admits, trying to make sense of everything.

“Why do you think the son of witches could destroy a ghost?” Jen asks, and as she does Lilia comes to a realisation.

“You’re not a witch,” Lilia says to Rio.

“Technically I’m the first Green Witch,” Rio admits. “But these days I’m better known as Lady Death,” Rio reveals, and she isn’t at all surprised when Lilia, Alice, and Jen take a step back from her, it being perfectly clear they are all shocked.

“You’re dating death!” Jen exclaims, giving Agatha a shocked look.

“Married to Death actually,” Agatha corrects, sounding rather proud and she is amused by the shocked look on Jen’s face.

“That’s so cool,” Alice says, causing both Agatha and Rio to laugh.

“Your son has a long path ahead of him, will face challenges no one else has faced, experience profound changes, is capable of thing you can’t imagine, he will need more support than you realise,” Lilia says, in her ‘wispy’ tone of voice which tells the others that she is making a prediction.

“He’s got it, no matter what,” Agatha says and Rio nods in agreement.

“Got what?” Lilia asks confused, and Rio turns to look at her.

“Don’t worry about it, but thank you,” Rio tells Lilia who feels even more confused, and as she turns around she realises something.

“You’ve got to be kidding me,” Rio says annoyed, as there is what looks like a cabin in the distance which tells her they will find another trial there. “We do not have time for this,” Rio says, as all she wants is to get to her son, not go through a trial that is clearly hers.

“He’s inside,” Agatha tells Rio, who turns to look at her, sounding as annoyed as Rio. “Nicky’s inside the trial,” Agatha reveals, knowing that without a doubt.

“Of course he is,” Rio realises, knowing that she should have seen this coming. “Down the rabbit hole I go then,” Rio says.

“Not alone,” Agatha says, squeezing Rio’s hand and the two of them walk towards the ‘Cabin’ and even though they are still shocked by everything that was revealed in the past few minutes, Lilia, Jen, and Alice follow behind and together they enter the trial, all prepared to face whatever is to come as a coven.

Chapter 28

Chapter 28:

AN: I have decided to update more frequently. My goal is going to be to update two or three chapters in a day. ALSO, I am definitely going to keep writing Agathario and have a list of stories I want to write, so if there is anything you want to see please leave in a comment and I will add it to my list, and see if I feel inspired to write it.

The second they enter the 'cabin' are once again changed to fit the trial as all five of them find themselves in what seems to be a clearing that seems strikingly familiar to both Agatha and Rio, while the entire group have been changed into outfits fitting of the late 1600s.

"I'm guessing this has some significance for the two of you," Jen comments, assuming that not only because it is clearly Rio's trial, but because of the looks on both Agatha and Rio's faces.

"You could say that," Agatha says, knowing that the 'trial' has become a place that is the place where she had both one of the worst moments in her life, but also one of her best, both moments happening within minutes of each other, and as she says that a raven files and lands on a nearby log with a parchment around it's leg.

"I assume that's for me," Rio assumes, as that is what makes the most sense.

"It would be the start of the trial," Jen tells her.

"Of course," Rio says, walking over to the bird and taking the piece of parchment. As she knows that whatever the note says effects everyone else just as much as her Rio opens it and reads the message out loud:

"The Road welcomes you to the penultimate trial. You have learned secrets of the past but now you need to understand how the past affects you. As the first Green Witch, a cosmic being, you need to be grounded, at peace within yourself, but you are not. You have the job of maintaining harmony within the universe, but you cannot do that if you don't have inner harmony. A journey through your past to find what you are missing awaits, but be warned, the past has a way of coming back with a vengeance," Rio reads, and as she finishes the note, she looks at Agatha.

"Well, that sounds like it's going to be fun," Agatha says sarcastically, though she cannot help but be considered about how the note described Rio's current state.

"Yeah," Rio says, really not looking forward to this. "Can you tell where Nicky is?" Rio asks Agatha, wanting to focus on him, and Agatha shakes her head in response.

"No, I can just tell he is here," Agatha admits.

"Great," Rio says annoyed, as that doesn't help, and right now she would much rather find her son than compete a trial. "So, I guess we should figure out what way to go," Rio comments, looking around, and seeing there is no exit, but several paths that come off the clearing.

"If this location is connected to you past then you know where each path will lead too," Lilia points out.

"Well, that path led to town," Rio says, pointing to one of the paths that is coming off the clearing. "The path leads to your mothers house," Rio says, pointing to another path as she looks at Agatha.

"Which we are definitely not going down," Agatha says, having no intention of going back there, even if it is a protected simulation, and Rio has to agree with her about that.

"What about that path?" Jen asks, pointing to the one that Rio hasn't explained.

"That's the one we went down the first time we left this clearing together," Rio says, looking at Agatha as she speaks.

"Sounds like the perfect place to start if the trial is about learning how the past affects you," Alice admits.

"Yeah, I guess it would be," Rio admits, feeling very nervous, and Agatha once again takes her hand, wanting to show Rio that no matter what may have happened between them in the past they are okay now, that she isn't alone.

"Whatever it is, you can face it, we can face it," Agatha assures Rio, and feeling comforted Rio nods.

Taking strength and comfort from Agatha Rio starts to walk down the path they walked all those years ago, and as they walk down the path, they find an arch made of the same kind of flowers Rio gave Agatha when she showed up on the road. Exchanging one more look with Agatha Rio, with Agatha by her side, and the rest of the coven walking behind, walks through the arch.

As soon as they walk through the arch the group find themselves in a location that is just as significant to Rio and Agatha as the clearing, they were just in.

"No," Rio mutters, horror in her voice, looking around and seeing that they have been transported to the home where she and Agatha lived for the few months that proceeded Nicky dying.

" Rio? Is that you?" Agatha's voice says, coming from a partially open door, both present Agatha and Rio knowing exactly what they will find throughout the door.

"I don't want to go in there," Rio says, trying to move back form the door, falling backwards as she is trying so hard to get away from the door, as even though Nicky has returned to them it doesn't take away the pain, grief, and anger that his death caused.

"I know, I know Mi Amour," Agatha says, walking over to her. "I don't want to either," Agatha admits, as she squats down on the ground. "But we have to," Agatha reminds Rio, reaching out and pushing Rio's hair out of her face. "Sweetheart, what we're going to see is our past, and as hard as it's going to be, you need to remember that our son, our Nicky, is alive; you brought him back to us," Agatha reminds her. "We've got to go through this to get to him," Agatha reminds her, trying to get Rio to focus on what they need to do rather than what they are going to experience.

"I hate this," Rio says to Agatha in a quiet voice.

"Me too," Agatha responds, and Rio leans forward and hugs Agatha. For a few moments Agatha returns the hug, holding her tightly, and kissing her check, until they finally break apart. "We can do this," Agatha tells Rio.

"We can do this," Rio responds, and before she can think better of what she is going to do Rio stands up, and once Agatha once again takes her hand the two of them head through the partially open door, and the others, who have no idea what they are going to find, follow behind.

As soon as the group walk through the door, they see Agatha, clearly a little younger, sitting on a bed, holding Nicky when he was on seven, and it is clear to everyone that he isn't well.

"It's me, I'm here," Rio, who looks exactly the same, hurries into the room, as unknown to everyone, except for the version of her watching on, she was trying to find a way to prevent what she knew was about to happen.

"Mommy," Nicky says, and he barely gets the word out before he starts gasping, and coughing.

"Pneumonia?" Jen asks, as that's what it seems like to her, and considering what time period it appears to be she can guess what's about to happen.

"Yeah," Agatha confirms, fighting back her reaction, as she wants to be strong for Rio, even if she feels her own heart break.

"It's okay, Sweetheart, we're right here," Agatha assured her son. "You're going to be okay," Agatha said, then she noticed the look on Rio's face. "Don't," Agatha said to Rio, who looked heartbroken.

"Nicky, Mi Conejito," Rio said, as she reached out and took her son's hand. "Mama and I love you so much," Rio said, as Nicky continued to gasp, it was perfectly clear he struggled for every strangled breath. "You can let go, it's okay," Rio said, as she could tell how much her son was suffering, and she didn't want that for him.

"No! stop! No!" Agatha yelled, as she clung to her son. "Hold on, Nicky, please, just hold on," Agatha begged.

"Mama?" Nicky asked confused.

As they both know what is coming both Agatha and Rio close their eyes, not wanting to see what is about to happen again, while the rest of the coven just watch in silent, very much feeling like they are intruding, but also feeling that it explained so much about the two women.

"I love you, I love you so much," Agatha told her son, as she held him, and as does she felt the instant he stopped breathing. "Nicky?" Agatha asked her son, her voice breaking. "Nicky?" Agatha asked again, desperate for him to respond.

"Agatha…" Rio stared to say, and as she did Agatha turned to look at her with a look of pure fury on her face, her purple magic clearly crackling behind her eyes.

"Bring him back!" Agatha exclaimed.

"I can't," Rio said.

"You're death! You can do anything!" Agatha told her.

"Not this," Rio said, Agatha being so caught up in her own grief that she did not realise that every word was causing Rio pain. "He's…." Rio started to say.

"No! don't you dare say it!" Agatha said. "He's our son! Save him! please! Don't take him!" Agatha begged.

"I have to," Rio told Agatha.

"You don't have to do anything! and if you loved us, you wouldn't!" Agatha said.

Hearing her past words Agatha knows what she has to do and because of that she moves and stands in front of Rio, blocking her view of what they are re-experiencing, causing Agatha's past words, words that were full of pain, hate and grief, to fade away.

"I know you love us," Agatha tells Rio. "I know you had no choice, that you had to do your job," Agatha tells Rio. "I'm sorry for what I am about to say, I'm sorry I blamed you," Agatha tells Rio, finally giving the apology she should have given a long time ago.

"I deserved it," Rio says. "I did take him away, I'm so sorry," Rio says, her voice breaking. "I didn't want to," Rio says, and in response Agatha hugs her, holding her close. "I'm sorry, I'm so sorry," Rio says, as she breaks down in Agatha's arms, and because they are so consumed by their own grief neither Rio nor Agatha notice who has joined them.

"Mom, it's okay," Nicky says, and his mothers break apart and see him, both feeling amazed. "It was my time, I was too little, too sick," Nicky says, walking towards his mothers. "But you made sure I was okay, you made sure I found peace, and I did, until you were able to bring me back for my second chance," Nicky tells his mothers. "I was okay because of you, I love you, both of you, so much," Nicky tells his mothers and in response they both hug him, tightly. "You both need to forgive yourselves, because I do, because I'm okay because of the two of you," Nicky assures her mothers, as they continue to hug him tightly.

"Are you?" Agatha asks her son, when they finally break apart after a few moments. "Are you really okay?" Agatha asks concerned.

"Yeah, a little bruised, but I'm okay," Nicky tells his mothers. "Um, so I may have destroyed Evanora's ghost," Nicky admits, feeling that it is important he tells them that, and knowing that his mom was right, and that Evanora has no right to be called Grandmother.

"You did," Rio tells him. "That's something pretty incredible," Rio tells her son, clearly proud of him, despite everything else she is feeling.

"What can I say? I take after my moms," Nicky says with a smile, and in response, both Agatha and Rio, hug him again.

"We love you so much," Rio says as she hugs her son.

"I know, I love you too," Nicky says, and the three of them break apart once more. "Mom, you need to forgive yourself, you need to let go of the guilt I know you carry," Nicky tells his mother.

"I don't know if I can," Rio admits, and as she does everyone feels a small Earthquake.

"I think you have to," Agatha tells her wife, not saying that because of the earthquake, but because she knows it's what Rio needs. "I think that's your trial," Agatha tells her. "Ri, I know I've hurt you, and I've blamed you, and I'm sorry about that, but I don't anymore. I don't think I ever truly did it was just easier to blame you than myself," Agatha admits. "But no more, I forgive you, Nicky forgives you, it's time to forgive yourself," Agatha tells her. "You were doing your job, it wasn't your fault," Agatha says. "Say it," Agatha encourages.

"I was doing my job… it wasn't my fault," Rio says, and as soon as she says the words three things happen, the first is that both Agatha and Nicky hug her again, the second is that another flower arch appears, and the third is the earth stops shaking.

After a few moments Rio, Agatha, and Nicky all break apart and once they do Agatha reaches out and wipes the tears off Rio's face.

"We should go," Agatha tells Rio.

"I know," Rio responds, and after taking a deep breath Rio, with her son and her wife standing either side of her, while the rest of the coven stand behind them, walk through the arch, walking to the next part of her past that Rio needs to forgive herself for.

As soon as the group walk through the arch they find themselves outside again, and this time it is a location that not just Rio and Agatha recognize, but Nicky does too.

"We lived here," Nicky says, looking around and seeing the house he died in, in burned ruins. "What happened?" Nicky asks, feeling confused, as he is sure that it didn't look like this the last time he was actually there.

"When mom took you to the veil I lost control, destroyed almost everything," Agatha reveals, though judging by the exact way everything is destroyed she is sure that this memory isn't from exactly after Nicky died, in fact, she has a sinking suspicion she knows exactly when this is.

"I got back and found everything in ruins… just like the life we built together," Rio says sadly, remembering what it felt like to find their home on fire, and that that is exactly why she has tried so hard to keep the cottage in good condition, because she didn't want to lose another place, she considered to be a home.

"It's not destroyed anymore," Agatha assures Rio, who nods.

"So, if this is your memory where are you?" Jen asks, feeling confused about that.

"Wait," Agatha says, and seconds after she does both Agatha and Rio, neither looking particularly older than the previous memory, teleport into the location.

"Here? Really?" Agatha asked, a look of fury on her face.

"I wanted to remind you of who you used to be," Rio told Agatha, and even though it is just a memory everyone can almost feel the power, and pain, radiated off both women.

Hearing that Nicky suspects he is about to see the fight that caused his mama to hide herself from his mom, and while he is incredibly curious about that, he is also incredibly concerned about how his moms are going to handle this.

"Well then you picked the wrong place," Agatha said. "All I see here is everything you took from me," Agatha said, angrily.

"I took from you? He was my son too! And he died! I couldn't change that!" Rio exclaimed, and as she did Agatha gave a bitter laugh.

As she is reminded of her past selves' words Rio looks down at the ground and after a few moments she feels Agatha reach out and take her hand, offering her silent support.

"You're death! You can do anything you want," Agatha said to her.

"Not that," Rio said. "Agatha, nothing can bring him back," Rio told Agatha.

"I don't believe that I'm going to get him back!" Agatha exclaims.

"How? By losing yourself in the Darkhold?" Rio asked, taking a step forward.

Hearing that Jen and Lilia exchange looks, both of them knowing enough about the Darkhold to appreciate the significance of that, while Jen suspects they're about to find out how Agatha got the Book of Dammed.

As Nicky hears the words, he realises that what he is suspected is true, that his mama went after the Darkhold because of him, which means everything that followed happened because of him, something which makes him feel incredibly guilty.

"It's not the answer, Agatha," Rio told her. "Even if the book was able to bring him back, if you use it, if you gave what you would need to give it to do, so you'd be so lost Nicky wouldn't even recognize you," Rio told Agatha, having felt that she needed to do whatever she could to stop Agatha from going after the Darkhold which she was close to getting.

"You have no right! No right to say his name!" Agatha told Rio as tears of fury came to her eyes. "I am going to get my son back," Agatha said, stressing the 'my'. "And I'm never going to see you again," Agatha told Rio.

"You can't hide from me, Agatha," Rio told her.

"Watch me," Agatha said, at the time already having decided that she was going to use the Darkhold to hide from Rio, and she turned away from Rio.

"Agatha! Please! Don't do this," Rio begged. "Don't use that damn book!" Rio exclaims. "It's not the answer!" Rio exclaimed, reaching for Agatha, and in response Agatha used her magic to throw Rio backwards.

"Because of you it's the only answer I have," Agatha said. "Goodbye Rio," Agatha said before teleporting away, as Rio broke down.

"You blamed yourself because I went after the Darkhold?" Agatha asks Rio surprised, as she didn't realise that.

"I couldn't stop you," Rio says, guilt in her voice, as she can't help but wonder how different things would have been if she had managed to stop Agatha from going after that Darkhodl.

"Ri, nothing was gong to stop me," Agatha said, the old nickname slipping from her lips without her even thinking about it. "At this point the Darkhold was already calling for me, already influencing me, nothing was going to keep me from that book," Agatha admits. "But that was my choice, my decision, not yours," Agatha tells her.

"I hate that I couldn't save you from it," Rio admits.

"You can't save someone who doesn't want to be saved," Alice says, knowing that from her own experience.

"She's right," Agatha says, feeling thankful for Alice. "I didn't want to be saved," Agatha admits. "You did everything you could, but this was something even you couldn't change," Agatha tells her wife. "This is on me, so is everything that happened because of it, not you," Agatha tells Rio. "This guilt, this blame, you need to let go of it," Agatha says, and after a few moments of hesitation Rio gives a nod.

As soon as Rio nods another flowered arch appears, but instead of walking through it Agatha once again embraces Rio, holding her tight, wishing she could keep Rio from needing to re-experience this pain, but she knows she can't.

"I'm sorry," Rio says to Agatha in a quiet voice.

"You don't have to be," Agatha assures Rio, as she kisses her cheek.

As he watches his mothers embrace each other Nicky wants to do something to help them, but as he watches he knows he can't, so instead he just watches them, wishing very much that his mothers weren't in so much pain.

After a few moments Agatha and Rio break apart and once they do, they once again walk, hand in hand through the arch, neither having any idea what they are gong to face on the other side, but knowing that, as hard as it may be, they will face it together.

Chapter 29

Chapter 29

AN : Thank you so much for the support. Here is another chapter. I may post another chapter when I am working, or be closer to my normal time, I'm not sure yet. It depends on how busy I am while working.

As Rio and Agatha lead themselves, their son, and their coven, through the next arch they find themselves in a location that for once Agatha doesn't recognize, but both Rio and Nicky do.

"A hospital?" Agatha asks confused, as she looks around, trying to figure out the time period this is taking place in.

"I remember this," Nicky realises. "Mom, this wasn't your fault," Nicky tells her, understanding exactly what is going on.

"I left you," Rio tells him. "It was my fault," Rio tells her son, and while Agatha is incredibly confused, she doesn't say anything, she just watches the memory play out as she knows it's the best way to get the answers, she is seeking without causing Rio even more pain.

" Help! I need help!" Rio yelled, panic having been perfectly clear in her voice, as she carried who everyone recognized as Nicky into the emergency room.

"When was this?" Alice asks, looking between Rio and Nicky, trying to figure out exactly how long ago this was.

"A little over a year after mom brought me back form the veil, seven years ago," Nicky explains, and Agatha realises that Nicky would have been eight.

"What happened?" A nurse asked, as she came out from the behind the reception desk.

"I got home, and all the windows were open, he's so cold, I don't know how long he has been like this," Rio said, and Agatha can hear the guilt in his voice.

"Mom, it wasn't your fault. I choose to open the windows in October, when we were in the Scottish Highlands," Nicky reminds her, knowing now that wasn't the smartest decision he's ever made, but at the time he didn't even think about it.

"And you wouldn't have gotten so sick if I had been home sooner," Rio tells Nicky, still feeling incredibly guilty about that, and everyone watches as past Rio is lead over to a bed where she lays Nicky down on the bed.

"What's his name? how old is he?" the nurse asked.

"Nicky… Nicholas Scratch," Rio says.

"Is that really your name?" Jen asks, feeling that that is very unfortunate.

"No, it's my main alias," Nicky explains.

"You need an alias?" Lilia asks.

"Does that surprise you?" Nicky asks, feeling that out of everyone Lilia should be the least surprised by that.

"No, I guess not," Lilia admits, feeling that considering who his mothers are that actually makes perfect sense.

"Any medical conditions? Or past medical issues?" The nurse asked.

"Pneumonia," Rio said, her voice breaking, and hearing the pain in Rio's past selves voice, Agatha squeezes her hand. "Last year… it was bad," Rio said. "Please, please help him," Rio begged.

"Death begs," Jen mutters, feeling shocked by that, and luckily for her neither Agatha nor Nicky hear her.

"We will, ma'am," the nurse said as several people came running over to the bed. "But we need you to give us some space so we can work,"

"No, I'm not leaving my son," Rio said.

"I shouldn't have left," Rio mutters, feeling guilty that she did, even though she was forced out of the room.

"You had to, it's okay," Nicky assures his mother, and everyone watches as Rio is dragged out of the hospital room.

"Nicky! I'm right here! I'm not going anywhere! I love you," Rio yelled to her son.

"I heard you," Nicky tells his mom. "And because of that I knew I was going to be okay," Nicky assures Rio.

"You did?" Rio asks surprised, as she didn't know that.

"Yeah, I did," Nicky confirms. "You made me feel brave, Mom," Nicky assures his mother.

"Damn it," Rio said angrily, as she walked over to a wall which she punched. "Damn it Agatha, you should be here," Rio said, as she punched the wall again. "Why did you have to become so obsessed with that damn book, why did you have to hide yourself," Rio said, her voice breaking. "We need you," Rio said as she slid down the wall as she broke down in tears.

"I'm so sorry I wasn't there," Agatha tells Rio. "That I wasn't there for both of you," Agatha says, as she looks between Rio and Nicky, feeling incredibly guilty that she wasn't there for them, especially when they so clearly needed her.

"You didn't know," Rio tells her. "I shouldn't have been angry at you for not being there," Rio admits.

"You were trying to do everything alone, some anger is justified… it's okay," Agatha assures her, feeling that considering the circumstances Rio was completely justified in what she was feeling.

"Mom, you looked after me," Nicky assures his mother. "Even with an entire universe of responsibilities you looked after me. You did everything you could to make sure I was safe, you have nothing to feel guilty about," Nicky assures her.

"Rio for eight years you were there for our son, you looked after him, supported him, you protected him, made sure he was happy," Agatha reminds her. "I am so amazed by you, so proud, and so incredibly thankful," Agatha assures her.

"Mom, I'm okay because of you," Nicky tells her. "I may not have had the most normal upbringing, but I was never going to have that, what you gave me was incredible, I love you," Nicky tells his mom before hugging her and whispering something in her ear. As mother and son embrace, and as Rio forgives herself just a little more, another arch appears.

This time, even though the arch appears, Rio and Nicky don't break apart, Rio just continues to hold her son who she feels like she let down, and it becomes clear that that is not what the trial is as the Earth begins to shake once more.

"Guess we should go," Nicky realises, as he breaks apart from his mom.

"Yeah, guess so," Rio says reluctantly, and once again the group make their way to the arch.

Walking through the arch the group find that they are once again outside, this time in a location that they all recognize.

"This is Westview," Jen realises, and as she does Nicky is looking around, trying to figure out exactly when it was.

"Oh, no," Nicky says, as decorations that tell him exactly when it is; New Years Eve 2024.

"Nicky?" Agatha asks her son concerned, but before Nicky can answer the entire group hear Nicky and Rio's voices so they turn to the house they share where Nicky, who is younger than he currently is not overly so, and Rio are both walking out of.

"I won't be too late, I'll make responsible choices, and promise I won't do anything dangerous," Nicky told his mother.

"You know I am meant to be giving you rules, it's kind of the parent thing," Rio told Nicky, and Agatha can't help but smile at that.

"Oh? What rules would you give me?" Nicky asked his mother, and Rio paused for a moment.

"Whatever you just said sounds good," Rio said, and Nicky laughed.

"Seriously?" Jen asks amused, though as she watches Rio and Nicky it perfectly clear that they are a mother and so who truly care about each other.

"Nicky's a pretty responsible teenager, what he was saying seemed fine to me," Rio responds, feeling nervous about what is going to happen next as while she remembers this conversation with Nicky, she doesn't remember much of what happened next.

"In all seriousness I want you to have fun, okay?" Rio said to her son, and only Agatha appreciates the irony of Rio saying 'seriousness'.

"Okay," Nicky said before hugging her. "I love you mom," Nicky said.

"Love you too," Rio said, and after a moment they broke apart. "Now, go, have fun," Rio told her son.

"I will, by mom," Nicky said before hurrying down the path, heading towards the town centre.

After watching her son go it is clear Rio is debating what do, and rather than heading back inside she, likes Nicky, walks out of the yard, but instead of going in the direction he went in she goes in the opposite direction and walks down the street, and Agatha realises exactly where she is going.

"You going to see me," Agatha realises.

"Yeah," Rio confirms, and for Nicky what he found when he returned home that night is starting to make a lot more sense.

"I thought you said you had been apart for a while," Alice says, confused, not understanding what she is missing.

"We were," Agatha says. "I was under a spell, under the control of another, I wasn't myself," Agatha says. truthfully, she is curious to see herself under the spell, see how she interacts with Rio, but, considering Nicky's reaction, she is incredibly concerned about what she is going to witness, as she can't help the horrible feeling that is telling her that as 'Agnes' she is about to do something that is going to hurt Rio.

As Rio gets to what everyone recognizes as Agatha's house it is clear that for a second Rio questions her decision, but then she clearly uses magic to conjure a bottle of scotch before walking the rest of the way to the house where she knocks on the door.

After a few seconds the door opens to reveal Agatha dressed in short shorts and a tank top, clothing very inappropriate for the middle of winter in New Jersey, with her hair up in a messy bun.

" What the hell do you want?" Agnes asked, angrily and the fact that Rio looks completely unphased by her anger concerns, and hurts, Agatha deeply as it tells her that it is something she had gotten used to.

" A brought a peace offering," Rio said as she showed Agatha the bottle of scotch she conjured.

" Then I guess you better come in," Agnes said, and Rio followed her into the house.

" That explains the outfit," Rio said to herself quietly as she felt how hot it was into the house, it having been perfectly clear to her that the heater and fireplace where both on high. "Bit warm in here, isn't it…. Agnes," Rio said.

" It's the middle of summer, what do you expect," Agnes said, showing everyone who is watching just how out of phase with reality she is, something which makes Lilia, who appreciates just how much control Agatha would have been under to achieve this result, frown.

" Right, summer," Rio muttered, as she followed Agatha through to the kitchen.

" You know all these new recruits are driving me crazy, almost makes me miss the old days," Agnes, said, and everyone notices Rio tense at that.

" When you were the one driving people crazy?" Rio asked, as she tried to adapt to Agatha's reality.

" It was much more fun," Agatha said, giving Rio a very pointed look. "The things we got up to," Agnes said, lowering her voice.

" Impossible to forget," Rio said, returning the look on Agatha's face.

Hearing the tones, and seeing the looks on both hers and Rio's face Agatha feels concerned as she knows what usually follow those looks, but she also knows Rio, and knows that when she wasn't herself there is no way Rio would let anything happen between them, which means something they are about to witness something very uncomfortable.

"I've got no clean glasses over here; can you grab some form that cupboard?" Agatha requested.

"Sure," Rio said, before walking over to the cupboard to get the cups. Once she has the cups Rio turns around to Agatha pushing up against her. "Aga…nes," Rio said, it being clear that she was about to say Agatha and not Agnes. "What are you doing?" Rio asked, moving out of the way as Agnes tried to kiss her.

"Exactly what you intended when you showed up on my door," Agnes said, as she tried to kiss Rio again, but Rio once again moved out of the way.

As she watches the memory play out Rio looks down at the ground, feeling incredibly guilty that she let it go on for as long as she did. While Nicky is very uncomfortable but because he doesn't want his moms to feel worse than they clearly already do he does his best not to let that show.

"I didn't come here for this," Rio said, and she pushed Agatha back, with a little more force than she intended, which caused Agatha to stumble, and hit her leg on the kitchen island. "I should go," Rio said, and without another word she ran out of the house, clearly looking upset, and to her own house.

Once inside her own house everyone watches as Rio picks up multiple bottles of scotch and starts to drink them, quickly.

"Can Death get drunk?" Jen asks, trying to lighten the mood as they all understand the implications of what they just watched.

"Not easily," Rio admits. "But I guess I must have succeeded, because I don't remember much after this," Rio admits, and as she does, she notices Nicky looking down at the ground, clearly avoiding looking at everyone else. "But you do," Rio says to her son. "Nicky, what happened?" Rio asks worried, feeling worried about what she must have put him through, and Nicky avoids answering her. "Nicky, tell me," Rio tells her son in a stern tone of voice, one that Nicky knows not to ignore as it's not often his mom uses it.

"Um, so I got home just before midnight, and there was a lot of empty bottles," Nicky says, trying to explain as little as possible, as he really, really doesn't want to cause his mom more pain.

"What else?" Rio asks, knowing her son well enough to know that there is something he isn't saying.

"You were crying," Nicky says, and Agatha feels a rush of guilt, as she knows it's her fault, that she caused Rio so much pain. "You said how you missed her, how you just wanted her back, I assumed you were talking about Mama," Nicky admits, causing both his mothers to feel guilty about that. "You passed out, I used my magic to levitate you to bed," Nicky explains.

"I am so sorry you had to do that," Rio tells her son, feeling incredibly guilty that she put him through that.

"Mom, it's okay, you were hurting, it's okay," Nicky assures her, and he hugs his mother.

"Neither of you have any reason to apologize," Agatha says, and once she does both Rio and Nicky break apart to look at her. "You did the right thing in an incredible painful situation," Agatha says to Rio.

"I couldn't do anything else, not when you weren't yourself," Rio tells Agatha, wanting to make it clear that she never let anything happen between them when Agatha was Agnes.

"I know," Agatha says, having never even considered she would. "And Nicky, you looked after mom, that was incredible of you," Agatha tells her son. "I am sorry that you were even put in the situation in the first place," Agatha tells them.

"You were under a spell, you didn't willingly choose it," Rio reminds her.

"I did choose to go after the Scarlett Witch, the spell was my consequence," Agatha tells her. "Neither of you have any reason to feel guilty about what happened to me because of that," Agatha says, wanting to make that clear.

"Easier said than done," Nicky tells his mama as for him he feels guilty that he didn't break the spell sooner, and nothing either of his moms say is going to change that.

"I know," Agatha says.

"I think that's the point of this trial," Lilia says, and everyone looks at her. "It's not just about Rio forgiving herself, but all three of you forgiving yourselves… and each other," Lilia says. "You all need to let go of the past, so that you can move on, find harmony, together," Lilia says and as she speaks Westview fades away and they are back in the clearing they were in when they first appeared in the trial.

"We're back where we started," Alice realises.

"But no exit, or memory," Jen says as the ground starts to rumble.

"That's because Lilia's right," Agatha says, saying words she wouldn't have said not too long ago. "All three of us have guilt, all three of us have pain, but we need to move forward, we need to be in harmony with each other," Agatha says. "I am sorry about the choices I made that kept us apart, I am sorry for the unjust hate and anger I felt towards you," Agatha says to Rio. "And I'm sorry that I wasn't there for you. I'm sorry that I missed so much of your life," Agatha says to Nicky, tears coming to her eyes.

"I forgive you Mama," Nicky assures her. "And I'm sorry that I didn't figure out how to break the spell sooner," Nicky admits. "I'm sorry that I couldn't bring you back together sooner," Nicky tells his moms.

"I forgive you Nicky," Rio tells her son, even though she doesn't feel he needs to be she can appreciate that he needs to hear the words. "And I forgive you, Agatha," Rio says, looking at her. "I am sorry that I couldn't spare you all those years ago, that I had to take you," Rio tells Nicky. "And I am sorry that I couldn't find you, stop you; I'm sorry that we were apart for so long because I couldn't put us back together," Rio says, as she looks between Nicky and Agatha.

"I forgive you Mom," Nicky says.

"I forgive you, Rio, and you Nicky," Agatha says, and as soon as she says the words the three of them embrace, holding each other tight as they all finally let go of guilt, and pain, they have been carrying around for a very long time. "I love you, I love you both, so much," Agatha says as she holds the two people who she loves most.

"And we love you too," Nicky says.

"So much," Rio adds, and as she does Jen, Lilia and Alice see, to their relief, the way out of the trial appears.

"The exit," Alice says, pointing to it. "We should go," Alice says and as they hear her words Agatha, Rio, and Nicky break apart, and almost feeling lighter, the family of three and their Coven, head out of the trial together; knowing they still have a lot to deal with, to come to terms with, but they just took a huge first step.

A couple of hours, or at least that’s what it feels like even though time moves differently on The Road, after Alice had a nightmare Agatha, who didn’t go back to sleep is collecting more water for everyone.

While filling the water containers Agatha closes her eyes and lost focuses on the feeling of the soil beneath her feet, of the gentle wind blowing. “I’m not lying,” Lilia says, and Agatha turns to look at her. “In the old days Covens were true sisterhoods. Even if we didn’t completely understand each other’s specific magic, we looked out for each other, protected each other,” Lilia reveals. “It was understood that if one of us were hurt we were all hurt,” Lilia says.
