“I know; I’m sorry about that,” Lilia tells her. “Agatha, you deserved what every other witch born in our time had,” Lilia tells Agatha, who has to fight back her emotions at that, as she doesn’t want to admit that Lilia’s words are actually getting to her. “You deserved a coven who helped you instead of hurt you, who did everything they could to understand your powers not be afraid of them, and I’m sorry that you never had that,” Lilia tells Agatha.

“I… thank you,” Agatha says, turning away from Lilia so that the older woman doesn’t see the tears in her eyes, and the two of them drift into silence as they stand together, Lilia knowing there is something else she wants to offer Agatha, but as she doesn’t want to overwhelm her she doesn’t make the offer, and instead just makes a note of it so that she can make it at a better time.

While Agatha is with Lilia Nicky had walked over to his mom, who is watching everyone from a distance like she tends to do, and once he is close enough, he sits down with her.

“You okay?” Rio asks her son, as she knows the time of the Road has been rather intense, and because of that she wants to make sure he is okay.

“Yeah,” Nicky responds. “Mom, I destroyed a ghost,” Nicky says to her, still feeling rather amazed by that.

“I know,” Rio responds.

“How did I destroy a ghost?” Nicky asks, as that is something he is still confused about.

“I’m still tyring to figure that out,” Rio admits. “Why don’t you tell me what happened,” Rio suggests, feeling that Nicky’s explanation about what he did could give her son real insight into what happened, and maybe help her figure it out.

“Um, so I already had my knife in my hand, just in case, figured it was the smart choice,” Nicky admits.

“It was,” Rio confirms, feeling glad that he had enough sense to do that.

“Yeah, that became clear,” Nicky admits. “I wasn’t even thinking about what I was doing,” Nicky admits. “All I knew is that Evanora was flying towards me, she was going to possess me again, and I couldn’t let that happen, not again,” Nicky reveals, and as he does Rio notices exactly what he said.

“Again?” Rio asks concerned.

“That was how I got below the Road, she possessed me and threw me into the swamp,” Nicky explains.

“Nicky, I’m so sorry that happened,” Rio tells her son, adding that to the list of many, many, reasons why she hates Evanora Harkness.

“It wasn’t as bad as hearing her talk about mama,” Nicky admits, clearly pained about that, and because she knows Evanora Rio can guess just how awful that would have been. “The things she was saying….” Nicky starts to say, before trailing off. “I knew that if she had another chance, she was going to use me to hurt Mama, again, and I wasn’t going to let that happen,” Nicky admits. “So, when she came towards me, I just stabbed,” Nicky explains. “At first, I didn’t think anything happened, but then I felt my magic, felt it encircle the blade, and spread through her, and then she was gone, and I was blown backwards,” Nicky explains, and as he does Rio considers what her son said so that she can make sense of things.

“It was both parts of you that allowed you to destroy her,” Rio realises. “The magic you got from me, and the magic you got from Mama,” Rio realised. “It combined with your heart, the desire you had to protect your mama, in a way so uniquely you to do the impossible,” Rio admits. “I’m so proud of you,” Rio tells her son.

“Thanks Mom,” Nicky responds. “Mom, the things Evanora was saying to me about Mama, she said them to mama before, hadn’t she?” Nicky asks, wanting to know, but not wanting to cause his Mama more pain by asking her directly.

“Probably,” Rio says, as while she can’t be sure without knowing exactly what Evanora said also knows enough to know that anything Evanora said to Nicky she likely said to Agatha.

“That’s awful,” Nicky says, growing.

“That’s Evanora,” Rio responds simply.

“I get it now, why you never talked about it,” Nicky admits. “She doesn’t deserve our thoughts, our energy, Mama does,” Nicky admits.

“Yeah, she does,” Rio says, as she notices Agatha and Llia walk back into the clearly. As they do Rio sees the look on Agatha’s face, the look she is trying to hide, and because of that she can’t help but feel concerned because she knows what it means. Due to knowing what the look means Rio is glad when Agatha walks straight over to them, and sits down with them. “You okay?” Rio asks in a quiet voice.

“Later,” Agatha tells Rio, also in a quiet voice, as she wants to protect Nicky from what she is feeling. “So, birthday cake in bed, any other traditions I should know about?” Agatha asks curious, wanting to catch up on what she has missed out on.

“Well, it’s not really a tradition, but I like cooking when Mom’s doing her job,” Nicky reveals. “Actually… I just like cooking, I do it a lot,” Nicky reveals.

“He’s really good at it,” Rio reveals, and Nicky smiles proudly.

“Good to know,” Agatha says, and as she does, she realises something. “Those baked goods at my house, you made them?” Agatha asks, as she assumes that made sense.

“Yeah, I brought you food whenever I could… usually when I made too much,” Nicky admits.

“Thank you,” Agatha tells her son.

“I also don’t have a bedtime,” Nicky says. “Mom lets me stay up as late as I want doing whatever I want,” Nicky says, and Rio laughs at that, as Agatha gives her a disapproving look.

“That’s not true,” Rio assures Agatha. “But I appreciate you trying to pull that,” Rio tells Nicky.

“Had to try,” Nicky says with a shrug.

“If we didn’t give Nicky a bedtime, he would stay up all night reading and then sleep in school,” Rio explains to Agatha, who suspects that that is such a specific detail that it likely happened, as while she is pretty lax when it comes rules bedtime is actually one, she usually tends to be pretty strict about, even if she makes exceptions for certain occasions.

“Good to know,” Agatha admits. “So, I guess we can expect to have you try asking both of us the same thing so that you can get the answer you want,” Agatha realises.

“I mean, isn’t that exactly what you’d want me to do?” Nicky asks, looking between his moms, knowing them well enough to know that.

“Yeah,” Rio admits, and she is a little amused that Nicky realised that.

“Which is why we’re going to make sure we are on the same page,” Agatha says, knowing that that is what they decided when Nicky was first born so it’s something they’ll continue.

“This is going to be fun,” Nicky says amused.

“You might want to remember you said that,” Agatha tells her son, as she doesn’t need Lilia’s powers to know that the day is gong to come where Nicky regrets being happy about his moms being on the same page.

“I’m sure the two of you will remind me,” Nicky says.

“Yep,” Agatha and Rio say together, and Nicky smiles, as this is what he has wanted every day for the last eight years, his moms to be together again, for the three of them to be together.

While Nicky, Rio, and Agatha are off on their own talking, getting to finally spend some time together, Jen, Alice and Lilia are off on the other side of the clearing.

“We should probably get going to the next task,” Jen says to the others in a quiet voice.

“We should, but do you want to be the one to tell them that?” Lilia asks, clearly referring to Agatha, Rio, and Lilia.

“We shouldn’t have to. They should know, we’re here for a reason, we shouldn’t put everything on hold because of them, it’s not fair, they should know that,” Jen says annoyed, and once she does Alice reaches out and puts a comforting hand on her leg.

“Hey, it will be okay,” Alice assures her, being able to tell that Jen is tensed because she is worried about what is going to happen. “So, how about we give them a few more minutes together,” Alice suggests.

“Fine, but you have to be the one to tell them we’ve got to move on,” Jen tells Alice, though it is clear to Lilia that Alice’s touch has relaxed her a little.

“Deal,” Alice responds.

Even though she got the others to agree to a few minutes it is closer to ten minutes before Alice gets up and walks over to where Agatha, Rio, and Nicky are sitting.

“Um, so, we Jen, Lilia and I think it’s time for us to move onto the next trial,” Alice tells the trio.

“Yeah, probably is,” Agatha reveals.

“This will be the last one right?” Nicky asks his moms. “So, when we exit it, we exit the road?” Nicky asks, knowing that they will know because of their previous experience.

“No, we exit back onto the Road, and then walk a little more before our true exit will be revealed and we get what we want, what’s missing,” Agatha explains to her son, knowing they may face one more thing before then, but that is up to the Road.

“Okay,” Nicky says, as he, and both his mothers, standing up, as do Lilia and Jen.

Once everyone is standing, they walk over to one another and once again, as a coven, they start to walk down the Road, Lilia feeling nervous about what her trial is going to be.

Chapter 32

Chapter 32

AN: So, considering how amazing Lilia’s trial was on the show I was extremely nervous about how to write it, so I hope you like what I came up with.

Thank you so much for the support. Hope you like this chapter, will post the next chapter in about 12 hours, then another chapter before I go to bed. Due to the fact that I have to go into the office on Monday I will only update one chapter Monday then post the last of the chapters on Tuesday.

For a few minutes, or at least that’s what it feels like for them, after Nicky asked his moms what happened when they finish this task the group, the coven, continue to walk together, following the almost yellow path, until they finally see a structure in the distance. Exchanging looks the group continue to walk until they see just what the structure is.

“A castle?” Nicky asks surprised, as he certainly was not expecting that.

“Apparently,” Lilia says, feeling even more nervous, as she can’t imagine that means something good for her trial.

“Whenever you’re ready, we are too,” Alice tells Lilia in a reassuring voice as she remembers how nervous she was about her trial and because of that she completely understands if Lilia wants to take a moment before entering.

“I’m ready,” Lilia says, and she takes a deep breath before taking the last few steps before getting to the door and opening it, walking into the castle with the others followed behind her.

As soon as she walks though the threshold of the castle Lilia sees a bright light and once the light fades away, she realises two things, the first is that she is completely alone, and the second is that she is dressed up as Glinda the Good Witch.

“This is so insulting,” Lilia mutters, but as she knows she cannot change that fact she doesn’t dwell on it.

As she can’t change what she is dressed at Lilia instead looks around the room and realises she is in what appears to be a chamber in a castle. Looking around the room she sees a stone table. Assuming the table has something to do with her task Lilia walks over to it and sees that there is a stack of tarot cards, seven spots that are clearly the right size for tarot cards, and each of the spots has words carved in front of them;

“The Goal, The Guiding Hand, The Soul, The Strength, the Heart, The Conscience, the Ultimate Destination,” Lilia reads, running her hand over each of the words. “Now what do I do?” Lilia asks, as it’s not perfectly clear what she is going to have to do; though she could make a few guesses.

“Has it been so long that you’ve forgotten?” A familiar voice says, and Lilia turns to the shadows where the voice is coming from.

“Who’s there?” Lilia asks, feeling both comforted and worried about what she hears.

“A reminder,” the voice says again and a person who meant so much to her, her Maestra, walks out from the shadows.

“A reminder? Of what? Of how I failed?” Lilia asks, as that is the first thing she thinks of when she sees her Maestra, how she failed her.

“Of what you once were, and can be again,” her Maestra says, walking towards Lilia. “You just need to remember your lessons, your responsibilities, remember your craft…. Remember yourself,” her Maestra tells Lilia and even though Lilia has a thousand questions she doesn’t get a chance to answer them as her Maestra fades away.

“Thanks for another cryptic lesson,” Lilia says, though even if it was just for a few seconds, it means a lot to see her Maestra again; even if it did make her feel like a teenager again.

Turning back to the table Lilia realises what she needs to do, and because of that she picks up the first of the tarot cards.

“Queen of Cups,” Lilia reads. “Empathetic, intuitive, inner voice to be trusted,” Lilia recites, and as she looks between the cards, and the words on the table, it’s like everything falls into place and she knows exactly what to do. “The guiding hand,” Lilia says. “Me,” Lilia says before putting the card in the right spot.

As soon as Lilia puts the card down, she feels the entire room sway, and a door appears, very similar to how the arches appeared during Rio’s trail, except her doors are old, almost familiar. Assuming that it is what she has to do to complete the task Lilia leaves everything on the table and walks through the door.

Walking through the door Lilia finds herself back in her past, a garden she spent a lot of time learning her craft in, and once again she sees Maestra sitting at a table where once Lilia spent a lot of time.

“You’ve taken the first step,” Lilia’s Maestra says to her, clearly well aware of what is going on.

“The first step to what?” Lilia asks, as she approaches her Maestra.

“To becoming who you’re meant to be, to becoming who you’ve have hid from,” Lilia’s Maestra says to her.

“I’m not meant to be anything,” Lilia says, as over the centuries she has come to believe that, come to believe that she is just a forgotten old woman.

“Are you sure about that?” Lilia’s Maestra asks, giving Lilia a look which Lilia knows to mean ‘are you sure?’. “What card brought you here?” Maestra asks, in a tone that makes it clear that she already knows what Lilia is about to say.

“Queen of cups…. The guiding hand,” Lilia remembers. “Are you saying I have to guide the others?” Lilia asks surprised, as she tries to figure out what is actually being said beneath the clues she is receiving.

“I’m not saying anything, the universe is,” Maestra admits. “The question is whether you have the courage to embrace what you are being shown or turn away from it, again,” Maestra tells Lilia, who feels hesitant as she realises something.

“I don’t know if I could handle losing everything again,” Lilia admits, as loosing her coven the first time broke her, destroyed her, and she isn’t sure she can handle that again.

“Death comes for us all,” Maestra tells Lilia. “You need to decide whether you a prepared to have regrets when your time comes,” Maestra tells Lilia.

“I already have regrets,” Lilia admits.

“Do you really want to add more?” Maestra asks, and Lilia considers the words.

For a few moments Lilia and her Maestra are both silent as Lilia considers what she has been told, considers the implications and what it would mean, and after a few moments, just as Lilia comes to a a decision, a door appears again.

“I see you’ve made your decision,” Lilia’s Maestra tells her. “You have an inner voice to be trusted, allow that to guide you, and those around you,” Lilia’s Maestra says, clearly wanting to give one more piece of advice.

“Thank you,” Lilia says, thanking her not just for what just happened, but everything the older woman has done for her, before heading back through the door.

Seconds after she walked through the door in her past Lilia finds herself back in the chamber she started in, and feeling a newfound confidence Lilia walks back over to the table and without hesitation picks up another tarot card.

“Three of Swords,” Lilia reads. “Heartbreak, sorrow, Grief,” Lilia recites from memory, looking between the cards, and the table, and as she does the answer comes to her. “Agatha… the soul,” Lilia says, as she places the card down, and just like the last time she placed a card down as soon as she does the room sways and another door appears, a door which, without even thinking about it, Lilia walks through.

As she finds herself on the others side of the door Lilia isn’t surprised to find herself in a location she doesn’t recognize, as considering what happened when she put down the tarot card that symbolised her, she has to assume that she is in a locations significant to Agatha.

Trying to figure out exactly where she is, and assuming that she will find Agatha somewhere, Lilia looks around, and as she does, she realises that she is in what appears to be a cellar, or basement, and judging by some of the things she sees Lilia assumes it is a cellar from the late 1600s.

As she looks around Lilia hears sniffling, crying, and knowing exactly who it is Lilia heads towards the sound where she finds Agatha, who looks to be a teenager, huddled in a corner, blood on her face, in a dirty dress, clearly terrified.

“Agatha?” Lilia asks, hesitantly, as she walks towards her, having no idea what the rules are, whether she can get hurt, but also knowing she doesn’t want to cause Agatha more fear.

“Who…. Who are you?” Agatha asks in a scared voice, so different to the Agatha who Lilia has gotten to know, and truthfully it makes her incredibly uncomfortable to hear the infamous Agatha Harkness so afraid.

“It’s me, Lilia,” Lilia says, walking closer, but stopping when she is several steps away from her, as she doesn’t want to overwhelm her more than she already is. “I’m a witch too,” Lilia says, it being the first thing she can think to say that may get Agatha to trust her.

“Did my mother send you?” Agatha asks, bringing her legs up to her chest, clearly trying to make herself as small as possible, and as she does Lilia sees the bruises, both old and new, covering Agatha’s legs.

“No,” Lilia tells her, fighting back the feeling of being sick when she realises that some of the bruises that are on Agatha’s legs were clearly made by fingers. “I’m here to help you, Agatha,” Lilia tells her.

“I do not deserve help,” Agatha says, sounding so sure of that, and Lilia can’t help but wonder how many times Evanora Harkness said those words to Agatha, and what she did to make Agatha believe her.

“Yes, you do,” Lilia assures her. “You deserve help, and support, you deserve love, and friendship, and family,” Lilia tells her.

“But I am evil,” Agatha tells Lilia, clearly believing that.

“No, you’re not,” Lilia tells her. “You have magic you can’t control, but that’s nor your fault, you were never taught how to use it properly,” Lilia says. “If you’d let me, I’d like to try to tech you,” Lilia says, as while she can’t guarantee she is going to be able to help Agatha she wants to try.

“Mother is always saying I cannot be taught, that I cannot be good,” Agatha tells Lilia.

“That’s not true,” Lilia tells her. “Agatha, if you come with me, we can work together, I can help you,” Lilia says, suspecting that as soon as they walk out of the ‘cellar’ present day Agatha will be back with her. “Will you let me help you?” Lilia asks, sticking out her hand for Agatha to take.

For a moment Lilia is sure that Agatha isn’t going to take her hand, something which isn’t surprising considering the trust issues Agatha understandably has, that she is going to stay lost in her past, but then Agatha reaches out and takes her hand. As soon as Agatha and takes Lilia’s hand the door appears.

“That’s for us, are you ready to go?” Lilia asks.

“I think so,” Agatha says, struggling to her feet, and together with Lilia the two of them head out of the past together.

Just as Lilia suspected as soon as she and Agatha leave the task Agatha is herself, but she is wearing the costume of the Wicked Witch of the West.

“Are you alright?” Lilia asks, as it is clear that Agatha has remembered everything that has just happened.

“Fine,” Agatha responds, looking around, clearly not wanting to talk about what they just experienced. “Where are the others?” Agatha asks, wanting to see Nicky and Rio especially, but she is also a little worried about the others.

“I’m not sure, but I think I think we are gong to come together one at a time,” Lilia admits, as that is what makes sense. “Agatha, I meant what I said, I will do everything I can to help you gain control of your ability; to give you the help, mentorship, you should have gotten a long time ago,” Lilia tells Agatha, wanting to make that clear.

“Ah… thank you,” Agatha responds, having no idea how to feel about that, still feeling like she doesn’t deserve that. “We should probably get the next person back,” Agatha says, hoping it will be either Nicky or Rio.

“Yeah, we should,” Lilia says, and she walks back over to the table and picks up another tarot card. “The Knight of Wands,” Lilia reads “Full of fire, Fights Bravery,” Lilia says, looking at Agatha as she speaks.

“Alice,” Lilia and Agatha say together, both realising who that description fits.

“The strength,” Lilia says, as she puts the card down, and just like every other time she has put a card down the chamber sways and a door appears.

“Is that for you? Or for both of us?” Agatha asks, knowing that it is Lilia’s trial, so it would make sense if it is just for her.

“Both, we need to do this together,” Lilia says, as she knows that that’s one of the lessons she is being taught, that she cannot do everything alone, that she doesn’t have to.

“Then lead the way,” Agatha says and together she and Lilia walk through the door, neither knowing what they ae going to be facing on the other side, but knowing that whatever it is they have to help Alice face it, just like Lilia helped Agatha.

After walking through the door, it takes both Lilia and Agatha a few seconds to realise where they are, but it quicky becomes clear that they are outside a hotel fire; leading both Lilia and Agatha to realise where, or more specifically, when they are.

“We’ve got to find her,” Agatha says, trying to hide the panic in her voice as she knows what the Alice of this time would be going though.

“I know,” Lilia says, and the two older witches quickly start to look around, looking for any sign of Alice. “There!” Lilia says, seeing Alice sitting alone, a way from anyone else, with a body bag next to her when a person who both Lilia and Agatha realise is a part of Alice’s mothers bad, walks over to her.

“Alice, we’ve got another hotel if you’d like to come with us,” the band member says.

“I’m fine,” Alice responds, and both Agath and Lilia recognize signs that tell them that she is trying to hold it together, that she isn’t wanting to be seen falling apart.

“Are you sure? We’ve got plenty of room, your mom…”

“Is gone,” Alice says, an edge to her voice. “I want to be alone,” Alice says, causing both Agatha and Lilia to exchange looks, as they very much doubt it.

“Okay,” the band member says. “Here’s a card, if you change your mind,” The band member says, and Alice takes it without a word. “I’m sorry, Alice,” The band member says, before walking away.

After watching the band member walk away Agatha and Lilia exchange looks, and realising what they need to do they walk over to Alice and sit down next to her, Lilia sitting next to her and Agatha sitting down next to Lilia.

“Why won’t you people leave me the hell alone, I want to be alone,” Alice says annoyed, both Liila and Agatha being able to see through the cracks which tell them she is barely holding it together.

“No, you don’t,” Lilia says, and Alice turns to look at her with an angry look on her face.

“How the hell do you know?” Alice asks angrily.

“Because I’ve been you, we both have,” Lilia says. “So afraid of losing someone else, or being betrayed, that you don’t let anyone close because you figure it will be easier,” Lilia says to Alice.

“Isn’t it?” Alice asks, as that’s what she assumes.

“No,” Lilia, and to Lilia’s surprise, Agatha, say.

“It just makes you lonely,” Agatha says, clearly speaking from her own experience.

“You can convince yourself that you don’t need anyone, that you can’t count on anyone, because you think it’s easier, but it’s not; it just makes you hurt in a different way,” Lilia admits. “No one is meant to go through life alone, and you don’t have to, Alice,” Lilia tells her. “You have people, a coven, a family, who want to be there for you, you just have to let us,” Lilia tells her. “You are incredibly strong, brave, full of fire, but the thing about fire is it burns when left alone; don’t let it burn you, let us in, let us be your coven,” Lilia tells the younger witch. “You don’t have to be alone anymore,” Lilia tells her, and for a few moments she isn’t sure her words have gotten through to Alice, but then they see a door appears.

“That’s our way out,” Agatha says. “You coming Alice?” Agatha asks, knowing that as hard as she and Lilia may try it ultimately has to be Alice’s choice to accept what they are saying.

“Where to?” Alice asks.

“To where you don’t have to be alone,” Lilia answers.

“A place like that exists?” Alice asks, almost like she can’t quiet believe that.

“It does,” Lilia says, standing up, and just like she did with Agatha she sticks out her hand for Alice to take, which she does.

Once Alice has taken Lilia’s hand Agatha stands up too, and together the trip head through the door together.

Seconds after they left Alice’s past Lilia, Agatha, and Alice who is now dressed as Morgan Le Fey, find themselves in the chamber once more.

“Did you mean it?” Alice asks Lilia, once she realises where they are and what has happened.

“Every word,” Lilia responds, and she isn’t at all surprised when Alice glances at Agatha.

“Rio and I already agreed that we’re going to look out for you when we get out of here,” Agatha says, and while it is clear that both Lilia and Alice are surprised by that it is equally as clear that they are both very glad to hear that. “You’re not getting rid of us, Kid,” Agatha assures her, as while Alice isn’t actually that young, compared to how old Agatha, Lilia, and even Jen, she is.

Hearing the words, looking between the two older women, older witches, standing before her Alice feels what she hasn’t felt since her mother died; looked after. Looking between Agatha and Lilia, and knowing it applies to Rio too, Alice realises that while she has lost her mother, and no one can every completely replace her, she has people who will look after her, want to care about her, be there for her, just like her mother would if she could, and that is something she long ago accepted she would never have again.

“Thank you,” Alice says before walking forward and hugging both Agatha and Lilia hug at the same time, and together three witches who have been alone for a long time, who long ago forced themselves to believe that they are better off alone, realise that they don’t have to be alone anymore; they just need to find the courage to believe that.

Chapter 33

AN: Thank you so much for the support you give I so very much appreciate it. I will be posting one more chapter tonight, then tomorrow I will post one chapter in the afternoon before posting the last two chapters on Tuesday my time (Australia)

Having no idea how long they have been holding each other, as time seemingly fades away, Lilia, Agatha and Alice allow them to feel what they long ago accepted they didn’t need, that that they believed they didn’t want, but then Lilia realises that they need to continue going.

“We need to get the others,” Lilia says looking between Agatha and Alice as they break apart. “We need them too,” Lilia says.

“And they need us,” Alice realises, and Lilia nods.

“It’s your show, Lilia, we’re here for support,” Agatha says, as that has become perfectly clear.

“I know,” Lilia says, feeling incredibly grateful for that, and she once again walks over to the table, Agatha and Alice doing the same and standing either side of her, offering her silent support.

Once at the table Lilia once again picks up another card, and this time the one that she picks up is upside down. “The tower… reversed,” Lilia explains.

“What does that mean?” Alice asks, as while she doesn’t know a lot about tarot, she knows that a card being reversed changes the meaning.

“Upright it means disaster, destruction, sudden upheaval,” Lilia reveals, looking at Alice. “But when it’s reversed it means miraculous transformation,” Lilia explains, looking at Agatha.

“Nicky,” Agatha says, remembering what Lilia said to her and Rio earlier, and that makes her both worried about what is going to happen to her son, but also very interested to see.

“The Heart,” Lilia says, putting the card down in the right spot, and as soon as it is gone the room once again sways and another door appears. As they know exactly what they need to do the trio exchange looks and without a word head through the door, Agatha very much looking forward to seeing her son, even if she is worried about what kind of state she is going to find him in.

As soon as they walk through the door Lilia, Agatha, and Alice are all incredibly confused, because they are back on the Road, but as they look around, they see Nicky digging Sharon’s grave, which tells them they are before they summoned Rio.

“I don’t understand, why are we here?” Alice asks confused, and it is clear that Lilia is just as confused, while Agatha isn’t as she realises exactly why they would be brough to this particular time and place.

“Nicky knew Sharon was going to die,” Agatha reveals, causing both Lilia and Alice to look at her, it being clear that both are surprised by that. “Because he’s Rio’s son he can sense when someone is going to die, only when there is no chance of survival, and he can sense when a lot of people have died in the same place,” Agatha explains, feeling that considering it is Lilia’s trial she needs to know that, but also not wanting to break her son’s confidence. “He’s struggling with that,” Agath admits, it being clear that she doesn’t like that her son is struggling, but she isn’t completely sure the best way to help him.

“I see,” Lilia says, and without waiting for the others she walks over to where Nicky is digging the grave. “Nicky,” Lilia says, and she isn’t surprised when he looks at her with a look of complete shock on his face.

“Lilia? You know who I am?” Nicky asks shocked. “How?” Nicky asks, as from his perspective the Sigil is still in place.

“I’m not from this moment, I’m from a little way in the future,” Lilia says, feeling that is the best way to explain, and considering the circumstances, and she figures that considering how he’s grown up Nicky likely won’t been too overwhelmed with the situation.

“We all are,” Agatha says, causing Nicky to look at her and realise just who is with Lilia.

“Mama?” Nicky asks amazed, as for him this is the first time his mother knew who he actually was since he was seven.

“Hi Sweetheart,” Agatha says, smiling back at him. “We’re here to help you,” Agatha assures him, and as she does Nicky looks between the grave he is digging and the three people standing before him.

“Do you know what I did?” Nicky asks, clearly nervous, clearly worried about what they are going to say, and think of him.

“We do,” Agatha says, even if technically only she does. “She was going to die anyway, there was nothing you could do to change that, you brought her some peace,” Agatha tells her son, causing the pieces to fall into place for Lilia and Alice.

“It doesn’t feel like peace,” Nicky admits. “I really hate this ability,” Nicky admits, as he hates that he knows when people are going to die and there is nothing, he can do to save them.

“I understand,” Agatha tells her son, as while she does understand she also knows it’s something she never, ever, wanted for him.

“So do I,” Lilia assures Nicky. “Nicky I’ve been where you are, I know what it’s like to know tragedy is coming and be powerless to stop it,” Lilia tells him.

“How do you handle it?” Nicky asks, as right now he doesn’t think he is going to ever be able to handle it.

“For a long time I didn’t,” Lilia admits, feeling that it is important to tell him the truth. “I shut it down, buried that part of myself…. And I lost myself because of that,” Lilia says, taking a step forward. “I’m telling you this because I don’t want the same for you,” Lilia tells him. “No good comes from hating apart of yourself, of being so ashamed of yourself that you lose yourself,” Lilia says.

“She’s right, trust me on that,” Agatha says to her son. “Nicky, I know your ability to sense death is painful, and maybe even frightening, but it’s also apart of you, apart of you that you need to learn about, understand, embrace,” Agatha tells her son, saying to him what she wishes someone, anyone, had told her when she was Nicky’s age.

“What if I don’t know how?” Nicky asks, looking between Lilia and Agatha.

“Then we’ll help you figure it out,” Liila tells him. “You’re at the beginning of your journey, of your transformation, don’t cut your journey short because it’s painful,” Lilia tells him. “You’re not alone, Nicholas,” Lilia tells him.

“I forgot everything my mom taught me, pushed it all down, and I regret that, don’t be like me,” Alice tells Nicky. “We can figure this out, you just have to be wiling to try,” Alice tells him.

“Nicky, you are not alone, you are never alone,” Agatha promises her son. “Let us help you figure out what your abilities mean, and how to use them, don’t push them down; don’t be ashamed of them,” Agatha tells her son, wanting better for him than what she experienced. “Please don’t be that much like me,” Agatha tells her son.

“I…” Nicky starts to say, but because no words can explain what he is feeling he walks over and hugs his mother tightly.

As Agatha and Nicky hug Lilia and Alice watch on, and as they do neither are sure what they can do, but then they see the door appear, which tells them Nicky has come to a decision, he has decided to accept himself a little more.

“Agatha, the door,” Lilia tells her, and as she does Agatha breaks apart from her son.

“I’m really proud of you,” Agatha tells her son.

“Thanks Mama,” Nicky says amazed.

“Let’s get our of here,” Alice says, and together the group head back through the door.

As soon as they walk through the door Lilia, Agatha, Alice and Nicky find themselves back in the chamber of the castle. Just like the others Nicky has been transformed into a costume; in his case it is Maleficent.

“Are you okay?” Agatha asks her son concerned, wanting to make sure he is okay.

“I think so,” Nicky says, though he isn’t completely sure. “Where are Mom and Jen?” Nicky asks, looking around and not seeing them.

“We haven’t got them yet,” Lilia explains. “This is a one at a time kind of thing,” Lilia explains.

“Guess that makes sense,” Nicky admits, though he does really want to see his mom. .

“Let’s see who we are getting next,” Lilia says, though she suspects that, because of who Rio is, that she will be the last, and she walks over to the table and picks up the next card, leaving two still in the deck. “The High Priestess,” Lilia reads. “Immense Spiritual Power, unable or unwilling to use it,” Lilia receipts. “The Conscience… Jen,” Lilia says, placing the card down, leaving the spots labelled the ultimate destination and the goal left to be filled.

“I guess we walk through that,” Nicky says when the room sways and a door appears.

“Yep,” Alice confirms, as Lilia heads to the door and the others follow behind, Agatha making sure to stay close to her son as she wants to make sure he is okay, as they go.

Just like all the other times before as soon as they exit the door the group find themselves in a different location, this time on the outskirts of a town that Agatha recognizes.

“Where is she? Where is Jen?” Alice asks worried, as she looks around and sees no sign of her.

“Over there, behind the trees, trying to hide from the villagers,” Agatha explains, knowing that, and no one questions how she knows that they just follow what she said.

Just like Agatha said they would the group quickly finds Jen sitting alone, clearly upset, staring at her hands, only Agatha noticing the blade tucked into her sleeve, why she sits by the fire, which makes everyone, except for Agatha who already realised, suspect they know exactly when this memory is taking place.

“Jen,” Lilia says, in a gentle voice, as she approaches her.

“Who are you? What do you want” Jen asks in a frightened voice, as Agatha purposely takes several steps back as she knows that right now the last thing Jen, from this time period, needs is to see her.

“My names Lilia, I want to help you,” Lilia explains, feeling that that is the best place to start.

“I don’t know if I can be helped,” Jen admits.

“You can be, because you help others, because that’s who you are,” Lilia assures Jen. “Your magic is powerful, yes, but it’s not your only power,” Lilia tells her. “Your knowledge, your heart, the moral centre you have within you, that’s also powerful; you’re powerful, even without your magic,” Lilia says, feeling that it is important that Jen all parts of herself.

“I want my magic back,” Jen admits.

“I know,” Lilia tells her. “But before you get it back you need to accept that you don’t need it, that you’re powerful without it, and that it’s just one part of you,” Lilia tells Jen, as it is clear to her that while Nicky needs to accept the magical part of himself Jen needs to accept the non-magical part of herself; they both need to accept their whole selves, not just parts of them.

“You don’t know me yet,” Alice says, walking towards her. “But I think you’re pretty incredible, and I don’t know you with your magic,” Alice says, trying to help. “I can see how incredible you are, you need to see it for yourself,” Alice says.

“I don’t know you, and I’m meant to believe you?” Jen asks, feeling doubtful about that, and because of that Agatha knows what she has to do.

“You do know me,” Agatha says, taking several steps forward.

“Agatha?” Jen asks shocked, it being clear that Agatha is the last person she expected to see.

“The one and only,” Agatha says. “Look Jen, I may find you insufferable, but even I know that everything that is being said is true, and you should listen for once,” Agatha tells her.

“You need to accept all of yourself Jen,” Nicky says, saying the same things Lilia said to him, feeling that Is the best thing to say considering what his Mama just said.

“It’s the only way for you to understand where your magic fits within you, not how you fit your magic,” Lilia tells her, feeling that that is an important distinction.

“I’ve never thought about it like that,” Jen admits. “But I’ll try to,” Jen admits.

“That’s the best any of us can do,” Alice says, giving her an encouraging look, and as she does the door appears.

“What’s that?” Jen asks, referring to the door.

“Your future,” Lilia says, offering her hand to Jen, who takes it and the group once again head through the door.

Just like every time everyone has returned to the room they have turned back into their costumes, which in Jen’s cast is the Evil Queen from Snow White.

“Serious? What are with the costumes?” Jen asks annoyed, as she looks at not only hers, but the ones the others are wearing.

“Don’t ask,” Lilia responds, clearly annoyed.

“It’s time for Mom now, right?” Nicky asks, as it is clear that he wants to see his mom again.

“There are two cards left, one is the goal, the other is the ultimate destination,” Lilia explains.

“I think I can guess which one Rio is going to be,” Agatha admits, as out of those two options there is only one that make sense considering who Rio is.

“I think so too,” Lilia says, walking over to the tarot table, and she picks up the second last card, and can’t help but laugh when she sees it. “Death,” Lilia says, showing the others.

“A bit on the nose,” Agatha comments, a little amused, as she knows it’s the exact kind of thing Rio would love.

“But no need for interpretation,” Lilia says, as she places the Death card in the spot where the card for the Ultimate Destination goes, and just as they expected the room starts to sway, and a door, which they all walk through, appears.

Unlike every other time in this trial that the group walked through the door they don’t have to go far as they see Rio, clearly waiting, leaning up against a tree.

“Took you long enough,” Rio says, when she notices the group, it being perfectly clear that she has been waiting for them.

“You knew we were coming?” Jen asks, sounding a little surprised by that.

“I’m an all powerful cosmic being… of course I knew,” Rio says, feeling that should be obvious, and Agatha smirks, as she always likes it when Rio makes it clear how powerful she is, though of course she loves ever single part of Rio. “Are you all okay?” Rio asks, trying to make it seem like she doesn’t care.

“Yeah, we’re okay,” Agatha assures her.

“Good,” Rio says, pushing herself off the tree. “So, Lilia, this is your trial, how do we get out of here?” Rio asks, looking at her.

“For the rest of us the door appeared when we accepted something, not just about ourselves, but about us as a collective,” Lilia realises. “What do you need to accept?” Lilia asks, and only Agatha recognizes the signs of Rio starting to become uncomfortable, as the group drift into a tense silence.

“That you’re allowed to care,” Nicky tells his mom, causing everyone to look at him. “Mom, you’re inevitable, all roads lead to you, nothing can change that, and because of that you’ve only allowed yourself to care about Mama, and Me... but that’s starting to change,” Nicky realises, as he seen that. “You need to give yourself permission to care, you need to tell yourself that it’s okay to care about not only me and Mama,” Nicky realises.

“When did you get so smart?” Rio asks her son, it being perfectly clear that both she and Agatha are proud of their son.

“I’ve always been smart,” Nicky tells his mom.

“You are, but Rio accepting that it’s okay to care, isn’t the only thing that needs to happen for the door to appear,” Agatha says, causing everyone to look at her, wondering what she has realised that the rest of them haven’t. “The rest of us need to accept that Rio’s job is something she can’t control, as painful as it can be when we lose someone, hating her, hating death, won’t help,” Agatha says, staring at Rio as she speaks. “It’s all of our ultimate fate, we all need to accept that, I have,” Agatha says, looking at Rio, and an understanding look passes between them.

“Thank you,” Rio says, in a very quiet voice, as hearing Agatha finally say those words, hearing her finally accept that there are things she cannot change, means everything to her.

“I have no issues with you, except I do questions your taste in romantic partners,” Jen says, causing Agatha to roll her eyes.

“I did blame you, for what happened to my original coven… I don’t anymore,” Lilia admits, speaking quickly before a fight can break out between some combination of Agatha, Rio, Jen, and possibly Nicky.

“After last night we’re good,” Alice assures Rio, who gives a nod, as she realises that it means more than she would have expected it to hear that from Alice and Lilia, and as she realises that the door appears.

“Let’s get out of here,” Nicky says to his mom, and the group once again head through the door that will take them back to the chamber.

As the group walk back into the chamber everyone is once again changed in the costumes, the one exception to that is Rio is changed into her ‘job’ outfit, except she has her regular ‘Rio’ face rather than the skull she usually has when she is in this particular outfit.

“Why didn’t you get an insulting outfit?” Jen asks, seeing what Rio is wearing, and knowing that out of all of them she certainly has the best one.

“Who knows, I guess The Road decided that my work outfit is suitable,” Rio says with a shrug.

“We’re all back together now, so what do we do?” Alice asks confused.

“There is one more card,” Lilia says, walking over to the table. “Three of Pentacles,” Lilia says. “Collaboration, Community, Singular voices waiting to Harmonize,” Lilia says, as she puts the card down in the spot that says, ‘the goal,’.

The second Lilia puts the card down the entire chamber starts to shake, but unlike the previous times where it was just a gentle sway it is a violent shake, it’s like there is strong wind echoing throughout the chamber.

“There’s the way out,” Jen realises, pointing to the door, as everyone struggles to get to their feet.

“How do we get there?” Nicky asks worried, as he isn’t sure if they are going to make it across the chamber.

“Just like the card says, we collaborate,” Lilia realises. “We work together; as one,” Lilia says, as she looks between the others and as she does, she sticks out her hand, which Jen takes, without hesitation, and Alice takes her hand, then Rio takes Alice’s, Nicky takes Rio’s, and Agatha takes Nicky’s.

Once everyone is hand in hand, they all, as one line, start to make their way towards the door. While they are fighting against the shakes, and they are barely able to move, the group are able to slowly make their way across the chamber, as they work as one, until they finally get to the to the door. Once they are at the door Lilia is able to gasp the handle, and using everyone’s weight, because they are working against they wind, they are able to pull the door, yank it open, and finally exit the final trial.

Chapter 34

Chapter 34

AN: Thank you so much for the support. I am going to apologize in advance for the clifthanger this chapter ends on, especially because it will be a while before I can update the next chapter. Hope you enjoy it despite that. Let me know what you think.

Due to the force they used to pull open the door no one is surprised to find that they don’t have the smoothest exit and rather than walking out of the trial they tumble out in a way similar to the way they exited the first trial; which is pretty fitting considering everything.

“Everyone okay?” Lilia asks, being the first one to get her bearings, and as she looks around, she notices that the road doesn’t have a specific colour, but rather it looks like it’s daytime, looks like everything is it’s right colour; a combination of all of them, a representation of how unified they have become.

“Yeah, I think so,” Alice says as she helps Jen to her feet.

“Yep,” Jen confirms.

“Yeah, I’m good,” Nicky says, looking at his moms as he speaks as he knows they would be worried about him.

“Same,” Agatha confirms, feeling glad that Nicky is okay.

“I always am,” Rio assures the others as she looks over both Nicky and Agatha to make sure they are okay.

“So, is this it? we’ve completed all the trials?” Nicky asks, looking between his moms, as he knows that they have completed the trials before so they will know if this is what it is like when they are completed.

“Looks like it,” Agatha says, being able to tell that her powers haven’t come back yet, but knowing from last time that that won’t happen until they are close to leaving the Road, or even not until they leave it completely.

“What happens now?” Alice asks, looking between the others, wondering if they have some answers, because she doesn’t.

“We keep walking, and we’ll find the exit, The Road will give us our prizes, what we want most, as we leave,” Agatha explains.

“What about the Seven?” Nicky asks worried, as he knows that they are still a big concern.

“We can trap them here if we leave. They won’t be able to leave if we leave first,” Rio explains, knowing that because of who she is. “Can you sense them?” Rio asks Nicky, as she is sure that right now, they are against the clock, not against the Road but the Salem Seven, and Nicky closes his eyes.

“They’re not close,” Nicky assures everyone after a few moments, and everyone hope they stay away.

“Which means we’ve got some time, so I need a minute,” Jen says, as after what she experienced, she needs a minute, and so she walks away from the others.

“Jen!” Alice calls, feeling concerned, clearly about to follow her.

“Let me go,” Agatha says, having a suspicion what is going on with her, and because of that she follows Jen before Alice can; to everyone’s confusion.

“Um, anyone else have a bad feeling about that?” Alice asks concerned, as even after everything that has happened it is still perfectly clear that Agatha and Jen do not get along so she can’t imagine anything good happening from the two of them going off on their own.

“A little,” Lilia admits.

“I’m sure it will be fine,” Nicky says, trying to be optimistic, but he is a little worried, and as he tries to reassure the others Rio, who gives her son a reassuring look, walks over to where Alice is standing.

“Are you okay?” Rio asks Alice, as she can tell that she is affected by what happened during Lilia’s trial.

“I think so,” Alice admits, though she isn’t completely sure. “It was just hard being back there, remembering what I felt,” Alice admits, reaching up and wiping a tear away, as while she knows it wasn’t real as she sat by the body bag her mother was once inside her she remembered what she felt when it was real. “Um, so Agatha said that you already agreed to look after me,” Alice says, clearly changing the subject as she really doesn’t want to go down that particular memory road, even with Rio.

“We did,” Rio confirms. “Agatha, Nicky and I haven’t talked about what we’re going to be doing when we leave The Road, how we are going to live, but what I do know is that we have a spare room at our Westview house,” Rio explains. “It’s yours if you want it, whenever you want it,” Rio offers, making it clear that it is Alice’s choice, but it will always be a place for her if she wants it.

“I… thank you,” Alice says amazed, not sure how to respond to that, not sure if she is going to take her up on that offer, but it means everything to her that Rio, and by extension Agatha, made the offer to her.

As she knows Jen pretty well Agatha isn’t at all surprised to find that she has sought out water and is sitting by a creek, running her hands through it. After pausing for a moment to push down the annoyance that Jen is always able to bring out in her, as she knows it won’t do either of them any good right now, Agatha walks over to her.

“Leave me alone, Alice,” Jen’s voice says, without turning around, clearly having heard the footsteps, and Agatha isn’t at all surprised that she assumed Alice would be the one to follow.

“I’m not Alice,” Agatha says, and Jen quickly turns to look at her, the shock she is feeling being perfectly clear on her face.

“Agatha?” Jen asks shocked. “I really didn’t expect you,” Jen admits, feeling suspicious about what she is up to, as in her experience Agatha is always up to something.

“Hove long have you known me? You should know by now that I always do the unexpected,” Agatha says, as she sits down on a rock near, but not too near, where Jen is.

“What the hell do you want, Agatha?” Jen asks annoyed.

“So many things,” Agatha responds, and Jen rolls her eyes. “I thought you might want to talk about what you saw, from someone who was there,” Agatha says.

“You? Talk?” Jen asks, sounding both shocked and annoyed. “Last time I wanted to talk, you slammed a door in my face!” Jen exclaims as she stands up.

“I was going through something,” Agatha says, in way of explanation, even though she knows It’s not much of one.

“You weren’t the only one!” Jen exclaims. “I was too, but of course you didn’t care because for you the world only revolves around Agatha Harkness!” Jen says angrily, and as she has heard a lot worse, including things she has heard from Jen herself, Agatha doesn’t take the words personally. “I came to you for help! I was desperate… and you threw me away… I had nothing left,” Jen says, her voice breaking.

“Is that why you had the knife?” Agatha asks, and Jen looks at her surprised.

“You noticed that?” Jen asks, as she though it was pretty well hidden, she certainly did not expect Agatha to notice.

“Yes, because I knew to look for it,” Agatha explains simply.

“Because you understood why I had it so close?” Jen realises, seeing Agatha in a new light.

“Yes,” Agatha confirms, a mutual understanding passing between them. “But when you bind yourself to death for all eternity a knife isn’t going to do much,” Agatha tells her, and while Jen has a million questions Agatha and Rio tying themselves together that isn’t what she is going to ask about as it’s not the conversation they are having.

“But you still used it,” Jen realises, knowing that without Agatha explicitly saying.

“Yes, but was careful, never let it get so close that Rio would be called. She was the last person I wanted to see after all,” Agatha admits, admitting what she hasn’t told anyone before.

“I felt so weak without my magic…. I still don’t know how he did it,” Jen admits, as she has spent decades trying to figure it out and she still can’t, as she sits down across from Agatha. “Why did you push me away?” Jen asks, finally asking the question she hasn’t asked for so because the time has come where she needs an answer, especially after her conversation with Lilia.

“Because I don’t help people, Jen, I hurt them, you know that,” Agatha tells her, as Jen is one of the people she hurt, there being a sad certainty to Agatha’s voice which tells Jen that that is something she truly believes. “I knew how you felt when you first showed up, it was written all over your face, and while I never felt the same, I still used your feelings for my own goals,” Agatha admits, and that isn’t new information for Jen, she knows Agatha used her, so she doesn’t react to that. “I wanted to believe that I could have an actual friend, wanted to believe that my mother was wrong, and I didn’t corrupt everyone who came close to me, but then you showed up bound…” Agatha starts to say.

“And you thought you ruined me too,” Jen realises.

“I did encourage you to go to Boston,” Agatha reminds her. “I didn’t know what would happen, but it was still my idea,” Agatha explains, as at the time Boston was having a lot of mothers die in childbirth so she truly believed that they could use Jen’s skills, she believed that Jen could save the lives of mothers and their babies. “And between that guilt, and everything that came with having the Darkhold, when you showed back up, I thought it was better to push you away, and make sure you never came back,” Agatha tells Jen.

“You were trying to protect me,” Jen realises, everything making a lot more senses, and she can’t help but wonder if that is what Lilia realised as that would make sense considering how the older witch reacted.

“Seemed like the only thing to do,” Agatha says with a shrug, trying to make it seem like it’s no big deal, and for a few moments they drift into an awkward silence, neither overly sure what to say next considering the; incredibly personal, conversation they just had.

“Did you just call me a friend?” Jen asks, wanting to make sure she heard right, and she figures it’s a good change of subject.

“More like an annoying little sister,” Agatha responds, and Jen picks up a couple of small pebbles which she throws at Agatha. “Very mature,” Agatha says, as she also picks up a couple of pebbles which she throws at Jen, who dodges them, causing both of them to laugh. “Jen, I had hoped that your anger at me would help you keep going,” Agatha admits.

“It did, for a while,” Jen admits, and as she does another look of understanding passes between them. “We should probably get back, everyone else are probably worried we killed each other,” Jen tells Agatha.

“Rio knows we haven’t, but you’re probably right getting back,” Agatha says, standing up. “We’ve got a Road to finish walking down, power to get back,” Agatha says, walking over to Jen and sticking out her hand for her to take.

“That we do,” Jen says, taking Agatha’s hand and once they are both standing up Jen looks at Agatha who looks between them, and an understanding once again passes between them, both of them knowing that their past is not forgotten, but understood.

Why Jen and Agatha are talking Nicky, who is trying to distract himself from worrying about just how their conversation is going as he can’t imagine it going well, has walked over to Lilia, who is sitting on a rock, and sits down next to her.

“Are you okay?” Nicky asks curious, once he is sitting down too, as he knows it must have been intense for her to go through her trial.

“You know what… for the first time in a long time I think I am,” Lilia admits, smiling with a newfound confidence, as for the first time, in a long time, she knows who she truly is, what she should be doing, and what she is apart of.

“That’s awesome,” Nicky admits, being able to tell that Lilia is feeling better and that is amazing to see.

“What about you, Kiddo?” Lilia asks him, turning to look at him, waning to see just how he is doing right now as she knows that considering everything that has happened he has gone through a lot since they started to travel down The Road.

“I don’t know,” Nicky admits, as he is still trying to figure that out, but figures being honest is best. “This whole thing was my plan, and even though the story of when my moms went down the Road last time was my favourite bedtime story, I didn’t expect it to be so… intense,” Nicky admits, having struggled to figure out the right word to use, and Lilia isn’t at all surprised to know that last time Agatha went down the Road Rio was with her, but she does question their judgement when it comes to telling Nicky the story of their journey down The Road as a bedtime story.

“Life has a way of surprising us… especially this place,” Lilia informs Nicky.

“Ain’t that the truth,” Nicky admits, as he looks around. “Lilia, how old were you when you first predicted tragedy?” Nicky asks curious, feeling very interested to know because he knows they have abilities that are similar.

“Young,” Lilia admits. “Probably around seven or eight,” Lilia explains, as she doesn’t remember exactly how old she was because it was so long ago. “What about you?” Lilia asks curious, though considering his current age she can’t imagine Nicky was too old when he first sensed death.

“Not long after I turned eight,” Nicky explains. “It was a bird at first, but then Mom and I went to London, and I touched someone, a random lady walking down the street, and I knew,” Nicky says sadly, knowing he will never forget what he felt in that moment. “For the four years that followed we moved so much that it didn’t happen much, but then when we got to Westview it happened a little more,” Nicky admits.

“And you didn’t know how to handle it,” Lilia realises, feeling that that is a completely understandable reaction, as it is certainly how she reacted.

“I also didn’t want Mom to worry,” Nicky admits, and that doesn’t surprise Liila. “I avoided touching people when I could, it was easy, but then we got to The Road…” Nicky starts to say.

“And you felt it without touch,” Lilia realises, and Nicky nods. “Nicholas, abilities like ours, like your mama has, they can be a burden, they can make you feel like you’re carrying a weight around with you, but you what you need to know is that are not carrying that weight alone,” Lilia assures him. “You have your moms, and your coven; we’re going to help you,” Lilia assures him. “We’re going to figure this out together,” Lilia promises him.

“Thank you, Lilia,” Nicky says, feeling incredibly grateful towards her, as for so long it has just been him and his moms, and that was everything he needed, so he never though he would have more family than just them, but it is clear that the Road has given him just that, as Jen and Agatha walk back towards them.

“No, bloodshed, I’m a little surprised,” Rio admits, trying to lighten the mood as she can tell that whatever Agatha and Jen talked about was intense, even if she didn’t know exactly what it was that they talked about.

“Disappointed?” Agatha asks with a smirk.

“That’s an answer I’m not going to give in front of our son,” Rio tells Agatha, showing that she does have some level of self-control, Agatha smirks at that, while Lilia, Jen and Alice exchange looks.

“That’s just as bad as answering,” Nicky says, pulling a face.

“Good luck living with those two, Nicky,” Jen tells Nicky, sounding amused.

“Appreciate it, I’m going to need a lot of therapy,” Nicky says, then he realises something. “Do witches have therapists?” Nicky asks, looking between the others, as he realises he doesn’t know that.

“No,” Lilia, Agatha, Jen, and Alice say together.

“That explains so much,” Nicky admits. “I’m really happy you’re back together, just try not to disturb me too much,” Nicky requests, as he looks between his moms.

“No promises,” Agatha tells him.

“But we’ll try,” Rio adds.

“Guess that’s the best I can hope for,” Nicky comments, though he doesn’t have much hope.

“Well, now that that is decided we should probably get going,” Alice tells the others, as she really doesn’t want to stay on the Road for longer than they have to.

“Yeah, we really should,” Jen confirms, and the others nod.

Seeing the nod Nicky and Lilia both stand up and the group once again continue their walk down the road.

“So, how long are we going to have to walk?” Nicky asks his moms, who he is walking between.

“Not sure, it will depend on The Road,” Agatha responds, Nicky nods and the group drift into silence as they group walk together.

For a little while, no one sure exactly how long, not even Rio, the group walk together down the road, occasionally engaging in conversation, but for the most part just walking. As they round a corner in the path the group sees something on the horizon, something which they all recognize.

“That’s the exit,” Agatha says, smiling.

“We’re all so close,” Alice says, exchanging amazed looks with Jen, and without even thinking about it everyone in the group start to walk fast.

As everyone almost run towards the door Nicky realises something, something awful;

“STOP!” Nicky suddenly yells, and everyone stops and look at him.

“Nicky? What is it?” Rio asks her son as she pulls her knife, knowing her son well enough to know that that tone of voice doesn’t mean anything good.

“We’re surrounded,” Nicky reveals, and as he does everyone else looks around, and realises that Nicky is completely right, they are surrounded by the Salem Seven with no way to get to their exit.

“Fucken hell,” Agatha says annoyed, as she and Rio push Nicky into the middle of the group so that he is as protected as possible while the rest of them stand back to back, each of them facing a different directly, with Nicky in the middle.

As Agatha faces the direction that will allow them to leave The Road, the one that is blocked, and considers everything that is happening, who she is facing, and what an all out fight will mean Agatha knows exactly what she needs to do; that there is no only one option, and because of that she glances at Rio.
